Unbelievers' Domination and Property Ownership: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling when unbelievers dominate and seize property, with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when unbelievers own captured Muslim property and explain the basis of the Shafi'i disagreement using the concepts of isma, mubah, and ihraz.

Core Idea
Unbelievers own Muslim property they capture and bring to their dar because its inviolability (isma) is lost, and their domination becomes a legal cause for ownership.

This passage presents a core Hanafi ruling on the legal consequences of enemy seizure of property. It distinguishes two scenarios — unbelievers dominating other unbelievers, and unbelievers dominating Muslims — and then engages the Shafi'i objection that a prohibited act cannot be a legal cause. Understanding this debate is essential for determining how recaptured property is treated in Islamic law of war and booty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases discussed
Read the opening statements: first, Turks dominating Byzantines (non-Muslim on non-Muslim); second, unbelievers dominating Muslim property. Both lead to ownership according to Hanafi.
The first case is straightforward; the second is the disputed one.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each case
For the first: the Turks own the Byzantine property because they seized permissible property (mubah). For the second: unbelievers own Muslim property after they secure it in their own territory (ihraz bi al-dar).
3
Extract the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the seizure by unbelievers is prohibited (mahzur) from beginning to end, so it cannot be a valid cause for ownership.
This is a principled objection based on the rule that something forbidden cannot produce a lawful effect.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi proof uses istihsan: the property, once seized and taken beyond Muslim control, loses its inviolability (isma) and returns to its original state of mubah. The domination then becomes a cause for ownership by necessity (hajat al-mukallaf), analogous to our domination over their property.
The response also notes that a prohibited act can still be a cause for reward (jihad), so ownership is even more plausible.
5
Note the condition of ihraz bi al-dar
Ownership is not complete merely by capture; the property must be secured in the enemy's territory (ihraz), which implies full control over the property both now and in the future.
This condition is agreed upon by both schools, but they differ on whether the seizure itself is a cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ اسْتِيْلَاءِ الْكُفَّارِ
وَإِذَا غَلَبَ التُّرُكُ عَلَى الرُّومِ فَسَبُوهُمْ وَأَخَذُوا أَمْوَالَهُمْ مَلَكُوهَا لِأَنَّ الْإِسْتِيلَاءَ قَدْ تَحَقَّقَ فِي مَالِ مَبَاحِ وَهُوَ السَّبَبُ عَلَى مَا يُبينُهُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فَإِنْ غَلَبْنَا عَلَى التَّرْكِ حَلَّ لَنَا مَانَجِدُهُ مِنْ ذَالِكَ اعْتِبَارًا بِسَائِرِ أَمْلاكِهِمْ ترجمہ اگر تا تاری کافروں نے ملک روم کے نصاری پر غلبہ پا کر ان کو قید کر لیا۔ اور ان کے اموال چھین لئے تو (ان کا قبضہ تسلیم ہوگا اور ) تا تاری ان مالوں کے مالک ہو جائیں گے ۔ کیونکہ انہوں نے مال مباح پر غالب آکر ان پر قبضہ کر لیا ہے۔ اور سبب ملک بھی یہی ہوتا ہے۔ (انشاء اللہ یہ بحث ہم آئندہ بیان کریں گے ۔ اس کے بعد اگر ہم لوگ ان تاتاریوں پر غالب ہو جائیں تو ان تاتاریوں نے جو کچھ بھی رومیوں سے لیا اور قبضہ کیا ہے اسے ان تاتاریوں سے چھین لینا جائز ہے۔
وَإِذَا غَلَبُوا عَلَى أَمْوَالِنَا وَالْعِيَاذُ بِاللَّهِ وَأَحْرَرُ وهَابِدَارِهِمْ مَلَكُوهَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا يَمْلِكُونَهَا لِأَنَّ الْإِسْتِيلاء مَحْظُورُ ابْتِدَاء وَانْتِهَاء وَالْمَحْفُورُ لَا يَنْتَهضُ سَبَبًا لِلْمِلَكِ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ مِنْ قَاعِدَةِ الْخَصْمِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْإِسْتِيلاء وَرَدَ عَلَى مَالِ مُبَاحٍ فَيَتَعَقِدُ سَمَّا لِلْمَلَك دَفْعًا لِحَاجَةِ الْمُكَلَّفِ كَاسْتِيْلَاتِنَا عَلَى أَمْوَالِهِمْ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الْعِصْمَةَ تَثْبتُ عَلى مُنَافَاةِ الدَّلِيلِ ضَرُورَةَ تَمَكَّنِ الْمَالِكِ مِنَ الْاِنْتِفَاءِ فَإِذَا زَالَتِ الْمَكْنَةُ عَادَ مُبَاحًا كَمَا كَانَ غَيْرَ أَنَّ الاسْتِيْلَاءَ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ إِلَّابِالإحْرَازِ بِالدَّارِ لأَنَّهُ عِبَارَةُ عَنِ الْإِفْتِدَارِ عَلَى الْمَحَلَّ حَالًا وَمَالًا وَالْمَحْظُورُ لِغَيْرِه إِذَا صَلَحَ سَبَا لِكَرَامَةٍ تَفُوقُ المِلكَ وَهُوَ الثَّوَابُ الأجِلُ فَمَاظَنُّكَ بِالْمِلْكِ الْعَاجِلِ ترجمہ اور اگر خدانخواستہ ونعوذ باللہ من ذالک بھی کفار ہمار ہے مالوں پر غالب آجائیں اور ان کو اپنے ساتھ اپنے ملک لے جائیں تو وہ بھی ان مالوں کے مالک ہو جائیں گے ( ۔ امام مالک واحد تم التعلیما کابھی یہی قول ہے۔ ) لیکن امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ وہ
Chapter on the domination of unbelievers. If the Turks dominate the Byzantines and take them captive and take their wealth, they own it because domination has been actualized over permissible property, and that is the cause (of ownership) as we will explain. Then if we dominate the Turks, it is permissible for us to take what we find from that, analogously to the rest of their property. And if they dominate our property (Allah forbid) and secure it in their dar, they own it. Al-Shafi'i said: They do not own it, because domination is prohibited from beginning to end, and what is prohibited cannot serve as a cause for ownership according to the known principle of the opponent. Our proof: Domination occurs over permissible property, so it becomes a valid cause for ownership to fulfill the need of the responsible person, just as our domination over their property. This is because inviolability (isma) is established contrary to the evidence due to the necessity of enabling the owner to benefit; when that ability is lost, [the property] returns to being permissible as it was, except that domination is only realized by securing it in the dar, because it is the ability to control the object in terms of present and future. And what is prohibited for another reason, if it becomes a cause for a honor that surpasses ownership—that is, eternal reward—what do you think about immediate ownership?
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a chapter on the legal effect of unbelievers' domination (isti'la') over property. It contains two rulings: first, when one group of unbelievers (e.g., Turks) dominates another (Byzantines), they own the captured property because they seized permissible property (mubah) that lost its previous owner's protection. Second, when unbelievers dominate Muslim property and bring it to their own land (Dar al-Harb), they own it as well (according to Hanafi). The Shafi'i objection is that their seizure is inherently unlawful (mahzur) from start to end, so it cannot be a legal cause for ownership. The Hanafi response uses istihsan: the property, once it falls into their hands and is secured in their dar, loses its previous inviolability (isma) for Muslims because we cannot exercise ownership over it. Thus it reverts to being mubah (permissible to take), and their domination serves as a cause for ownership just as our domination over their property does. The text also notes that the condition of 'securing in their dar' is necessary for full ownership (ihraz). The discussion continues with a rhetorical point: if a prohibited act can earn eternal reward (jihad), it can certainly earn temporary ownership.

Key Terms
استيلاء (isti'la'): Domination and seizure of property by force, especially by unbelievers.
مال مباح (mal mubah): Property that is not protected by inviolability (isma) and thus legally permissible to take.
إحراز بالدار (ihraz bi al-dar): Securing captured property in one's own territory (dar) as a condition for full ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when do unbelievers fully own Muslim property they have seized?
A) Immediately upon capture
B) When they have brought it to their own territory (Dar al-Harb) and secured it
C) Never, because their seizure is unlawful
D) Only if they pay compensation

Key Takeaway
Unbelievers own captured Muslim property only after it is secured in their dar (ihraz), because its inviolability is lost and their domination becomes a legal cause for ownership.

Recovery of Seized Property Before or After Division Among Mujahideen
Ruling on original owner's right to retake property recovered from kuffar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Muslim's right to reclaim property recovered from kuffar before and after division of spoils, and explain the underlying rationale of balancing harm.

Core Idea
Before division, owner takes property free; after division, he pays its value to avoid harming the individual ghazi.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on a common scenario in military campaigns: property that was unjustly seized by the enemy and later recovered by the Muslim army. The classical text from al-Hidayah presents a clear ruling based on a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and supported by legal reasoning. You will learn the distinction between pre- and post-division scenarios and the principle of justice (i'tidal al-nazar) that underlies it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios and their rulings
The text distinguishes between finding the property before division of spoils and after division. State the ruling for each: free before, payment after.
This is the core legal outcome to remember.
2
Examine the primary dalil (hadith)
The hadith explicitly addresses both scenarios. Note that the chain is weak (as narrated by Bayhaqi, Darqutni, etc.) or mursal (Abu Dawud).
Hanafis accept this hadith due to supporting evidence from reasoning and practice.
3
Understand the supporting reasoning (qiyas)
The text provides a rational argument: before division, the property is common; harm to each ghazi is minimal. After division, it is private property; taking without compensation causes severe harm.
This illustrates the Hanafi use of qiyas in supporting a naqli proof.
4
Recognize the Hanafi position on weak hadith
Despite the weak chain, the ruling is upheld because the reasoning (qiyas) and the hadith reinforce each other, and the Companions acted upon it.
This is a methodological point: a weak hadith can be accepted if supported by other evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسلمان دوبارہ انہیں چھینے ہوئے مال پر غالب آگئے تو تقسیم سے قبل پہلے مالکوں کیلئے بغیر کسی عوض کے لینے کا حق ہے فَإِنْ ظَهَرَ عَلَيْهَا الْمُسْلِمُونَ فَوَجَدَهَا الْمَالِكُونَ قَبْلَ الْقِسْمَةِ فَهِىَ لَهُمْ بِغَيْرِ شَيْءٍ وَإِنْ وَجَدُوهَا بَعْدَ الْقِسْمَةِ أَخَذُوهَا بِالْقِيِّمَةِ إِنْ أَحَبُّو الِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِيهِ إِنْ وَجَدْتَهُ قَبْلَ الْقِسْمَةِ فَهُوَ لَكَ بِغَيْرِ شَيْءٍ وَإِنْ وَجَدَتَهُ بَعْدَ الْقِسْمَةِ فَهُوَلَكَ بِالْقِيْمَةِ وَلأَنَّ الْمَالِكَ الْقَدِيمَ زَالَ مِلْكُهُ بِغَيْر رِضَاهُ فَكَانَ لَهُ حَقُّ الْأَخْذِ نَظَرْ الَهُ إِلَّا أَنَّ فِي الاحد بَعْدَ القِسْمَةِ ضَرَرَا بِالْمَاحُوذِ مِنْهُ باِزَالَةِ مِلْكِهِ الْخَاصَ فَيَأْخُذُهُ بِالْقِيْمَةِ لِيَعْتَدِلَ النَّظَرُ مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ وَالشَّرُكَةُ قَبْلَ الْقِسْمَةِ عَامَّةٌ فَيَقِلُّ الضَّرَرْقَيَا خُذُهُ بَغَيْرِ قِيمَة ترجمہ پھر اگر مسلمان ان مالوں پر غالب آگئے ( جو کفار مسلمانوں سے زبردستی لے گئے تھے ) اور ان کے مالکوں نے ان کی تقسیم سے پہلے ہی اپنا اپنا مال پالیا تو وہ لوگ کچھ بھی بدلہ دیے بغیر یعنی مفت میں لے جاسکیں گے۔ اور اگر ان کی تقسیم کے بعد وہ مالکان پہنچے تو اب ان کو اس بات کا اختیار ہوگا کہ اگر ان کا جی چاہے تو مال کی قیمت دے کر لے لیں ۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اس فرمان کی وجہ سے جو اس بارے میں فرمایا ہے کہ اگر تم نے تقسیم سے پہلے اس کو پا لیا تو وہ کسی عوض کے بغیر ہی تمہارا ہو گا۔ اس کی روایت بیہقی ، دارقطنی طبرانی اور طحاوی نے ضعیف سندوں سے کی ہے۔ اور ابو داؤد نے جید سند سے مرسلا اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ اس مال کے پرانے مالک کی ملکیت اس کی رضامندی کے بغیر کفار کے غلبہ سے ناحق ختم ہوئی ہے ۔ تو اس بات کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے اس مالک کو لینے کا حق حاصل ہے۔ لیکن مال کی تقسیم ہو جانے کے بعد لے لینے سے جس غازی کے حصہ سے لیا جائے گا اس کازبردست نقصان ہوگا کیونکہ تقسیم کے بعد وہ مال خاص اسی غازی کا حصہ بن چکا ہے۔ اس لئے اگر اپنا مال واپس لینا ہی چاہتا ہے تو قیمت دے کر لینے کی اسے اجازت ہوگی تاکہ دونوں شخصوں (پرانے اور نئے مالکان) کے لحاظ میں انصاف رہ جائے ۔ اور مال تقسیم ہونے سے پہلے اس مال میں تمام غازیوں کا مشترک حصہ ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے سکھوں کا صرف تھوڑا تھوڑا سا نقصان ہوگا۔ اسی لئے بغیر قیمت کے لے سکتا ہے۔
If the Muslims then dominate over them (the property that the kuffar forcefully took from Muslims), and the owners find it before division, then it is for them without anything (i.e., free). And if they find it after division, they take it with the price (i.e., they pay the value) if they wish. The saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding this: 'If you find it before division, it is for you without anything; but if you find it after division, it is for you with the price.' This hadith is narrated by Bayhaqi, Darqutni, Tabarani, and Tahawi with weak chains, and by Abu Dawud with a strong chain as mursal. And also due to the evidence that the former owner's ownership was removed without his consent due to the kuffar's dominance, so considering this, the owner has the right to take. However, taking after division causes severe harm to the one from whom it is taken because after division, that property has become the specific share of that ghazi. Therefore, if he wants to take his property back, he will be allowed to take it with the price so that justice is maintained from both sides. And before division, the property is commonly shared among all ghazis, so the harm to each is small; therefore, he can take it without price.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof, addressing the fate of property that was seized by kuffar from Muslims, then recovered by the Muslim army. The matn (from al-Hidayah) states the ruling: If the original owner finds his property before the spoils are divided among the mujahideen, he takes it free of charge. If after division, he may take it by paying the current value (qima). The proof is a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to this effect, though the commentators note its chain is weak (as narrated by Bayhaqi, etc.) or mursal (Abu Dawud). Nevertheless, the ruling is also supported by sound reasoning (qiyas): The original owner's property was taken unjustly, so he has a right to reclaim it. Before division, the property is communal among the mujahideen; taking it back harms each one only slightly, so no compensation is needed. After division, it has become the specific property of an individual; taking it without payment would cause him severe harm, so justice requires the owner to pay its value. This ruling is a classic application of the principle of 'taking with consideration to both parties' (i'tidal al-nazar min al-janibayn). The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as the matn is from al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
قسمت (qismah): Division of spoils (ghanima) among the mujahideen after the Muslims have collected and distributed it.
قیمت (qimat): Monetary value or price paid by the original owner to the ghazi who received the property in division, to compensate for its loss.
نظر (nazar): Consideration or regard; here, the principle of balancing justice between the two parties (i'tidal al-nazar min al-janibayn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a Muslim finds his property that was seized by kuffar and then recovered by the Muslim army, AFTER the spoils have been divided?
A) He may take it free of charge.
B) He may take it by paying its value (qimat) if he wishes.
C) He may not take it at all; it belongs to the ghazi.
D) He must take it with compensation determined by the ruler.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school balances the original owner's right with the ghazi's individual ownership after division by requiring payment of value only after division.

Ruling on a Twice-Captured Slave Purchased Twice
States the ruling on redemption rights after successive captures and purchases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on redemption rights for a slave captured twice and identify which owner has the right to redeem.

Core Idea
The right to redeem a captured slave follows the ownership at the time of capture.

This lesson examines a nuanced case from the Hanafi Siyar: a slave captured twice and purchased by two different Muslims. The ruling distinguishes between the original owner and the first buyer based on whose ownership the capture occurred. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the principles of ownership and redemption in Islamic law of war.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
List the original owner (malik qadim), the first buyer, the second buyer, and the slave (ghulam). Note the sequence of events: capture → purchase by first buyer → recapture → purchase by second buyer.
The slave is the same throughout; ownership changes with each sale.
2
Determine ownership at each capture
First capture occurred while slave was owned by original owner. Second capture occurred while slave was owned by the first buyer (after the first purchase). This is the key determinant.
3
Apply the principle: right to redeem follows ownership at capture
The original owner cannot redeem from the second buyer because the second capture did not occur on his ownership. The first buyer can redeem from the second buyer because the capture occurred on his ownership.
The proof is the explicit 'illa (cause) given in the text.
4
Determine the original owner's right vis-à-vis the first buyer
The original owner may take the slave from the first buyer by paying the total amount the first buyer paid (two thousand), because the first buyer acquired the slave for two prices.
This is a permission, not an obligation.
5
Note the absence rule
If the second buyer is absent, the first buyer's right remains valid, but the original owner still cannot bypass the first buyer.
The absence does not transfer any right to the original owner.

Source Text

۹۳ كتاب السير اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہفتم سے خریدا تھا۔ یہ پہلا اور اصل مالک اس غلام کی قیمت اس لئے دے گا کہ مفت میں لینے سے دوسرے مالک ( خریدار ) کا نقصان لازم آئے گا لیکن اس نے غلام کی آنکھ کے نقصان کے عوض جو کچھ پایا ہے اس کا مطالبہ وہ پہلا شخص (مالک) نہیں کر سکے گا۔ کیونکہ جس وقت اس کی آنکھ چھوڑی گئی تھی اس وقت اس غلام پر اس خریدار کی ملکیت صحیح تھی (یعنی اس نے اپنے مملوک اور جائز غلام سے یہ نفع حاصل کیا ہے ) اب اگر پہلا مالک اس خریدار سے اس دیت کو بھی لینا چاہتا ہو تو اس پر لازم ہو گا کہ وہ دوسرے مالک یعنی مشتری کو اس غلام کی اصل قیمت کے ساتھ اس کا جرمانہ بھی ادا کر دے۔ لیکن ایسا کرنے سے اس کا کوئی مالی فائدہ بھی نہ ہوگا ( کہ جتنا وصول کرے گا اتنا ہی اسے ادا بھی کرنا ہوگا ۔ اب یہ بات بھی معلوم ہونی چاہئے کہ اس غلام کی آنکھ ضائع ہو جانے سے اس میں جو کچھ کمی ہوئی ہے وہ اصل قیمت سے کم نہیں ہوگی۔ پھر واضح ہو کہ آنکھ پھوٹنے کی وجہ سے اس غلام کی قیمت ادا کرنے میں کوئی کمی نہیں کی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اوصاف کے مقابلہ میں کوئی قیمت نہیں ہوتی ہے اور یہ صورت شفعہ (فقہاء کے نزدیک زمین یا مکان میں ہمسائیگی یا شرکت کی وجہ سے خریداری کا حق، تفصیل کتاب الشفقہ میں آئے گی) سے خلاف ہے اس لئے کہ صفقہ ( ہاتھ کی تھیکی لگانا ، فروخت میں ہاتھ پر ہاتھ مار کر معاملہ کو یقینی بنانا، عقد بیع ، مزید تفصیل کتاب البیع میں آئے گی۔ انوار الحق قاسمی ۱۱/۹۴ع) بدل کر جب شفیع کے پاس گیا تو مشتری کے پاس وہ خریدی ہوئی چیز خرید فاسد کے حکم میں ہوگئی۔ حالانکہ خرید فاسد میں اوصاف کی ضمان واجب ہوتی ہے جیسے غصب میں واجب ہوا کرتی ہے ( کیونکہ ملکیت مکمل نہیں ہے ) اور یہاں جاری مسئلہ میں وہ ملکیت صحیح ہے اس لئے ان صورتوں میں فرق ہو گیا۔ کفار نے کسی مسلمان کے غلام کو قید کیا پھر دوسرے مسلمان نے اسے خرید لیا پھر دوبارہ
اسے گرفتار کر لیا گیا اور دوبارہ خریدا گیا مالک اول کیلئے واپس لینے کا حکم
وَ إِنْ أَسَرُوا عَبْداً فَاشْتَرَاهُ رَجُلٌ بِأَلْفِ دِرْهَم فَأَسَرُوهُ ثَانِيَةً وَأَدْخَلُوهُ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ فَاشْتَرَاهُ رَجُل  َاحَرُ بِأَلْفِ دِرْهَـ فَلَيْسَ لِلْمَوْلَى الْاَولِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ مِنَ الثَّانِي بِالشَّمَنِ لِأَنَّ الْاَسْرَ مَا وَرَدَ عَلَى مِلْكِهِ وَلِلْمُشْتَرِى الْأَوَّلِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ مِنَ الثَّانِي بِالشَّمَنِ لأَنَّ الْأَشْرَوَرَ دَعَلى مِلْكِهِ ثُمَّ يَأْخُذُهُ الْمَالِكُ الْقَدِيمُ بِالْفَيْنِ إِنْ شَاءَ لِأَنَّهُ قَامَ عَلَيْهِ بِالثَّمَنَيْنِ فَيَأْخُذُهُ بِهِمَا وَ كَذَا إِذَا كَانَ الْمَاسُورُ مِنْهُ الثَّانِي غَائِباً لَيْسَ لِلأَوَّلِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ اعْتِبَارًا بِحَالٍ حَضْرَتِهِ ترجمہ اگر کافروں نے کسی مسلمان کے غلام کو قید کیا۔ پھر اس غلام کو کسی مسلمان نے ہزار روپے دے کر خرید لیا۔ اور دارالاسلام لے آیا۔ پھر کافروں نے دوبارہ اس غلام کو قید کر لیا اور وہ اسے دار الحرب لے کر چلے گئے۔ پھر کسی دوسرے مسلمان نے اس کو ایک ہزار روپے میں خرید لیا تو پرانے اور اصلی مولی کو یہ اختیار نہیں ہو گا کہ اس دوسرے خریدار سے اس غلام کی قیمت دے کر خرید لے کیونکہ وہ غلام اس کی ملکیت میں قید نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔ البتہ پہلے خریدار کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ اس دوسرے خریدار سے اس کی قیمت دے کر غلام کو خرید لے کیونکہ اس پہلے خریدار کی ملکیت میں رہتے ہوئے وہ قید کیا گیا ہے۔ پھر اصل مالک کو یہ اختیار ہو گا کہ اگر چاہے اس پہلے خریدار سے دو ہزار سے خرید لے کیونکہ پہلے خریدار نے اس غلام کو دوبار ایک ایک ہزار دے کر مجموعہ رو ہزار میں خریدا ہے۔ الحاصل اگر پہلا ما لک پسند کرتا ہو تو دو ہزار دے کر خرید لے اور نہ نہیں اور اگر پہلا خریدار اس وقت موجود نہ ہو کہیں اور چلا گیا ہو تو اس پہلے مالک کو یہ اختیار نہ ہوگا کہ دوسرے خریدار وغیرہ سے لے۔ جیسے کہ پہلے خریدار کی موجودگی میں دوسرے خریدار سے نہیں لے سکتا ہے۔
If they (disbelievers) capture a slave, then a man buys him for a thousand dirhams, then they capture him a second time and take him into dar al-harb, then another man buys him for a thousand dirhams, then the first master is not entitled to take him from the second buyer for the price, because the capture did not occur on his ownership. The first buyer is entitled to take him from the second buyer for the price, because the capture occurred on his ownership. Then the original owner may take him from him (the first buyer) for two thousand if he wishes, because he (the first buyer) acquired him for two prices; so he may take him for both. Similarly, if the one captured from the second is absent, the first is not entitled to take him, considering the case of his presence.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_commentary on a specific case in the book of Siyar: a Muslim's slave is captured by disbelievers, then purchased by a Muslim, then captured again and purchased by another Muslim. The text first explains the ruling in Urdu, then gives the Arabic matn from the Hidayah, and then provides a Urdu translation and further commentary. The key rulings are: (1) the original owner cannot redeem the slave from the second buyer because the capture occurred when the slave was not in his ownership; (2) the first buyer can redeem from the second buyer because the capture occurred while the slave was in his ownership; (3) the original owner can then take the slave from the first buyer by paying the total amount the first buyer paid (two thousand), if he wishes; (4) if the second buyer is absent, the first buyer’s right to redeem from him is still valid, but the original owner cannot bypass the first buyer. The text also discusses a related point about diminution in value due to loss of an eye, concluding that no reduction is made because qualities do not affect price in this context, contrasting with the case of shuf'ah (pre-emption) where a faulty sale occurs. The overall ruling is a clear application of the principle that capture and purchase affect ownership rights.

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): A male slave owned by a Muslim master.
اسر (asr): Capture; taking a free person or slave into custody by the enemy.
ثمن (thaman): Price or payment for a purchase; here specifically the monetary value given to acquire the slave.
مالک قدیم (malik qadim): The original owner before any captures or purchases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a slave captured twice and purchased by two different Muslims, who has the right to redeem from the second buyer?
A) The original owner
B) The first buyer
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The right to redeem a captured slave belongs to the owner at the time of capture, not necessarily the original owner.

Freedom of a Harbi's Slave Upon Conversion and Arrival
Ruling on a harbi's slave becoming free upon conversion and arrival

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a harbi's slave becomes free upon conversion and arrival, and explain the two proofs: the hadith of the slaves of Ta'if and the istihsan based on self-possession.

Core Idea
The slave of a harbi is freed by his own conversion and arrival — the Prophet's decree 'they are Allah's freed ones' is decisive.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the author addresses a specific scenario: a slave belonging to an enemy non-Muslim (harbi) converts to Islam and makes his way to Muslim territory. The ruling is immediate freedom, supported by both a prophetic hadith and a rational argument based on self-possession. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi view on the effect of conversion and the priority of personal agency over external claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The scenario: a slave owned by a harbi converts to Islam and then either comes to Dar al-Islam or the Muslims prevail over Dar al-Harb. The ruling: the slave becomes free (hurr). This is the core legal outcome.
The ruling applies equally to slaves who join the Muslim army.
2
Examine the primary textual proof (dalil naqli)
The hadith of the slaves of Ta'if: when they converted and came to the Prophet (ﷺ), he judged them free and said, 'They are Allah's freed ones.' This is a direct prophetic decision (qawl and fi'l) that establishes the ruling for any similar case.
The hadith is narrated by Ahmad, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Tabarani; Abu Dawud's version is mursal, but it is accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the secondary rational proof (istihsan)
The author provides a rational argument: the slave has secured himself (ahraza nafsahu) by leaving his master. His own possession of himself is earlier and stronger than any claim by the Muslims. Therefore, his hand is prioritized, and he becomes free without needing capture.
This is istihsan because it overrides the general principle that property (including slaves) is respected; here the slave's own agency and freedom are preferred.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i reportedly holds that the slave does not become free unless he is actually captured by Muslims or his master converts. The Hanafi school responds that the hadith and istihsan override any general rule of property.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih) based on different methodologies.
5
Apply the ruling
If a harbi's slave converts and arrives in Muslim territory, the judge immediately declares him free. No need for a formal manumission or the master's consent. The slave becomes a free Muslim with full legal capacity.
The same applies if he was already in Dar al-Islam after Muslim conquest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ إِذَا أَسْلَمَ عَبْدُ الْحَرْبِي ثُمَّ خَرَجَ إِلَيْنَا أَوْظْهِرَ عَلَى الدَّارِ فَهُوَ حُرُّ وَ كَذَا لِكَ إِذَا خَرَجَ عَشِيدُ هُمْ إِلَى عَسْكَرِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ فَهُمْ أَحْرَارُ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ عَيدٌ مِنْ عَبْدِ الطَّائِفِ أَسْلَمُوا وَخَرَجُوا إلى رَسُولِ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَقَضَى بِعِتْقِهِمْ وَقَالَ هُمْ عُتَقَاءُ اللَّهِ وَلِأَنَّهُ أَحْرَزَ نَفْسَهُ بِالْخُرُوجِ إِلَيْنَا مُرَ اعْمَالِمَوْلَاهُ أَوْبِالْالْتِحَاقِ بِمَتَعَةٍ المُسْلِمِينَ إِذَا ظَهِرَ عَلَى الدَّارِ وَاعْتِبَارُ يَدِهِ أَوْلَى مِنَ اعْتَبَارِ بَدِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ لِأَنَّهَا أَسْبَقُ ثُبُوتًا عَلَى نَفْسِهِ فَالْحَاجَةُ فِى حَقَّهِ إِلى زِيَادَةِ تَوْرَكِيدِ وَفِي حَقِّهِمْ إِلَى إِثْبَاتِ الْيَدِ ابْتِدَاء فَكَانَ أَوْلى
ترجمہ اور اگر کافر حربی کا غلام مسلمان ہو کر ہمارے پاس دارالاسلام میں پہنچ گیا یا وہ وہیں تھا کہ مسلمانوں نے دار الحرب پر غلبہ پالیا تو وہ آزاد مانا جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر تربیوں کے غلام ان کے پاس سے نکل کر مسلمانوں کے لشکر میں آگئے تو وہ سب آزاد ہو جائیں گے۔ اس روایت کی وجہ سے کہ اہل طائف کے کئی غلام نکل کر رسول اللہ کے لشکر میں آگئے تھے تو رسول اللہ نے ان سب کی آزادی کا حکم دے دیا تھا۔ یہ فرماتے ہوئے کہ یہ لوگ اللہ تعالیٰ کے آزاد کئے ہوئے ہیں ۔ اس کی روایت احمد ابن ابی شیبہ بیہقی اور طبرانی نے کی ہے اور ابوداؤ درحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے اس کی روایت مرسلا کی ہے)۔ اور اس وجہ سے بھی کہ اس مسلمان غلام نے اپنے مولیٰ کو چھوڑ کر ہمارے پاس آ کر خود کو محفوظ کر لیا یا جب دار الحرب پر مسلمانوں کا غلبہ ہوا تو مسلمانوں کے لشکر سے مل کر محفوظ ہو گیا اور اس کا اس کی اپنی ذات پر اپنے قبضہ کا اعتبار کرنا اس بات کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ بہتر اور اولی ہے کہ اس پر مسلمانوں کا قبضہ ثابت کیا جائے کیونکہ اس کا اپنی ذات پر قبضہ پہلے ہی ہو چکا ہے۔ اور اس قبضہ کو صرف زیادہ مضبوط ہونے کی ضرورت ہے اور مسلمانوں کے قبضہ کو تسلیم کرنے سے اس کی ضرورت ہو جائے گی کہ کب سے ان کا اس پر قبضہ ثابت ہے۔ لہذا غلام کا اپنا ذاتی قبضہ ہی دوسروں کی بہ نسبت اولی ہوا۔
And if a harbi's slave becomes Muslim, then he comes to us or (the Muslims) prevail over the abode (of war), then he is free. Likewise, if their slaves go out to the Muslim army, they are free. Because it is narrated that some slaves from the people of Ta'if became Muslim and went out to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he judged them to be free and said, 'They are Allah's freed ones.' And because he secured himself by coming to us, leaving his master's hand, or by joining the Muslim force when they prevailed over the abode. Considering his own hand is more appropriate than considering the hand of the Muslims, because his hand is earlier established over himself. So in his case, only strengthening is needed, while in their case, establishing the hand from the beginning is needed, so his (hand) is more appropriate. Translation: And if a harbi disbeliever's slave becomes Muslim and arrives in Dar al-Islam with us, or he was there and the Muslims prevailed over Dar al-Harb, then he will be considered free. Similarly, if the slaves of the harbis leave them and come to the Muslim army, they will all be free. Due to this narration that several slaves from the people of Ta'if came out to the Muslim army and the Messenger of Allah ordered their freedom, saying, 'These people are the freed ones of Allah Almighty.' This narration is reported by Ahmad ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Tabarani; Abu Dawud (may Allah have mercy on him) narrated it as mursal. And also because this Muslim slave, by leaving his master and coming to us, secured himself, or when the Muslims prevailed over Dar al-Harb, he became secure by joining the Muslim army. And considering his possession over his own self is better and more appropriate than establishing the Muslims' possession over him, because his own possession of himself has already occurred. That possession only needs to be strengthened, whereas accepting the Muslims' possession would require establishing when they gained possession over him. Therefore, the slave's own personal possession is more appropriate than that of others.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah. It addresses the status of a slave belonging to a harbi (enemy non-Muslim) who converts to Islam either before or after reaching Muslim territory. The ruling is that such a slave becomes free immediately upon conversion and arrival or upon Muslim conquest. The primary proof is the hadith of the slaves of Ta'if who converted and joined the Prophet (ﷺ); he declared them free, stating they are 'Allah's freed ones.' This is a strong textual evidence (dalil naqli). Additionally, the author provides a rational argument (dalil aqli) based on possession and control. The slave, by his own action, gains control over himself; his own possession of his person is prior and therefore takes precedence over any claim by the Muslims. This is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) because it prioritizes the slave's own agency. The Urdu commentary expands on the hadith's narrators and clarifies that the slave's self-securing through coming to Muslim territory or joining the army establishes his freedom. The ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah, as it is based on authentic hadith and sound analogy. No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is mentioned; the school is unanimous.

Key Terms
عَبْدُ الْحَرْبِي (abdu al-harbi): A slave owned by a harbi (an enemy non-Muslim who is not under a peace treaty).
أَحْرَزَ نَفْسَهُ (ahraza nafsahu): He secured himself; used to describe the slave's action of acquiring control over his own person by coming to Muslim territory.
عُتَقَاءُ اللَّهِ (utaqa'u Allah): Allah's freed ones; the Prophet's description of the converted slaves, indicating a divine sanction for their freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a harbi's slave who converts to Islam and then comes to Dar al-Islam?
A) He remains a slave and is returned to his master.
B) He becomes free immediately upon arrival.
C) He becomes free only if his master also converts.
D) He becomes a prisoner of war and is enslaved by Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The slave of a harbi who converts and comes to Muslim territory becomes free immediately, proven by the Prophet's hadith and the principle of self-possession.

No Judgment for Debts or Usurpation between Musta'min in Dar al-Islam
Ruling on debts and usurpation between Muslim and Harbi who become musta'min

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on why a qadi does not judge debts or usurpation that occurred in Dar al-Harb when the parties later become musta'min, and explain the reasoning (talil).

Core Idea
The musta'min's aman binds him only for future acts; past acts in Dar al-Harb are beyond the qadi's jurisdiction.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya addresses a specific jurisdictional issue: when a debt or usurpation occurs in Dar al-Harb between parties who then enter Dar al-Islam as musta'min, can the qadi of Dar al-Islam give judgment? The text provides the Hanafi ruling and its underlying reasoning (talil). Understanding this ruling requires grasping the limited scope of aman and the status of property in Dar al-Harb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and acts
The passage addresses two scenarios: (1) debt between a Muslim and a Harbi (or two Harbis) in Dar al-Harb, and (2) usurpation (ghasb) between them. Both later become musta'min in Dar al-Islam.
2
State the ruling
In both cases, the qadi in Dar al-Islam will not issue any judgment (la yaqdi).
The ruling is procedural: the qadi lacks jurisdiction.
3
Examine reasoning for debt
The musta'min did not impose (lam yalzim) Islamic law on his past actions. Aman only obligates him to follow Islamic law in the future. Hence, the qadi has no authority over past debts.
The time of judgment (waqt al-qada') is irrelevant because the original debt occurred before the parties became subject to Islamic jurisdiction.
4
Examine reasoning for usurpation
The usurper became owner at the moment of seizure because the property was non-inviolable (ghayr ma'sum) in Dar al-Harb. Thus, no wrong remains to be adjudicated.
Ownership transfers by seizure in Dar al-Harb for non-Muslim property.
5
Confirm scope
The same ruling applies if both parties were Harbis and later become musta'min.

وقت الإِدَانَةِ أَصْلاً وَلَا وَقْتَ الْقَضَاءِ عَلَى الْمُسْتَأْمِ لأَنَّهُ مَا الزَّمَ حُكْمَ الْإِسْلَامِ فِيْمَا مَضَى مِنْ أَفْعَالِهِ وَإِنَّمَا العَزَمَ ذَالِكَ فِى الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ وَأَمَّا الْعَصَبُ فَلِأَنَّهُ صَارَ مِلْكًا لِلَّذِى غَصَبَهُ وَاسْتَوَلَّى عَلَيْهِ لِمُصَادَفَتِهِ مَا لَّا غَيْرَ مَعْصُومٍ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ وَ كَذَالِكَ لَوْ كَانَ حَرْبِيَّشِ فَعَلَا ذَالِكَ ثُمَّ خَرَجًا مُسْتَأْمِنَيْنِ لِمَا قُلْنَا
ترجمہ اگر کوئی مسلمان امان لے کر دار الحرب میں داخل ہوا اور وہاں کسی نے اسے کچھ مال قرض کے طور پر دیا یا اس نے وہاں کے کسی شخص کو قرض دیا یا اس مسلمان نے یا وہاں کے حربی نے ایک دوسرے کا مال غصب کر لیا۔ پھر وہاں سے وہ مسلمان دار الاسلام نکل آیا اور وہی حربی بھی امان لے کر دار الاسلام میں آگیا تو ان دونوں میں سے دوسرے کے لئے حکم کچھ بھی نہیں دیا جائے گا۔ ادھار کی صورت میں اس لئے حکم نہ ہوگا ( فیصلہ سنانے سے بھی قاضی کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا ) کیونکہ قاضی کا فیصلہ اسی صورت میں نافذ ہوتا ہے جبکہ قاضی کو اس پر فیصلہ کرنے کا کچھ اختیار بھی ہو ۔ حالانکہ ادھار لین دین کرنے کے وقت قاضی کو کسی قسم کا حق اس پر نہ تھا۔ اسی طرح اس وقت بھی یعنی اپنا فیصلہ دیتے وقت قاضی کو اس حربی بیجو کہ امان لے کر آیا ہوا ہے کسی قسم کا فیصلہ سنانے کا حق نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ آنے والے حربی نے اپنے پچھلے دنوں کے افعال کے متعلق خود پر اسلام کے حکم کو لازم نہیں کیا بلکہ صرف آئندہ محدود دنوں کے لئے اپنے افعال کے متعلق کچھ باتوں کا کیا ہے اور غصب کی صورت میں تو غصب کی ہوئی چیز اسی وقت غاصب کی ملک ہو گئی جبکہ وہ اس پر غالب ہو گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایسے مال کو غصب کیا ہے جو محترم مال نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ (یعنی دارالحرب کے لوگ اور ان کا مال اور وہ جگہ سب ملکیت میں آنے کے قابل اور غیر محترم ہیں ) اسی طرح اگر دو حربیوں نے آپس میں ایسا کیا ہو پھر امان لے کر ہمارے یہاں آئے اور ہمارے قاضی کے پاس آکر اپنا پرانا مقدمہ پیش کیا ) تو ان کے درمیان بھی قاضی کچھ فیصلہ نہ کرے گا ۔ کیونکہ قاضی کا فیصلہ اپنے اختیار پر اعتماد کر کے اور اسی بنیاد پر ہوتا ہے۔ ( یعنی قاضی کو یہ اختیار ہو کہ اس کا حکم ان لوگوں پر بھی نافذ ہو ۔ حالانکہ ان حربیوں نے جس جگہ یہ معاملہ کیا ہے وہ دارالحرب ہے جہاں اس قاضی کو کوئی اختیار نہیں ہے۔ یہ حکم اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ مسلمان کا ساتھی حربی یا دونوں حربی مسلمان ہو کر نہیں آئے بلکہ صرف امان لے کر آئے ہوں۔
The time of indebtedness originally, and there is no time of judgment upon the musta'min because he did not impose the rule of Islam upon his past actions; rather he imposed that for the future. As for usurpation, because it became ownership for the one who usurped it and he gained control over it due to its encountering non-inviolable property, as we have explained. Similarly, if two harbis did that then they came out as musta'min, for what we have said.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding transactions and usurpation that occurred in Dar al-Harb between a Muslim and a Harbi (enemy combatant), or between two Harbis, who later enter Dar al-Islam as musta'min (those granted safe conduct). The ruling is that the qadi in Dar al-Islam will not issue any judgment (qada) concerning the debt or the usurpation. The reason given in the text is twofold: First, for debt, the musta'min never subjected himself to Islamic law for past actions; his acceptance of aman only obligates him to follow Islamic law in the future. Since the qadi's authority is based on jurisdiction over those who have accepted Islamic law, he has no power over past transactions. Second, for usurpation (ghasb), the usurper became the owner of the property at the moment of seizure because the property of Dar al-Harb is considered non-inviolable (ghayr ma'sum) and thus can be owned by seizure. The text explicitly states that this ruling applies even if the wrongdoer is a Harbi who later becomes musta'min, or if two Harbis do the same.

Key Terms
مستأمن (musta'min): A non-Muslim (originally Harbi) who enters Dar al-Islam with a safe conduct (aman) for a limited period, or a Muslim who enters Dar al-Harb with aman.
غصب (ghasb): Wrongful seizure of property; in this context, seizure of property in Dar al-Harb which is not considered ma'sum (inviolable).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the musta'min did not bind himself to Islamic law for past acts
C) Because the qadi has no authority over musta'min
D) Because the debt was not witnessed

Key Takeaway
A qadi in Dar al-Islam lacks jurisdiction over acts committed in Dar al-Harb by musta'min because aman only governs future conduct, and property in Dar al-Harb is non-inviolable.

Debt Judged but Not Usurpation When Both Become Muslims
Ruling on post-Islam adjudication of pre-Islam financial dealings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes between debt and usurpation when both parties embrace Islam, and apply the reasoning to analogous scenarios.

Core Idea
Mutual consent preserves a debt contract; unilateral seizure transfers ownership irrevocably in Dar al-Harb.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: two Harbis who had dealings in Dar al-Harb embrace Islam and enter Dar al-Islam. The qadi must decide whether to adjudicate prior financial disputes. The Hanafi ruling makes a sharp distinction between debt and usurpation, rooted in the nature of each transaction and the status of the parties at the time. Understanding this distinction reveals deeper principles about the validity of contracts and property rights across Dar al-Harb and Dar al-Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two transactions
Read the passage and note that it deals with two types of dealings: debt (mudayanah) and usurpation (ghasb).
2
Note the condition
The condition is that both parties, originally Harbis, become Muslims and come to Dar al-Islam. This triggers the qadi's jurisdiction.
3
Trace the reasoning for debt
For debt: it was a valid contract because it occurred with mutual consent (taradi). Upon Islam, the parties bind themselves to Islamic rulings, so the qadi has authority to enforce the debt.
4
Trace the reasoning for usurpation
For usurpation: the usurper had already become owner of the object at the time of seizure. There is no impurity (khubth) in the ownership of a Harbi, so the qadi cannot order return.
5
Summarize the practical difference
Debt is enforceable because it is a consensual obligation; usurpation is not because ownership was validly transferred and there is no basis to reverse it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ لَو خَرَجًا مُسْلِمَيْنِ قُضِيَ بِالدِّيْنِ بَيْنَهُمَا وَلَمْ يُقْضَ بِالْغَضَبِ أَمَّا الْمُدَايَنَهُ فَلِأَنَّهَا وَقَعَتْ صَحِيحَةً لِوُقُوعِهَا بِالتَّرَاضِي وَالْوِلَايَةُ ثَابِتَةُ حَالَةَ الْقَضَاءِ لِإِلْتِرَامِهِمَا الْأَحْكَامُ بِالْإِسْلَامِ وَأَمَّا الْعَصَبُ فَلِمَا بَيْنَا أَنَّهُ مَلَكَهُ وَلَا حُبتَ فِي مِلْكِ الْحَرْبِيِّ حَتَّى يُؤْمَرُ بِالرَّةِ
ترجمه وَلَوْ خَرَجًا مُسْلِمَيْن.... الخ اور اگر دونوں حربی مسلمان ہو کر دار الاسلام چلے آئے تو ان کے درمیان ( مطالبہ کرنے کی صورت میں ) قرضہ کا حکم کیا جائے گا۔ یعنی جو قرض دار ہو وہ اپنا قرض ادا کر دے۔ لیکن غصب کی صورت میں کوئی حکم نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قرضہ کا لین دین تو صحیح طور پر ہوا تھا کیونکہ دونوں کی رضامندی سے ہوا تھا۔ اور قاضی کو اپنے فیصلہ سنانے کے وقت ان دونوں پر اختیار حاصل ہے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں نے اسلام قبول کر کے اسلام کے احکام کو اپنے اوپر لازم کر لیا ہے اور غصب کی صورت میں فیصلہ نہ کرنا اوپر بتائی ہوئی وجہ سے ہے۔ یعنی اس حالت میں غصب کرنے والا حربی دوسرے حربی کمال منصوب کا مالک ہو چکا ہے اور حربی کی ملکیت میں کوئی ناپاکی نہیں ہے۔ کہ اسے واپس کرنے کا حکم دیا جائے۔
And if both come out as Muslims, judgment is given for the debt between them, and not for the usurpation. As for the debt, because it occurred validly due to mutual consent, and authority is established at the time of judgment because they bound themselves to the rulings by Islam. As for the usurpation, because we have explained that he owned it, and there is no impurity in the ownership of the Harbi such that he would be ordered to return it.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage provides the contrasting ruling when the two Harbis (or a Muslim and a Harbi) embrace Islam and then enter Dar al-Islam. The qadi will now adjudicate the debt because: (1) the debt contract was valid when made (since it was based on mutual consent), and (2) the parties have now accepted Islam, thereby subjecting themselves to Islamic law, giving the qadi jurisdiction. However, the usurpation is not adjudicated because the usurper had already become owner of the property at the time of seizure, as per the earlier reasoning. Since the property of a Harbi is not considered inviolable (there is no khubth/impurity in it), the usurper's ownership is valid and there is no basis to order return. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that the debt transaction was sound (sahih) due to mutual consent, and now with Islam, the qadi's authority applies. For usurpation, the ownership had already transferred, so no judgment.

Key Terms
مداینة (mudayanah): A debt transaction, specifically a loan or credit sale.
خبث (khubth): Impurity; here, moral or legal defect in ownership that requires restitution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason the qadi judges the debt but not the usurpation when both parties become Muslims?
A) Because debt is more important than usurpation
B) Because the debt was contracted with mutual consent and Islam provides jurisdiction, while usurpation resulted in valid ownership
C) Because the usurped property is no longer available
D) Because Islam cancels all prior transactions

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of prior transactions upon embracing Islam depends on their nature: consensual contracts remain enforceable, while unilateral takings are not reversed.

The Distinction Between Judicial Judgment and Fatwa in Usurpation Cases
Ruling on Muslim who usurped from a Harbi before his Islam, then both come to Dar al-Islam as Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between binding judicial judgment (qada) and advisory fatwa (amr) in the case of usurped property from a Harbi, and explain the rationale of corruption of ownership due to breach of aman.

Core Idea
Ownership is valid by seizure but morally tainted by breach of aman; return is ordered by fatwa, not enforced by qada.

This lesson examines a nuanced case from Hanafi siyar: a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman, usurps property from a Harbi, and then both become Muslims and come to Dar al-Islam. The qadi does not issue a binding judgment to return the property because ownership was validly acquired. Yet the Muslim is ordered (amr) to return it as a fatwa, because the ownership was accompanied by a forbidden act—breach of the covenant of aman. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping Hanafi jurisprudence on the interplay between legal validity and moral obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and its elements
Note the three key facts: Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman, usurps property from a Harbi, then both become Muslims and come to Dar al-Islam.
2
State the two-part ruling
The passage gives two rulings: (1) the qadi does not give a binding judgment (qada) to return, but (2) the Muslim is ordered (amr) to return, meaning a fatwa is given.
Amr here is advisory, not enforceable by court.
3
Analyze the reason for no qada
The text says 'for what we have explained that he owned it.' In an earlier ruling, a Muslim who seizes property in Dar al-Harb owns it validly (provided it is from a Harbi). Hence no court can undo valid ownership.
Ownership by seizure in Dar al-Harb is a Hanafi principle.
4
Analyze the reason for the order to return
Although ownership is valid, it is considered corrupt (fasid) because it was accompanied by a prohibited act: breach of the covenant of aman (naqd al-ahd). The aman obligated the Muslim to safeguard the Harbi's property; usurping it violates that trust. The corruption necessitates return as a matter of religious duty.
The corruption is not in the contract of ownership but in the accompanying sin.
5
Understand the distinction between qada and fatwa
Qada is a binding judicial decree enforceable by the state. Fatwa is a non-binding legal advice given to the individual. The Muslim is ordered to return in the sense of a fatwa, not a qada. This shows the Hanafi recognition of moral obligation even when legal enforcement is absent.
This distinction is important in siyar and muamalat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا دَخَلَ الْمُسْلِمُ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ بِأَمَانٍ فَعَصَبَ حَرْبِيَّاثُمَّ خَرَجًا مُسْلِمَيْنِ أُمِرَ بِرَةِ الْعَصَبِ وَلَمْ يُقْضَ عَلَيْهِ أَمَّا عَدُمُ الْقَضَاءِ فَلِمَا بَيَّنَّا أَنَّهُ مَلَكَهُ وَأَمَّا الْأَمْرُ بِالرَّدَوَمُرَادُهُ الْفَتَوَى بِهِ فَلَانَ، فَسَدَ الْمِلْكُ لِمَا يُقَارِنُهُ مِنَ الْمُحَرَّمِ وَهُوَ نَقْضُ الْعَهْدِ
ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی مسلمان امان لے کر دار الحرب میں گیا اور اس نے وہاں کسی حربی کا کوئی مال غصب کر لیا پھر وہ حربی مسلمان ہو گیا اور مسلمان کے ساتھ ہو کر دونوں دار الاسلام آگئے ۔ تو دیانت داری کے طور پر اس سے کہا جائے گا کہ اس کا مال مغصوب واپس کر دے۔ مگر قاضی اس کا حکم نہیں کرے گا۔ اور یہ اسی وجہ سے حکم نہیں کرے گا جو اوپر بیان کی جاچکی ہے کہ مسلمان اس محترم مال کا مالک ہوا ہے۔ پھر بھی اس مسلمان کو واپس کرنے کے لئے کہنے اور فتوی دینے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ وہ غلط اور فاسد طریقہ سے اس مال کا مالک ہوا ہے۔ یعنی اس نے عہد کے خلاف اور غداری کے ساتھ غصب کیا ہے جو ایک حرام کام ہے۔ جس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ اصل مالک کو اس کا مال واپس کر دیا جائے۔
And when a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman and usurps from a Harbi, then both come out as Muslims, he is ordered to return the usurped property, but no judgment is made against him. As for the lack of judgment, for what we have explained that he owned it. As for the order to return—meaning the fatwa to that effect—because the ownership became corrupt due to what accompanies it of the prohibited, which is the breach of covenant.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents a special case: a Muslim enters Dar al-Harb with aman (safe conduct) and usurps property from a Harbi. Then the Harbi becomes Muslim, and both come to Dar al-Islam as Muslims. The ruling has two aspects: (1) The qadi will not issue a binding judgment (qada) to return the property because the Muslim had validly owned it by seizure in Dar al-Harb (as per previous ruling). (2) However, the Muslim is ordered (amr) to return it, meaning a fatwa (non-binding legal advice) is given that he should return it. The reason is that although the ownership was valid, it is considered corrupt (fasid) because it was accompanied by a prohibited act: breach of the covenant of aman (naqd al-ahd). The Muslim had entered with a pledge of safety, and usurping the Harbi's property violates that trust. Thus, moral and religious duty demands return, even though the qadi cannot enforce it.

Key Terms
أمر بالرد (amr bi al-radd): An order (non-binding, as a fatwa) to return usurped property, as opposed to a judicial decree (qada).
نقض العهد (naqd al-ahd): Breach of the covenant of aman; the Muslim violated the safe conduct by usurping property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the Muslim ordered to return the usurped property even though the qadi cannot force it?
A) Because the property was not validly owned
B) Because of the breach of covenant (naqd al-ahd) associated with the usurpation
C) Because the Harbi had rights as a Muslim now
D) Because the qadi has no authority over Muslims

Key Takeaway
Valid ownership does not always eliminate moral obligations; when ownership is tainted by a forbidden act like breach of aman, religious duty demands restitution, even if the court cannot enforce it.

Diyah and Kaffarah for Killing in Dar al-Harb between Muslims with Aman
Ruling on diyah, kaffarah, and qisas when one Muslim kills another in Dar al-Harb under aman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah, kaffarah, and qisas when one Muslim kills another in Dar al-Harb under aman, and explain the proofs for each.

Core Idea
A Muslim's inviolability follows him into Dar al-Harb, so diyah and kaffarah apply, but qisas falls due to lack of enforcement power.

This passage addresses a unique scenario: two Muslims with safe conduct (aman) in enemy territory, and one kills the other. The Hanafi school rules that diyah and kaffarah remain obligatory, but qisas is not, because the state authority needed for execution is absent. The reasoning highlights how Islamic protections are tied to the person, not the location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What are the three possible consequences of the killing? Diyah (blood money), kaffarah (expiation), and qisas (retaliation). The passage rules that diyah is wajib on the killer's own wealth, kaffarah is wajib in mistaken killing, and qisas is not wajib.
The ruling distinguishes between intentional and mistaken killing for kaffarah, but diyah applies in both.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
For kaffarah, the dalil is the Quranic verse (4:92) which is absolute regarding location. For diyah, the dalil is that the inviolability (isma) of a Muslim is not lost by entering Dar al-Harb with aman. For qisas, the dalil is that it requires power (mana'ah) which depends on the Imam and community, absent in Dar al-Harb.
The proofs are from Quran, legal principle, and practical impossibility.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for each
For kaffarah, the verse is mutlaq, so it applies wherever the killing occurs. For diyah, isma is a permanent attribute tied to the person, not the place. For qisas, the condition of enforcement authority is not met.
The mutlaq nature of the verse is key—no qualification for location.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools might argue that qisas could be applied if the Muslim community is present or if ta'zir (discretionary punishment) could be used. The Hanafi school maintains that qisas requires formal state authority.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is based on practical reality.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi. The reasoning is consistent with the principles of isma and the need for state authority in capital cases.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is noted; the ruling is relied upon.

وَإِذَا دَخَلَ مُسْلِمَانِ دَارَ الْحَرْبِ بِأَمَانٍ فَقَتَلَ أَحَدُهُمَا صَاحِبَهُ عَمَدًا أَوْ خَطَأَ فَعَلَى الْقَاتِلِ الدِّيَهُ فِي مَالِهِ وَعَلَيْهِ الْكَفَّارَةُ فِى الْخَطَا أَمَّا الْكَفَّارَةَ فَلِإطلاقِ الْكِتَابِ وَالدِيَّةُ لِأَنَّ العِصْمَةَ الثَّابِتَةَ بِالاحْرَازِ بِدَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ لَا تَبْطُلُ بِعَارِضِ الدُّخُولِ بِالْأَمَانِ وَإِنَّمَا لَا يَجِبُ الْقِصَاصُ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُ اسْتِنْفَاؤُه إِلَّا بِمَنَعَةٍ وَلَا مَنَعَةَ بِدُونِ الْإِمَامِ وَجَمَاعَةِ الْمُسْلِمِيْنَ وَلَمْ يُوجَدْ ذَالِكَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَإِنَّمَا تَجِبُ الدِّيَّةُ فِى مَالِهِ فِي الْعَمَدِ لِأَنَّ الْعَوَاقِلَ لَا تَعْقِلُ العَمَدَ وَ فِي الْخَطَا لأَنَّهُ لَا قَدْرَةَ لَهُمْ عَلَى القِيَانَةِ مَعَ تَبَائِنِ الدَّارَيْنِ وَالْوُجُوبُ عَلَيْهِمْ عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ تَرْكِهَا
ترجمہ وَإِذَا دَخَلَ مُسلِمَان .... الخ اور اگر دو مسلمان امان لے کر دار الحرب میں گئے اور وہاں ایک نے دوسرے کو قتل کر دیا خواہ عمداً ہو یا خطاہو تو قاتل پر مقتول کی دیت لازم آئے گی لیکن یہ دیت خاص قاتل کے اپنے مال پر واجب ہوگی یعنی اس کی برادری اس میں شریک نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور خطاء کی صورت میں اس پر کفارہ بھی واجب ہو گا ( یعنی عمد قتل کرنے کی صورت میں بھی قتل ( قصاص ) لازم نہیں آئے گا ) بلکہ صرف دیت لازم آئے گی ۔ اور قتل خطاء میں کفارہ اس لئے واجب ہوگا کہ کتاب اللہ میں حکم مطلق ہے ( یعنی کتاب اللہ قرآن مجید میں قتل خطاء کی صورت میں مطلقا کفارہ کا حکم ہے یعنی اس میں اس کی تفصیل نہیں ہے کہ یہ قتل دار الاسلام میں ہو یا دار الحرب میں ہو ۔ پس دار الاسلام ہونے کی کوئی خصوصیت نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ قرآن مجید میں ہے وَ مَنْ قَتَلَ مُؤْمِناً خَطَأَ فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُّؤْمِنَةٍ
And when two Muslims enter Dar al-Harb with aman, and one of them kills his companion intentionally or mistakenly, then on the killer is the diyah in his own wealth, and on him is the kaffarah in the case of mistake. As for the kaffarah, due to the absolute nature of the Book. And the diyah, because the inviolability established by being in Dar al-Islam is not nullified by the incidental entry with aman. Qisas is not obligatory because it cannot be carried out except with power, and there is no power without the Imam and the Muslim community, and that is not found in Dar al-Harb. The diyah is on his own wealth in intentional killing because the aqila do not bear intentional killing, and in mistaken killing because they have no ability to bear it due to the separation of the two abodes, and the obligation on them is contingent upon their being present.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where two Muslims, both with aman, are in Dar al-Harb and one kills the other. The ruling is that diyah (blood money) is obligatory on the killer from his own personal wealth, not on his aqila (male agnates). In cases of mistaken killing (khat'a), kaffarah (expiation) is also obligatory. The proof for kaffarah is from the absolute text of the Quran (Surah al-Nisa 4:92) which does not specify location. The diyah is due because the inviolability (isma) of the Muslim, which is established by his being in Dar al-Islam, is not negated by his temporary entry into Dar al-Harb with aman. Even in Dar al-Harb, his life is protected. Qisas (retaliatory execution) is not obligatory because it requires the authority of the Muslim Imam and community to execute, and that is absent in Dar al-Harb. The diyah is on the killer's own wealth because in intentional killing, the aqila never bear it (they only bear it for mistaken killing under normal circumstances). In mistaken killing, normally the aqila would bear it, but here they do not because they are not present in Dar al-Harb to assist, and the obligation is based on their ability to help. So the killer bears it himself.

Key Terms
عصمة (isma): Inviolability; the protection of life and property granted by Islamic law to a Muslim or dhimmi.
عاقلة (aqila): Male agnates (asaba) who bear the diyah in cases of mistaken killing.
قود (qisas): Retaliation, specifically capital punishment for intentional murder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is qisas not obligatory when a Muslim kills another Muslim in Dar al-Harb with aman?
A) Because the victim was not a true Muslim
B) Because qisas cannot be carried out without the authority of the Imam and Muslim community
C) Because it was accidental
D) Because Dar al-Harb is not subject to Islamic law

Key Takeaway
A Muslim's inviolability is not location-dependent; diyah and kaffarah are due for killing in Dar al-Harb, but qisas is suspended due to absence of enforcement authority.

Harbi Becomes Dhimmi by Staying One Year After Imam's Warning
Ruling with rational proof on harbi becoming dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a harbi becomes a dhimmi after staying one full year following the Imam's warning, and explain the rational proof based on istihsan and prevention of harm.

Core Idea
A harbi who stays a year after the Imam's warning becomes a dhimmi with binding obligations.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Book of Siyar: the legal status of a harbi who enters Dar al-Islam with aman, is told by the Imam to leave, but remains for a full year. The Hanafi position is that such a person becomes a dhimmi, with all the accompanying rights and duties. The proof is based on rational reasoning (istihsan) that emphasizes the binding nature of the dhimmah contract and the harm that would result from allowing him to return to Dar al-Harb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a harbi staying in Dar al-Islam for one full year after the Imam has warned him to leave. The ruling: he becomes a dhimmi.
2
Identify the condition
The Imam must have issued a warning or statement telling the harbi to leave. The harbi must then stay for a complete year. The Imam may set a shorter grace period, but the one-year condition remains.
The Imam's option to set a shorter period does not change the one-year requirement for becoming dhimmi.
3
Identify the proof type
The proof is rational (dalil aqli) based on istihsan (juristic preference) and consideration of public interest (maslaha).
4
Explain the rational reasoning
Once the harbi becomes a dhimmi, the contract of dhimmah is binding and cannot be broken. Allowing him to return to Dar al-Harb would lead to loss of jizya, strengthen the enemy (his children may fight Muslims), and harm Muslim interests.
The reasoning is: harm (ḍarar) must be prevented, and the contract is irrevocable.
5
Note the Imam's discretion
The Imam has the authority to set a specific grace period shorter than a year (e.g., one month). However, the harbi only becomes dhimmi if he stays for a full year after the warning; the shorter deadline does not accelerate the status change.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هفتم كتاب السير گا۔ یعنی آئندہ وہ اپنے وطن نہیں جا سکے گا۔ کیونکہ امام نے تو اس کو پہلے ہی کہہ دیا تھا۔ اس کے باوجود وہ جب یہاں مقیم رہ گیا تو گویا اس نے خود ہی اپنے اوپر جز یہ لازم کر لیا اور اب وہ ذمی ہو گیا۔ اور امام کو اختیار ہے کہ سال سے کم مدت میں کوئی خاص وقت مثلاً 1 مہینے مقرر کر کے اسے مہلت دے دے۔ امام کے کہنے کے باوجود وہ ایک سال ٹھہرارہا تو وہ ذمی ہوگا وَإِذَا أَقَامَهَا بَعْدَ مَقَالِ الْإِمَامِ يَصِيرُ دَمِيًّا لِمَا قُلْنَا ثُمَّ لَا يُتْرَكُ أَنْ تَرْجِعَ إِلَى دَارِ الْحَرْبِ لِأَنَّ عَقْدَ الدِّمَّةِ لَا يَنقُضُ كَيْفَ وَإِنَّ فِيْهِ قَطَّعَ الْجِزْيَةِ وَجَعَلَ وَلَدِهِ حَرْبا عَلَيْنَا وَفِيهِ مَضَرَّةٌ بِالْمُسْلِمِينَ ترجمہ وَإِذَا أَقَامَها الخ اور جب امام کے کہنے اور مہلت دینے کے بعد بھی وہ سال بھر ( مجموعا ) رہ گیا تو وہ ذمی ہو جائے گا۔ جس کی دلیل بیان کی جاچکی ہے۔ کہ اس نے امام کی حکم عدولی کر کے خود پر جزیہ لازم کر لیا ہے۔ پھر اسے دار الحرب واپس جانے کے لئے نہیں چھوڑا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ اسے ذمی بنا کر اس کا ذمہ لے کر اس کے خلاف نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ پھر اسے چھوڑ دینے سے جزیہ کم ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کی اولا د ہمارے خلاف لڑنے کے لئے تیار ہو جائے گی۔ جس سے مسلمانوں کا سخت نقصان ہو گا ۔
Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya, Volume 7, Book of Siyar. [Explanation:] That is, in the future he will not be able to go to his homeland. Because the Imam had already told him. Despite that, when he stayed here, it was as if he imposed jizya on himself, and now he becomes a dhimmi. And the Imam has the option to give him a specific time less than a year, for example one month, as a grace period. Despite the Imam’s statement, he stays a year, so he becomes a dhimmi. And when he stays after the Imam’s statement, he becomes a dhimmi for what we have said. Then he is not left to return to Dar al-Harb because the contract of dhimmah is not broken. How so? Indeed in that is interruption of jizya, and making his child a harbi against us, and in that is harm to the Muslims. Translation: When after the Imam’s statement and granting of grace he stays a full year (in total), then he will become a dhimmi, whose proof has already been given: that by disobeying the Imam he imposed jizya on himself. Then he will not be allowed to return to Dar al-Harb, because once he has been made a dhimmi and his liability taken, it cannot be acted against. Then leaving him would reduce jizya, and his child would become ready to fight against us, causing great loss to Muslims.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the status of a harbi who enters Dar al-Islam with aman and is told by the Imam to leave, but stays for a full year. The ruling states that he becomes a dhimmi. The commentator explains the reasoning: by staying despite the Imam's order, he effectively consents to pay jizya and remain permanently. Once he becomes a dhimmi, he cannot return to Dar al-Harb because the contract of dhimmah is binding and unbreakable. The passage also notes that allowing him to leave would harm Muslim interests by reducing jizya and increasing enemy manpower. The Imam has discretion to set a shorter deadline if he wishes.

Key Terms
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim from Dar al-Harb who has not been granted aman or dhimmah.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim who lives permanently in Dar al-Islam under a contract of protection, paying jizya.
امان (aman): Safe conduct granted to a harbi for temporary stay in Dar al-Islam.
جزیه (jizya): A tax paid by dhimmis in return for protection and exemption from military service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because he has paid jizya and must remain under Muslim protection.
B) Because the contract of dhimmah is binding and unbreakable, and allowing return would harm Muslims.
C) Because the Imam forbids it as a punishment.
D) Because his children will become Muslims.

Key Takeaway
A harbi who stays one full year after the Imam's warning becomes a dhimmi, and the contract is irrevocable to prevent harm to the Muslim community.

Becoming Dhimmi: The Role of Kharaj Imposition on Land
Ruling with proof via qiyas on when a harbi becomes dhimmi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a harbi who purchases kharaji land becomes a dhimmi, and explain the qiyas reasoning (jizya analogy) that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
A harbi becomes dhimmi only when kharaj is imposed, not upon purchase alone.

In this passage, we examine a specific case in international law (siyar): a non-Muslim enemy (harbi) who enters Dar al-Islam with a safe conduct (aman) and purchases land subject to kharaj. The key question is: at what point does he acquire the legal status of a dhimmi (protected resident)? The ruling clarifies that mere purchase does not suffice; it is the imposition of the land tax (kharaj) that triggers the change. This reasoning is based on an analogy (qiyas) between kharaj on land and jizya on the person, both being taxes that imply acceptance of permanent residence under Islamic sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What does the harbi do? What is the ruling on his status? The passage states that a harbi who buys kharaji land does not become dhimmi by purchase alone; he becomes dhimmi only when kharaj is actually imposed on the land.
The Arabic key phrase: 'idha wudi'a alayhi al-kharaj fahuwa dhimmi'.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The proof cited is qiyas: 'kharaj on land is like jizya on the head'. This is a clear analogy (qiyas jali) to the established rule that jizya obligates residence.
The illa is the imposition of a tax that implies permanent residence.
3
Analyze the qiyas structure
Asl: jizya on a harbi makes him a dhimmi. Far': kharaj on land purchased by a harbi. Illa: both are taxes that indicate acceptance of permanent residence. Hukm: imposition of kharaj makes the harbi a dhimmi.
The text explicitly uses 'bi-manzilat' (is like) to draw the analogy.
4
Understand the condition of imposition
Mere purchase is insufficient because the harbi may buy land for trade (tijarah) without intending to settle. The condition ensures that the harbi's acceptance of the tax demonstrates intention to reside.
The counterargument: 'he may buy it for trade'.
5
Examine the expansion from al-Jami' al-Saghir
Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir reinforces the condition: 'when kharaj is assessed on him, from that time he becomes a dhimmi'. This is explicit and derives many rulings from it.
The commentator emphasizes not to be heedless of this condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ دَخَلَ الْحَرْبِيُّ دَارَ نَابِ مَان فَاشْتَرى أَرْضَ حَرَاجِ فَإِذَا وُضِعَ عَلَيْهِ الْخِرَاجُ فَهُوَ ذِمِّيُّ لِأَنَّ حَرَاجَ الْأَرْضِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ خِرَاجِ الرَّأْسِ وَإِذَا الْتَزَمَهُ صَارَ مُلْتَرَ مَانِ الْمُقَامَ فِي دَارِنَا أَمَّا بِمُجَرَّدِ الشَّرَاءِ لَا يَصِيرُ وَمَا لأَنَّهُ قَدْيَشْتَرِبُهَا لِلتِّجَارَةِ وَإِذَا لَزِمَهُ حَرَاجُ الْأَرْضِ فَبَعْدَ ذَالِكَ تَلْزَمُهُ الْجِزْيَةُ لِسَنَةٍ مُسْتَقْبَلَةٍ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ ذِمِّيَّا بِلْزُومِ الْحَرَاحِ فَتُعْتَبَرُ الْمُدَّ مِنْ وَقْتِ وُجُوبِه وَقَوْلُهُ فِى الْكِتَابِ فَإِذَا وُضِعَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَرَاجُ فَهُوَ ذِمّى سريح بِشَرطِ الْوَضْعِ فَيُخَرَّجُ عَلَيه أَحْكَامُ جُمَّةٌ فَلَا يُغْفَل عَنْهُ ترجمہ اگر کوئی حربی ہمارے ملک دار الاسلام میں امان لے کر آیا یا اس نے یہاں کوئی خراجی زمین خریدی ۔ اس بناء پر جب بھی اس زمین پر خراج لازم کیا جائے گا تو وہ ذمی ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ زمین پر خراج لازم کرنا آدمی پر جزیہ لازم کرنے کے مانند ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب کہ اس حربی نے خود پر خراج کو لازم کر لیا تو گویا اس نے دار الاسلام میں خود رہنے کو لازم کر لیا ۔ مگر صرف زمین خرید لینے سے وہ ذمی نہیں ہو جائے گا کیونکہ زمین کبھی تجارت کے لئے بھی خریدی جاتی ہے۔ جب زمین پر خراج لازم کر دیا گیا تو اس کے بعد آئندہ سال کے لئے اس کی ذات پر جزیہ لازم کر دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ زمین پر خراج لازم ہونے سے ہی وہ ذمی ہو جائے گا۔ اس طرح جب سے اس پر جزیہ لازم ہو گا اسی وقت سے اس کی مدت شروع ہو جائے گی۔ اور امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے اپنی کتاب جامع صغیر میں جو یہ فرمایا ہے کہ جس وقت بھی اس پر خراج مقرر کیا جائے گا اسی وقت سے وہ ذمی ہو جائے گا۔ تو اس کلام میں صراحت کے ساتھ یہ شرط بنادی گئی کہ جزیہ مقرر کرنے پر ہی وہ ذمی ہو جائے گا یعنی اس سے پہلے تک اس پر ذمی ہو جانے کا حکم نہیں لگایا جائے گا پس اس کہنے پر اس سے بہت سے احکام نکل آتے ہیں ۔ اس لئے اس شرط کو بھی نہیں بھولنا چاہئے ۔
If a harbi enters our land (Dar al-Islam) with aman and buys a kharaji land, then when kharaj is placed upon it, he is a dhimmi, because kharaj on land is like jizya on the head. When he undertakes it, he becomes an undertaker of residence in our land. As for mere purchase, he does not become (dhimmi), because he may buy it for trade. When the land kharaj becomes due, after that the jizya becomes due on him for the following year, because he becomes a dhimmi by the imposition of kharaj. So the period is considered from the time of its obligation. And his statement in the book: 'When kharaj is placed upon him, he is a dhimmi' is explicit with the condition of imposition, so many rulings are derived from it; so do not be heedless of it. Translation: If a harbi enters our land Dar al-Islam with aman and buys a kharaji land, then when kharaj is imposed on that land, he will become a dhimmi. Because imposing kharaj on land is like imposing jizya on a person. So when the harbi has imposed kharaj on himself, it is as if he has required himself to stay in Dar al-Islam. But mere purchase does not make him dhimmi, because land is sometimes bought for trade. When kharaj is imposed on the land, after that jizya will be imposed on his person for the following year, because he becomes dhimmi by the imposition of kharaj. Thus from the time jizya becomes due, the period begins. And Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said in his book al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Whenever kharaj is assessed on him, from that time he becomes a dhimmi.' So in that statement the condition is clearly made that he becomes dhimmi only upon assessment of kharaj, meaning before that the ruling of being dhimmi is not applied. So many rulings come out of this statement, therefore this condition should not be forgotten.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage deals with a harbi who enters Dar al-Islam with aman and purchases land subject to kharaj (land tax). The key point is that he does not become a dhimmi merely by purchasing the land; he only becomes a dhimmi when the state imposes kharaj on that land. The rationale is that kharaj on land is analogous to jizya on a person: both are taxes that obligate residence under Islamic rule. If he buys land for trade, he may not intend to settle permanently. Once kharaj is imposed, however, his acceptance of that tax implies acceptance of permanent residence and thus he attains dhimmi status. The passage also notes that jizya is then due for the following year, and the period of his dhimmi status begins from that time. A special note is made about Imam Muhammad's statement in al-Jami' al-Saghir, emphasizing that the condition of imposition is crucial.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on agricultural land in Islamic state, typically on conquered lands.
ارض خراج (ard kharaj): Land subject to kharaj tax, usually former conquered lands.

Checkpoint
