Harbi's Return Voids Aman: Deposit and Debt Become Fay'
Ruling with proof: harbi's return voids aman and property becomes fay'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of a harbi's deposit (wadi'a) and debt (dayn) when he returns to Dar al-Harb after aman, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind each.

Core Idea
Return to Dar al-Harb voids aman; all property left in Dar al-Islam becomes fay'.

In this passage, Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a harbi enters Dar al-Islam with aman, deposits property or has debts, then returns to Dar al-Harb. What happens to his legal protection (aman) and his property? The answer reveals a key principle in Hanafi siyar: the harbi's return nullifies his aman, and his property follows his status. This lesson unpacks the ruling, focusing on the deposit and debt, and the rational proofs (adillah 'aqliyyah) that support the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Understand that a harbi who enters Dar al-Islam with aman and then voluntarily returns to Dar al-Harb has voided his aman. The consequence: his blood becomes permissible (mubah al-damm) for Muslims, and any property he left in Dar al-Islam is at risk.
The ruling is not about the act of returning itself, but the legal consequence of that return.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text states: 'because he voided his aman (li-annahu abṭala amānahu).' This is the core reasoning: the return is a voluntary act that terminates the protection granted. No explicit Quran or hadith is cited; the proof is a rational inference (dalil 'aqli).
In Hanafi usul, such rational proofs are valid when the underlying cause (sabab) is clear.
3
Analyze the application to the deposit (wadi'a)
The deposit is considered constructively in the harbi's hand because the depositee's hand is like the depositor's hand (yad al-mūda` ka-yadihi). Therefore, it follows the status of the depositor: like his person, his property becomes fay'.
The principle of 'al-yad al-ḥukmiyyah' (constructive possession) is key here.
4
Analyze the application to the debt (dayn)
For the debt, the text argues that possession over a debt is established only through demand (muṭālabah). Since the harbi's right to demand has fallen (due to the voiding of aman and his return), the debt is nullified. The debtor's hand over his own property is stronger than the general public's claim, so the debtor's property remains with him; the debt simply drops.
This preserves the debtor's ownership while extinguishing the harbi's claim.
5
Note the practical consequence
If the harbi is captured or the Muslims prevail and he is killed, the deposit becomes fay' (booty) for the Muslim treasury, and the debt is cancelled. The prior aman provides no ongoing protection.
Contrast with a harbi who remains in Dar al-Islam: his aman continues and his property remains protected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ أَنَّ حَرْبِيَّادَخَلَ دَارَ نَا بِأَمَانٍ ثُمَّ عَادَ إِلى دَارِ الْحَرْبِ وَتَرَكَ وَدِيْعَةً عِنْدَمُسْلِمٍ أَوْ ذِي أَوْ دَيْنَا فِي ذِمَّتِهِمْ فَقَدْ صَارَ أَوْدى دَمُهُ مُبَاحًا بِالْعَوْدِ لِأَنَّهُ أَبْطَلَ أَمَانَهُ وَمَا فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ مِنْ مَّالِهِ عَلَى خَطَرٍ فَإِنْ أُسِرَ أَوْ ظُهَرَ عَلَى الدَّارِ فَقْنِلَ سَقَطَتْ ديُونُهُ وَصَارَتِ الْوَدِيْعَةُ فَيْنًا أَمَّا الْوَدِيعَةُ فَلِأَنَّهَا فِي يَدِهِ تَقْدِيرًا لِأَنَّ يَدَ الْمُودَع كَيْدِهِ فَيَصِيرُ فَيْنًا تَبْعًا لِنَفْسِهِ وَأَمَّا الدِّينِ فَلأَنَّ إِثْبَاتَ الْيَدِ عَلَيْهِ بِوَاسِطَةِ الْمُطَالَبَةِ وَ قَدْ سَقَطَتْ وَيَدُ مَنْ عَلَيْهِ أَسَبَقُ إِلَيْهِ مِنْ يَدِ الْعَامَّةِ فَيَخْتَصُّ. ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی حربی ہمارے ملک میں امان و اجازت کے ساتھ داخل ہوا۔ پھر وہ اپنے ملک دارالحرب لوٹ گیا۔ اور چلتے ہوئے یہاں کسی مسلم کے پاس اپنی کوئی امانت یا ان کے ذمہ کچھ قرض چھوڑ کر گیا۔ تو (اس کے واپس چلے جانے سے اس کا امان نامہ ختم ہو کر وہ حسب سابق ہو گیا کہ لوٹ کر آنے سے ) اس کا خون مسلمانوں کے لئے مباح ہو گیا۔ اور دار الاسلام میں وہ جو کچھ مال چھوڑ کر گیا تھا وہ سب خطرہ میں ہے (یعنی اس کا یہ مال امان سابق باقی رکھنے اور حق جتانے کے لائق نہیں رہا ہے چنانچہ اگر وہ آنے کے بعد قید کر لیا جائے یا دار الحرب میں رہتے ہوئے مسلمانوں کے دار الحرب پر غالب ہونے کی صورت میں قتل کر دیا جائے تو اس کی پہلے کی رکھی ہوئی امانت مال غنیمت ہو جائے گی اور چھوڑا ہوا قرضہ ختم اور ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ امانت تو معنی اس کے ہاتھ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ دارالاسلام میں جس کے پاس رکھ کر گیا تھا اس کا قبضہ خود اس حربی کے قبضہ کی طرح ہے تو اب جیسے وہ خود غنیمت کے حکم میں ( اور مباح الدم ) ہو گیا اسی کے تابع ہو کر اس کی رکھی ہوئی امانت بھی غنیمت ہوگئی ۔ اور وہ قرض جو کسی پر چھوڑ کر گیا تھا یعنی کسی قرضدار پر جو اس کا قرض باقی ہے وہ اس لئے ساقط ہو جائے گا کہ اس کا مطالبہ کرنے کے بعد ہی اس پر قبضہ ثابت ہوگا۔ اور حربی کے واپس چلے جانے کی وجہ سے اس کے مطالبہ کا حق ساقط ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اس سے تمام مسلمانوں کا حق متعلق ہو گیا مگر جس شخص پر وہ حق باقی ہے چونکہ اس کا قبضہ اس مال پر دوسروں کی
And if a harbi entered our land with aman, then returned to Dar al-Harb and left a deposit with a Muslim or a dhimmi, or a debt in their liability, then his blood becomes permissible (mubah) by the return, because he voided his aman. And whatever property he has in Dar al-Islam is at risk. For if he is captured or if (the Muslims) prevail over the land and he is killed, his debts fall and the deposit becomes fay'. As for the deposit, because it is in his hand constructively (since the hand of the depositee is like his hand), so it becomes fay' following himself. As for the debt, because establishing hand over it is through claim, and that has fallen; and the hand of the one upon whom it is due has prior claim over the general public, so it becomes specific. Translation: And if a harbi entered our country with aman and permission, then returned to his country Dar al-Harb, and while leaving left some deposit with a Muslim or some debt in their liability, then (by his return, his aman is terminated and he becomes as before, meaning upon return his blood becomes permissible for Muslims). And whatever property he left in Dar al-Islam is all at risk (i.e., this property is no longer worthy of remaining under previous aman and claiming right). So if after coming (back) he is captured or while in Dar al-Harb the Muslims prevail over Dar al-Harb and he is killed, then his deposit left earlier becomes spoils of war, and the debt left is nullified and dropped. Because the deposit is in his hand in meaning, since the hand of the person with whom he left it is like his own hand. So just as he himself becomes subject to the rule of spoils (and his blood mubah), similarly the deposit follows him and becomes spoils. As for the debt left on someone, i.e., the debt that is still owed to him, that drops because possession over it is established only through demand, and his right of demand has dropped due to his return. And the right of all Muslims attaches to it, but the person on whom it is due has prior claim over that property over others...
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage rules on the status of a harbi who entered Dar al-Islam with aman, then voluntarily returns to Dar al-Harb. By his return, he voids his aman, and his blood becomes permissible (mubah al-damm) for Muslims. Any property he left behind in Dar al-Islam, whether a deposit (wadi'a) or a debt (dayn), loses its protected status. If he is later captured or killed, the deposit becomes fay' (spoils of war) because the depositee's possession is considered an extension of the harbi's possession. The debt is nullified because the right to demand it has fallen, and the property of the debtor becomes subject to the general Muslim public, though the debtor may have a prior claim over others. The text emphasizes that the deposit is treated as if still in the harbi's hand, so it follows his fate.

Key Terms
مباح الدم (mubah al-damm): One whose blood may be lawfully shed; i.e., for whom killing is permissible.
وديعة (wadi'a): A deposit left for safekeeping.
فىء (fay'): Booty taken from enemies without battle, or property that becomes state property.

Key Takeaway
A harbi who returns to Dar al-Harb loses all rights to property left in Dar al-Islam; his deposit becomes fay' and his debts are nullified.

Property of a Harbi Killed Without Conquest
Ruling on a harbi's debts and amanat when killed without Muslim conquest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a harbi's debts and amanat are not ghanimah when he is killed without Muslim conquest, and explain the reasoning based on the continuity of aman.

Core Idea
The aman of a harbi protects his property even after death if the enemy land remains unconquered.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in the Hanafi law of warfare: a non-Muslim (harbi) who entered Dar al-Islam with a safe conduct (aman) is killed in battle, but the Muslim forces do not conquer Dar al-Harb. The question arises whether his property in Dar al-Islam becomes war booty (ghanimah) or remains protected. The ruling draws a careful distinction based on the nature of aman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario involves a harbi who entered Dar al-Islam with aman (safe conduct). He is killed (either in battle or naturally) before the Muslims conquer his home territory. What happens to his property (debts owed to him and items left in trust) that is located in Dar al-Islam?
The key condition is that the Muslims do not conquer Dar al-Harb.
2
State the ruling
The passage rules that such property is not ghanimah. It belongs to the harbi himself (if alive) or to his heirs (if dead). Debts and amanat are to be returned to the heirs.
This applies whether the harbi is killed or dies naturally.
3
Identify the reasoning (dalil)
The reasoning is given in the text: 'because his person did not become spoil, and similarly his property; and the ruling of aman remains concerning his property.' The aman that protected his life from enslavement also protects his property from confiscation until the dar is conquered.
This is an analogical reasoning (qiyas): property follows the status of the person.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
The principle is that the effect of aman is comprehensive: it secures both life and property. Conquest of Dar al-Harb would terminate the aman retroactively, but without conquest, the aman remains intact.
This principle ensures that pledges of safety are honored even after the recipient's death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر وہ حربی قتل کر دیا گیا اور مسلمان دار الحرب پر غالب نہ آ سکے تو اسکا چھوڑا ہوا قرض اور امانت اس کے وارثوں میں تقسیم ہوگی
وَإِنْ قُتِلَ وَلَمْ يُظْهَرُ عَلَى الدَّارِ فَالْقَرُضُ وَالْوَدِيْعَةُ لورثته وكذالك إِذَامَاتَ لِأَنَّ نَفْسَهُ لَمْ تَصِرُ مَعْنُومَةً فكذالك مالة و هذا لأنَّ حُكم الأمان باق فِيمَالِهِ فَيُرَدُّ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ عَلى وَرَثَتِهِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ
ترجمه: اگر مسلمانوں سے مقابلہ میں صرف وہی حربی قتل کر دیا گیا اور عام مسلمان اس دار الحرب پر غالب نہیں آسکے تو اس کا چھوڑا ہوا قرض یا کسی شخص کے پاس رکھی ہوئی امانت جو کچھ بھی دارالاسلام میں ہے اس کے وارثوں کی میراث ہوگی۔ اسی طرح اگر وہ خود مر گیا (قتل نہیں کیا گیا) تو اس کا مال بھی غنیمت نہ ہوا۔ کیونکہ دارالاسلام میں آنے کے لئے جو اس نے امان نامہ حاصل کیا تھا وہ اس کے مال کے بارے میں باقی ہے۔ اسی لئے اس کا قرض یا امانت جو کچھ بھی ہے وہ خود اس کو یا اس کے بعد اس کے وارثوں کو واپس دی جائے گی۔
If he (the harbi) is killed and the Muslims are not victorious over the abode (of war), then the debt and the trust (amanat) belong to his heirs, and likewise if he dies naturally, because his person did not become a spoil (ghanimah), and similarly his property. And this is because the ruling of aman remains concerning his property, so it is returned to him or to his heirs after him.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: when a harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory) enters Dar al-Islam with an aman (safe conduct) and is later killed by Muslims in battle while the Muslims do not conquer Dar al-Harb, or if he dies naturally, his property (debts owed to him and items left in trust) remains under the protection of aman and is not considered war booty. Therefore, it is returned to him if alive, or to his heirs after his death. The reasoning provided is that the aman he received continues to protect his property, just as it protected his person from being enslaved. This is an application of the principle that aman grants inviolability to both life and property.

Key Terms
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim who is a subject of enemy territory (Dar al-Harb).
امان (aman): Safe conduct or guarantee of security granted to a harbi for a limited time.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule with which a state of war exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Status of a Harbi Convert's Family and Property After Conquest
Rulings on a harbi who converts after entering with aman; fate of wife, children, and property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal status of a harbi convert's wife, children, and property after conquest, and explain the role of territorial separation (ikhtilaf al-darayn) in determining taba'iyyah.

Core Idea
A harbi's conversion does not protect family or property in Dar al-Harb without physical custody and territorial unity.

This passage from the Hidayah deals with a specific scenario: a harbi enters Dar al-Islam with aman, converts, and then his homeland is conquered by Muslims. The key question is what happens to his wife, children, and property left behind. The ruling turns on the concept of taba'iyyah (following) and the effect of differing territories (ikhtilaf al-darayn). Let's walk through the analysis step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Core Principle
First, understand the facts: a harbi enters Dar al-Islam with aman, converts, and later his home territory (Dar al-Harb) is conquered. The underlying principle is that conversion grants protection to the convert's person and property only within Dar al-Islam; it does not automatically extend to persons or property in Dar al-Harb. Territorial separation (ikhtilaf al-darayn) affects legal capacity and taba'iyyah.
Note the sequence: conversion occurs before conquest.
2
Distinguish Between Family Members: Wife and Adult Children vs. Minors
The text treats the wife and adult children as independent harbis. Their legal status does not change due to the father's conversion. They become ghanimah (booty) because they are adult harbis and not considered followers (tabi'). For minors, however, the rule of taba'iyyah applies: they can follow their father's Islam and become Muslim and free, but only if they are under his physical custody (fi yadihi) and within the same dar. Since they are in different territories (Dar al-Harb), the following is not realized, so they also become booty.
Focus on the condition 'fi yadihi wa tahta wilayatihi' and the effect of ikhtilaf al-darayn.
3
Analyze the Ruling for Property
The convert's property deposited with a dhimmi, harbi, or Muslim all becomes ghanimah. The convert's own protection (by conversion) does not extend to his property in Dar al-Harb because the property was not in his actual possession or under the protection of Dar al-Islam at the time of his conversion. Territorial separation prevents the property from becoming protected (muhraz).
Contrast with the case where the property was in Dar al-Islam at the time of conversion.
4
Derive the General Principle and Apply to the Fetus
The general principle: taba'iyyah (following) in legal status requires physical custody and territorial unity. The fetus in the womb is considered part of the mother's body until birth, so it follows her status and becomes booty with her.
This ruling is consistent with the earlier principle that the fetus is a part of the mother.

حصہ کسی ذمی کے پاس اور تھوڑ اکسی حربی کے پاس اور کچھ مال کسی مسلمان کے پاس بطور امانت رکھا ہے پھر وہ حربی دار الاسلام میں مسلمان ہو گیا ۔ پھر غازیوں نے دارالحرب کو مغلوب کر لیا تو اس حربی کا کل مال غنیمت کا مال ہو جائے گا۔ چنانچہ بیوی اور بالغ اولاد کا غنیمت ہونا تو ظاہر ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ سب حربی اور کافر اور بالغ ہیں۔ اس لئے ایک حربی کے مسلمان ہو جانے کی وجہ سے یہ بالغ اولا د اور اس کی بیوی اس کی تابع ہو کر مسلمان نہیں ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح اس حربی کی بیوی اگر حاملہ ہو تو اس کے پیٹ کا بچہ بھی غنیمت ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ جب تک پیدا ہو کر پیٹ سے جدا نہیں ہو جاتا تب تک اپنی ماں کا جزء ہے لیکن اس کے وہ بچے جو ابھی تک نابالغ اور چھوٹے ہیں تو وہ اپنے باپ کے تابع ہو کر اسی صورت میں مسلمان سمجھے جائیں گے جبکہ اپنے باپ کے قبضہ اور اس کی ماتحتی اور ایک ہی حکومت میں ہوں ۔ حالانکہ ان کا باپ دارالاسلام میں اور وہ چھوٹے بچے دار الحرب میں ہیں۔ اس لئے دونوں حکومتوں کی جدائی کے ساتھ چھوٹے بچے اپنے باپ کے تابع نہیں ہو سکتے ہیں ۔ اسی طرح اس حربی کے خود مسلمان ہو جانے سے اس کی جان تو محفوظ ہو جائے گی مگر اس کے محفوظ ہو جانے سے اس کے اموال محفوظ نہ ہوں گے ۔ کیونکہ دونوں ملک علیحدہ ہیں ۔ یعنی وہ خود دار الاسلام میں اور اس کے اموال سب دار الحرب میں نہیں اس لئے یہ سب غنیمت ہو جائیں گے۔
And if a harbi enters our land with aman, and he has a wife in Dar al-Harb, and minor and adult children, and property, a part of which he deposited with a dhimmi, a part with a harbi, and a part with a Muslim, and he accepts Islam here, then the land is conquered, then all of that is in... As for the wife and his adult children, they are booty because they are harbi adults and not followers. Similarly, what is in her womb if she is pregnant, for what we said before. As for his minor children, the minor only becomes Muslim by following his father's Islam if he is in his hand and under his authority, and with the separation of the two lands, that is not realized. Similarly, his property does not become protected by his own acquisition due to the difference of the two lands, so all remains as booty.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah provides rulings on the fate of a harbi's family and property when he enters Dar al-Islam with aman, converts, and then Muslims conquer his homeland. The commentary explains that the wife and adult children become ghanimah (booty) because they are adult harbis and not followers of the convert. A fetus in the womb also becomes booty as part of the mother. Minor children, however, do not become Muslim or free because they were not under the father's physical custody at the time of conversion due to the separation of dar (territories). Similarly, all property left in Dar al-Harb becomes booty, regardless of with whom it was deposited, because the owner's conversion did not occur in the same land as the property.

Key Terms
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim subject of Dar al-Harb who is not under a covenant of aman or dhimma.
غنيمة (ghanimah): Booty taken from the enemy by force during war.
تابع (tabi'): A person who follows another in legal status; here, a minor child following the father's conversion.
إختلاف الدارين (ikhtilaf al-darayn): The separation of territories (Dar al-Islam and Dar al-Harb) that affects legal capacity and jurisdiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A harbi enters Dar al-Islam with aman, converts to Islam, and then Muslims conquer Dar al-Harb where his minor children reside. According to the Hanafi position in the passage, what is the status of those minor children?
A) They become free and Muslim, following their father's conversion.
B) They become booty (ghanimah) because they were not under the father's custody at the time of conversion.
C) They remain free but non-Muslim until they reach puberty.
D) They become dhimmi subjects.

Key Takeaway
Conversion of a harbi does not automatically protect family or property in Dar al-Harb; territorial separation blocks taba'iyyah for minors and prevents property from being secured.

Status of a Harbi Convert's Family and Property
Ruling on a harbi who converts in Dar al-Harb then moves to Dar al-Islam before conquest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of a harbi convert's minor children and deposited property when he moves to Dar al-Islam before conquest, and distinguish between protected and unprotected hands.

Core Idea
Conversion in Dar al-Harb before conquest frees minor children but only property in protected hands remains his; unprotected property becomes booty.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case from the law of jihad: a harbi who converts to Islam while still in enemy territory, then emigrates to Dar al-Islam before his former homeland is conquered. The Hidayah distinguishes between his minor children (who follow him), his wife and adult children (who do not), his property deposited with a Muslim or dhimmi (protected) and property in the hands of a harbi (unprotected). The key conceptual tool is the protected hand (yad muhtaramah) and the principle of tab'iyyah (following).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios of conversion timing
This passage deals with conversion in Dar al-Harb then moving to Dar al-Islam before conquest. If conversion occurred after arriving in Dar al-Islam, the ruling may differ (not discussed). Then identify the elements: minor children, deposited property, wife/adult children, property in harbi's hand.
2
Apply the principle of tab'iyyah for minors
The condition for minors following their father is that they were under his authority (wilayah) at the time of conversion and that the land is one (same dar). Since both were in Dar al-Harb, they follow. Note that after moving, they are in Dar al-Islam, and the conquest of Dar al-Harb does not affect their status.
The Arabic says 'إذ الدار واحدة' — the dar is one.
3
Distinguish between protected and unprotected hands
Property deposited with a Muslim or dhimmi is in a protected hand (yad muhtaramah), so it remains the convert's property. Property in the hand of a harbi is not protected, so it becomes ghanimah upon conquest.
The hand of a harbi is not respected because he is not under Islamic protection.
4
Identify the status of wife and adult children
They are not followers (tab') of the father; they are independent adults, so they remain as original harbis and become booty. The text says 'فلما قلنا' referring back to the previous ruling that they are booty.
This was established earlier in the chapter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ إِنْ أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ ثُمَّ جَاءَ فَظْهِرَ عَلَى الدَّارِ فَأَوْلَادُهُ الصِّغَارُ أَحْرَارٌ مُسْلِمُونَ تَبْعًا لِأَبِيهِمْ لِأَنَّهُم تَحْتَ وِلَايَتِهِ حِيْنَ أَسْلَمَ إِذِ الدَّارُ وَاحِدَةً وَمَا كَانَ مِنْ قَالَ أَوْدَعَهُ مُسْلِمًا أَوْ دِمِّيَّا فَهُوَ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ فِي يَدِ مُحْتَرَمَةٍ وَيَدُهُ يَدِهِ وَمَا سِوَى ذَالِكَ فَى أَمَّا الْمَرْأَةُ وَأَوْلَادُهُ الْكِبَارُ فَلِمَا قُلْنَا وَأَمَّا الْمَالُ الَّذِي فِي يَدِ الْحَرْبِي فَلِأَنَّهُ لَم يَصِرْ مَعْصُومًا لأَنَّ يَدَ الْحَرْبِي لَيْسَتْ يَدا مُحْتَرَمَةً ترجمہ اور اگر کوئی حربی پہلے دار الحرب میں اسلام لایا پھر دار الاسلام آ گیا۔ اس کے بعد مجاہدین نے اس کے ملک پر قبضہ کر لیا تو اس کے چھوٹے بچے اپنے باپ کے تابع ہو کر آزاد و مسلمان ہیں۔ کیونکہ اسلام لانے کے وقت وہ بچے اس کی ماتحتی اور اختیار میں تھے اس لئے کہ اس وقت وہ سب ایک ہی ملک یعنی دار الحرب میں تھے ۔ اور اس کے مال میں سے اس نے جو کچھ کسی مسلمان یاڈمی کے پاس امانہ رکھا تھا تو وہ اسی کا رہے گا ۔ کیونکہ وہ محترم قبضہ میں ہے اور قابض نے جو قبضہ کیا ہے وہ اس کے اپنے قبضہ کے حکم میں ہے۔ اور ان مذکورہ افراد اور اموال کے سوا اس کا جو کچھ بھی کہیں ہے وہ سب مال غنیمت ہے۔ کیونکہ بیوی اور بڑے بالغ اولاد کا مملوک ہونا تو اس لئے ہے کہ یہ لوگ بالغ حربی ہیں اور اب اس حربی کے تابع نہیں ہیں۔ اسی طرح اس کا وہ مال جو کسی حربی کے قبضہ میں ہے وہ اس لئے غنیمت کا مال سمجھا جائے گا کہ وہ مال محترم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حربی کا قبضہ محترم نہیں ہوتا ہے۔
And if he accepts Islam in Dar al-Harb, then comes, and the land is conquered, then his minor children are free and Muslim, following their father, because they were under his authority when he accepted Islam, since the land is one. And whatever property he deposited with a Muslim or a dhimmi is his, because it is in a protected hand, and his hand is his (the owner's) hand. And other than that is booty. As for the wife and his adult children, for what we said. And as for the property in the hand of a harbi, because it did not become protected, for the hand of a harbi is not a protected hand.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents a contrasting scenario: if the harbi converts while still in Dar al-Harb (before coming to Dar al-Islam), his minor children become free and Muslim followers because at the time of his conversion, they were under his authority in the same territory. However, property deposited with a Muslim or dhimmi remains his property because those hands are protected (muhtaramah). Property in the hands of a harbi becomes booty because the harbi's hand is not protected. The wife and adult children remain booty as they are not followers.

Key Terms
يد محترمة (yad muhtaramah): A protected hand, i.e., possession that is legally respected, such as that of a Muslim or dhimmi.
تبعية (tab'iyyah): The legal status of following another person, e.g., minors following their father in conversion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a harbi converts to Islam in Dar al-Harb and then moves to Dar al-Islam, what happens to the property he had deposited with a dhimmi in Dar al-Harb after the Muslims conquer that land?
A) It becomes booty (ghanimah) because it was left in enemy territory.
B) It remains his property because it was in a protected hand.
C) It becomes the property of the dhimmi with whom it was deposited.
D) It is divided equally between the owner and the Muslim treasury.

Key Takeaway
The protection of a convert's property depends on the hand (yad) holding it, not on the owner's status; minor children follow the father in conversion only if they were under his authority in the same territory.

Status of a Harbi Convert's Family and Property After Conquest
Ruling on fate of harbi convert's family and property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of a harbi convert's minor children, adult children, wife, and property after conquest, and apply the concept of yad muhtaramah to determine ownership.

Core Idea
A harbi convert's minor children follow his religion and freedom; his property's fate depends on whose hand holds it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical moment: a harbi accepts Islam in enemy territory, then escapes to the Islamic state, after which his former territory is conquered. The ruling distinguishes between those who are subservient to him (minor children) and those who are independent legal persons (wife, adult children). It also distinguishes property based on whether it is in a protected hand (Muslim/dhimmi) or an unprotected hand (harbi). This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principle that ownership is tied to the inviolability of possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A harbi converts to Islam in Dar al-Harb, then travels to Dar al-Islam, and later the Muslims conquer his former territory.
The conversion happened while the territory was still Dar al-Harb.
2
Categorize dependents: minors vs. adults
Minor children are under the father's authority (tab'iyyah) and become free Muslims. Adult children and the wife are independent, so they remain harbis and become spoils of war.
The principle of tab'iyyah applies to minors regardless of location.
3
Categorize property: protected vs. unprotected hand
Property entrusted to a Muslim or dhimmi is in a protected hand (yad muhtaramah), so it remains the convert's property. Property in the hand of a harbi is not protected and becomes booty.
The hand of a harbi is not muhtaramah.
4
Apply the concept of yad muhtaramah
A protected hand means the possession is inviolable. The convert's own hand is protected after his conversion, and the hand of a Muslim/dhimmi is protected. But the hand of a harbi is not.
5
Derive the ruling for each case
Minor children: free Muslims. Wife and adult children: harbis, become spoils. Property with Muslim/dhimmi: belongs to convert. Property with harbi: becomes booty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ أَسْلَمَ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ ثُمَّ جَاءَ فَظْهِرَ عَلَى الدَّارِ فَأَوْلَادُهُ الصِّغَارُ أَحْرَارٌ مُسْلِمُونَ تَبْعًا لِأَبِيهِمْ لِأَنَّهُم تَحْتَ وِلَايَتِهِ حِيْنَ أَسْلَمَ إِذِ الدَّارُ وَاحِدَةً وَمَا كَانَ مِنْ قَالَ أَوْدَعَهُ مُسْلِمًا أَوْ دِمِّيَّا فَهُوَ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ فِي يَدِ مُحْتَرَمَةٍ وَيَدُهُ يَدِهِ وَمَا سِوَى ذَالِكَ فَى أَمَّا الْمَرْأَةُ وَأَوْلَادُهُ الْكِبَارُ فَلِمَا قُلْنَا وَأَمَّا الْمَالُ الَّذِي فِي يَدِ الْحَرْبِي فَلِأَنَّهُ لَم يَصِرْ مَعْصُومًا لأَنَّ يَدَ الْحَرْبِي لَيْسَتْ يَدا مُحْتَرَمَةً
And if he accepted Islam in Dar al-Harb then came and the territory was conquered, then his young children are free Muslims following their father, because they were under his authority when he accepted Islam, since the territory is one [i.e., same] and whatever [property] he had deposited [i.e., entrusted] with a Muslim or a dhimmi, it is his because it is in a protected hand and that hand is like his hand. And besides that, as for the wife and his adult children, [they are not his] for what we said. And as for the property which is in the hand of a harbi, it is because it did not become inviolable because the hand of a harbi is not a protected hand.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Al-Hidayah. It addresses a specific scenario: a harbi (enemy combatant) embraces Islam in Dar al-Harb (territory of war) and then leaves to Dar al-Islam, after which Muslims conquer his former territory. The ruling distinguishes between categories of his dependents and property. His minor children become free and Muslim, following their father's status, because when he converted they were under his parental authority and the territory was the same (i.e., still Dar al-Harb at that time). The wife and adult children do not automatically share his status; they remain harbis because they are independent legal persons not subservient to him. Regarding property: any property he had entrusted to a Muslim or a dhimmi (a protected non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state) remains his, because it is held by a protected hand (yad muhtaramah) which has the same legal effect as his own possession. However, property in the hands of a harbi becomes spoils of war (ghanimah) because the hand of a harbi is not protected, and thus the property is unprotected and subject to capture. This ruling is based on the Hanafi principle of ownership depending on inviolability of possession, and the concept of loyalty following authority (tab'iyyah) for minors.

Key Terms
حَربِيّ (harbī): An enemy combatant from Dar al-Harb who is not under Muslim protection.
يَد مُحْتَرَمَة (yad muḥtaramah): A protected hand; lawful possession that is inviolable and cannot be taken without compensation.
تَبَعًا (tabaʿan): Following, subservient to; here meaning minor children follow the status of their father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what happens to the wife of a harbi who converts in Dar al-Harb and leaves, then the territory is conquered?
A) She becomes free and Muslim like her husband.
B) She remains a harbi and becomes spoils of war.
C) She becomes a dhimmi.
D) She is given the choice to convert.

Key Takeaway
A harbi convert's minor children become free Muslims following him; his wife and adult children remain harbis; property in a protected hand remains his, while property in a harbi's hand becomes booty.

Killing a Muslim Convert in Dar al-Harb: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Liability
Inter-madhhab dispute on liability for killing a new Muslim in Dar al-Harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between sin-making and compensable inviolability to determine liability for killing a Muslim convert in Dar al-Harb.

Core Idea
Muslim blood is inviolable but compensable only in Dar al-Islam.

This passage addresses a classic disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The scenario: a harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory) converts to Islam while staying in Dar al-Harb. A Muslim kills him, either intentionally or accidentally. The Hanafi ruling is that no qisas (retaliation) or diyah (blood money) is owed; only kaffarah (expiation) is required for accidental killing. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that Islam confers full inviolability, so qisas or diyah are due. The Hanafi position hinges on a distinction between two types of inviolability and a specific interpretation of Quran 4:92.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: no diyah or qisas; only kaffarah for accidental killing. Note the conditions: the convert remains in Dar al-Harb and has Muslim heirs there.
The ruling applies regardless of intention (amdan or khata'an).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that diyah and qisas are obligatory because the victim is a Muslim, and Islam alone creates inviolability (ismah).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i's evidence: Islam is the highest inviolability-maker; every Muslim's blood is protected regardless of location. He does not distinguish between sin-making and compensable inviolability.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response relies on two proofs: (1) Quran 4:92, which only requires freeing a slave (interpreted as exclusive via the particle fa), (2) a distinction between sin-making inviolability (exists in every human due to capacity for taklif) and compensable inviolability (requires secure possession in Dar al-Islam, analogous to property).
The companion of disbelievers (the convert being among hostile people) negates compensability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: under Hanafi, a killer pays no diyah and faces no qisas; under Shafi'i, he pays diyah or faces qisas. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

وَإِذَا أَسْلَمَ الْحَرْبِيُّ فِي دَارِ الْحَرْبِ فَقَتَلَهُ مُسْلِمٌ عَمْدًا أَوْ خَطَأً وَلَهُ وَرَثَةٌ مُسْلِمُونَ هُنَالِكَ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا الْكَفَّارَةُ فِي الْخَطَإِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ تَجِبُ الدِّيَةُ فِي الْخَطَإِ وَالْقِصَاصُ فِي الْعَمْدِ لِأَنَّهُ أَرَاقَ دَمًا مَعْصُومًا لِوُجُودِ الْعَاصِمِ وَهُوَ الْإِسْلَامُ لِكَوْنِهِ مُسْتَجْلِبًا لِلْكَرَامَةِ [؟] وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الْعِصْمَةَ أَصْلُهَا الْمُؤْثِمَةُ لِحُصُولِ أَصْلِ الزَّجْرِ [؟] وَهِيَ ثَابِتَةٌ إِجْمَاعًا وَالْمُقَوَّمَةُ كَمَالٌ فِيهِ لِكَمَالِ الِامْتِنَاعِ بِهِ فَيَكُونُ وَصْفًا فِيهِ فَيَتَعَلَّقُ بِمَا عَلِقَ بِهِ الْأَصْلُ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى {فَإِنْ كَانَ مِنْ قَوْمٍ عَدُوٍّ لَكُمْ وَهُوَ مُؤْمِنٌ فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ} الْآيَةَ جَعَلَ التَّحْرِيرَ كُلَّ الْمُوجَبِ رُجُوعًا إِلَى حَرْفِ الْفَاءِ أَوْ إِلَى كَوْنِهِ كُلَّ الْمَذْكُورِ فَيَنْتَفِي غَيْرُهُ وَلِأَنَّ الْعِصْمَةَ الْمُؤْثِمَةَ بِالْأَدَمِيَّةِ لِأَنَّ الْأَدَمِيَّ خُلِقَ مُتَحَمِّلًا أَعْبَاءَ التَّكْلِيفِ وَالْقِيَامَ بِهَا بِحُرْمَةِ التَّعَرُّضِ وَالْأَمْوَالُ تَابِعَةٌ لَهَا أَمَّا الْمُقَوَّمَةُ فَالْأَصْلُ فِيهَا الْأَمْوَالُ لِأَنَّ التَّقَوُّمَ يُؤْذِنُ بِخَيْرِ الْفَائِتِ وَذَلِكَ فِي الْأَمْوَالِ دُونَ النُّفُوسِ لِأَنَّ مِنْ شَرْطِهِ التَّمَاثُلَ وَهُوَ فِي الْمَالِ دُونَ النَّفْسِ فَكَانَتِ النُّفُوسُ تَابِعَةً ثُمَّ الْعِصْمَةُ الْمُقَوَّمَةُ فِي الْأَمْوَالِ بِالْإِحْرَازِ بِالدَّارِ لِأَنَّ الْعِزَّةَ بِالْمَنْعَةِ فَكَذَلِكَ فِي النُّفُوسِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الشَّارِعَ أَسْقَطَ اعْتِبَارَ مَعِيَّةِ الْكَفَرَةِ لِمَا أَنَّهُ أَوْجَبَ إِبْطَالَهَا وَالْمُرْتَدُّ وَالْمُسْتَأْمِنُ فِي دَارِنَا أَهْلُ دَارِهِمْ حُكْمًا لِقَصْدِهِمَا الِانْتِقَالَ إِلَيْهَا
And if the harbi accepted Islam in Dar al-Harb, then a Muslim killed him intentionally or accidentally, and he has Muslim heirs there, then nothing is owed upon him (the killer) except the expiation in (the case of) accident. Al-Shafi'i said: Diyah is obligatory in accident and qisas in intention, because he shed inviolable blood due to the existence of the inviolability-maker, which is Islam, because it brings honor. And this is because inviolability fundamentally [has two aspects]: the sin-making inviolability is established by consensus, and the compensable inviolability is perfection in it, due to the perfection of prevention by it, so it becomes a quality in it and attaches to what the original attaches to. Our proof is His statement exalted: {But if he was from a people hostile to you and he is a believer, then freeing a believing slave} the verse; He made freeing the entire obligation, by reference to the particle fa or to its being all that is mentioned, so other than it is negated. And because the sin-making inviolability is due to humanity, because the human was created bearing the burdens of obligation and fulfilling them with the inviolability of being harmed, and property is subsidiary to it. As for the compensable inviolability, the origin of it is property, because being compensable indicates a lost good, and that is in property not in lives, because one of its conditions is equivalence, and that is in property not in the self, so the self is subsidiary. Then the compensable inviolability in property is by secure possession in the abode, because honor is by defense, and similarly in selves, except that the Lawgiver dropped consideration of the company of disbelievers because He obligated its nullification. And the apostate and the musta'min in our abode are, in ruling, people of their abode, due to their intention to transfer to it.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi ruling: a Muslim who kills a harbi who converted to Islam while still in Dar al-Harb (before reaching Dar al-Islam) owes no qisas (retaliation) for intentional killing and no diyah (blood money) for accidental killing; only kaffarah (expiation) is required for accidental killing. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since the victim is a Muslim, his blood is inviolable (ma'sum), so qisas applies for intentional killing and diyah for accidental killing, regardless of location. The Hanafi response relies on two proofs. First, Quran 4:92: Allah says if the slain believer is from a hostile people (i.e., in Dar al-Harb), the only obligation is freeing a slave. The Hanafi usul interpretation: the particle fa indicates exclusivity, so no other compensation like diyah is due. Second, they distinguish between two types of inviolability (ismah): the sin-making inviolability (al-ismah al-mu'thimah) which makes killing a sin, is based on humanity and the capacity for taklif (legal responsibility). This exists in every human, including the convert, and is established by consensus. The compensable inviolability (al-ismah al-muqawwamah) which makes the life compensable like property, is derived from property law. Property is compensable when it is securely possessed (ihraz) in a protected abode (Dar al-Islam). By analogy, a human life is compensable only when the person's life is secured by being in Dar al-Islam. Since the convert is in Dar al-Harb, his life lacks this secure possession, so no diyah. The passage ends with a note that an apostate (murtad) or musta'min (non-Muslim with safe conduct) in Dar al-Islam are considered people of their abode (i.e., Dar al-Harb) in terms of some rulings, because they intend to return.

Key Terms
عصمة مؤثمة (ʿiṣmah muʾthimah): Inviolability that makes killing a sin; based on humanity and capacity for taklif.
عصمة مقومة (ʿiṣmah muqawwamah): Inviolability that makes life compensable (with diyah); derived from property law and requires secure possession in Dar al-Islam.
مستأمن (mustaʾmin): A non-Muslim who is given temporary safe conduct (aman) to enter Dar al-Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for not requiring diyah when a Muslim kills another Muslim who converted in Dar al-Harb?
A) Hadith stating no diyah for converts.
B) Quran verse 4:92, which only mentions freeing a slave.
C) Consensus of the Companions.
D) Analogy to killing a warrior in battle.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between sin-making and compensable inviolability; compensability requires secure possession in Dar al-Islam.

Classification of Conquered Land: Kharaj vs Ushr by Irrigation
Ruling on classification of conquered land as kharaji or ushri based on irrigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify conquered land as kharaji or ushri based on its irrigation source, applying the Hanafi ruling from Al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Core Idea
Irrigation source determines tax status: river water = kharaj, well/spring = ushr.

When land is conquered by force (عنوة), the default ruling in the Hanafi school is that it becomes kharaji land, subject to a fixed land tax. However, a critical exception exists: if the land is irrigated by wells or springs rather than rivers, it is classified as ushri, meaning a tithe on produce applies. This distinction, rooted in the text of Al-Jami' al-Saghir, ties the tax directly to the water source that nurtures the crop. Understanding this ruling is essential for determining the legal financial obligations on agricultural lands in the context of Islamic conquest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: the classification of land conquered by force (anwah) as either kharaji (subject to kharaj tax) or ushri (subject to ushr tithe). The passage states the general rule and an exception based on irrigation.
The default for conquered land left to its inhabitants is kharaji.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is cited from Al-Jami' al-Saghir, a foundational Hanafi text. The Arabic text is quoted: 'Every land conquered by force, if river water reaches it, it is kharaji; if river water does not reach it and a spring is extracted, it is ushri.'
This is a transmission (riwayah) from the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The proof establishes a direct causal link between the type of irrigation and the legal classification. River water (natural, requiring no effort) leads to kharaj; well/spring water (extracted with effort) leads to ushr. The reasoning is that ushr is tied to natural growth aided by water sources that do not require artificial irrigation.
The conditional phrasing in the proof is clear and binding.
4
Note the exception and its basis
Makkah is an exception: the Prophet conquered it by force but did not impose kharaj. This is a special case based on the Prophet's own practice and is not generalized.
No other exceptions are mentioned in this passage.
5
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a hypothetical conquered land, determine its classification: if it is irrigated by a river, it is kharaji; if by a well or spring, it is ushri. The default for conquered land is kharaji unless the irrigation source proves otherwise.
The burden of proof lies in establishing the water source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير وَتَرَكَهَا لِأَهْلِهَا وَلَمْ يُوْظِفِ الْخَرَاجَ اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بداری جلد بشتم ترجمه وَكُلُّ أَرْضِ فَيَحَتْ عَنوةً .. الخ اور دوز میں جو قبر اور غلبہ سے فتح کی گئی پھر وہاں کے باشندے ہی وہاں باقی رکئے گئے تو وہ خراجی زمین ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر ان لوگوں سے صلح کر لی گئی ہو تو بھی وہ زمین خرابی ہوگی۔ کیونکہ سب سے پہلے وہاں کا فر پر ہی لگان مقرر کرنے کی ضرورت پیش آئی ہے۔ اور کافر کے ساتھ خراج ہی زیادہ مناسب ہے۔ اور ایسی زمینوں سے مکہ مکرمہ کو خاص کر لیا گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ رسول اللہ نے مکہ مکرمہ کو اپنی طاقت سے فتح کر کے وہاں کے لوگوں کو ان کی جگہ پر ہی باقی رکھا۔ اور ان پر خراج مقرر نہیں کیا۔ وہ زمین جو قہر اور طاقت سے حاصل کی گئی اور نہروں کے پانی سے سینچی گئی وہ خراجی ہے وَفِى الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيْرِ كُلُّ أَرْضِ فُتِحَتْ عَنْوَةً فَوَصَلَ إِلَيْهَامَاءُ الْأَنْهَارِ فَهِيَ أَرْضُ خَرَاجِ وَمَالَمْ يَصِلُّ إِلَيْهَامَاءُ الْأَنْهَارِ وَ اسْتَخْرِجَ مِنْهَا عَيْنَّ فَهِيَ أَرْضُ عُشْرِ لِأَنَّ الْعُشْرَ يَتَعَلَّمُ بِالْأَرْضِ النَّاتِيَةِ وَنَمَاؤُهَا بِمَائِهَا فَيُعْتَبَرُ السَّفْى بِمَاءِ الْعُشْرِ أَوْ بِمَاءِ الْخَرَاجِ ترجمہ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ جو زمین قہر اور طاقت سے فتح کی گئی ہو پھر اس زمین میں نہروں کا پانی پہنچا تو وہ زمین خراجی ہے اور جس میں نہروں کا پانی نہیں پہنچا بلکہ وہیں کوئی چشمہ یا کنواں نکالا گیا تو وہ زمین عشری ہے۔ کیونکہ عشری کا تعلق زمین کی پیداوار سے ہوتا ہے اور اس کی پیداوار پانی سے ہوتی ہے لہذا اعتبار عشری پانی یا خراجی پانی سے سیراب کرنے پر موقوف ہو گا۔ یعنی جیسے پانی سے اس کی سیرابی ہوگی اس کا حکم دیا جائے گا۔
Book of Siyar: And he left it for its people and did not impose kharaj. Translation: Every land conquered by force and then its inhabitants remained, it is kharaji land. Similarly, if peace was made with them, it is also kharaji. Because first the need for tax on the disbeliever arose, and kharaj is more appropriate for them. Makkah is an exception; the Prophet conquered it by force and left the people without imposing kharaj. Land conquered by force and irrigated by river water is kharaji. In Al-Jami' al-Saghir: Every land conquered by force, if river water reaches it, it is kharaji land; if river water does not reach it and a spring is extracted from it, then it is ushri land, because ushr is connected to the land's produce, and its growth is by its water, so irrigation is considered by ushr water or kharaj water.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on lands conquered by force (عنوة) in the Hanafi school. The default is such land is kharaji (subject to land tax) when the original inhabitants are left in place. However, Makkah is an exception due to the Prophet's special treatment. The key proof is from Al-Jami' al-Saghir, a core text of Zahir al-Riwayah, which distinguishes between lands irrigated by rivers (kharaji) and those irrigated by wells/springs (ushri). The reasoning is that ushr is tied to natural produce aided by water sources not requiring artificial effort. The translation elaborates in Urdu, clarifying that the ruling depends on the water source for irrigation.

Key Terms
عنوة (anwah): Conquest by force, without peaceful treaty.
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on non-Muslims or conquered lands.
عشر (ushr): Tithe (10% or 5%) on agricultural produce from Muslim-owned land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to land conquered by force if it is irrigated by a well?
A) It remains kharaji regardless.
B) It becomes ushri.
C) It becomes tax-free.
D) The imam must decide.

Key Takeaway
Irrigation source is the decisive factor: river water → kharaj, well/spring water → ushr.

Abu Yusuf on Classification of Revived Dead Land by Proximity
Ruling on tax classification of revived dead land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Yusuf's rule for classifying revived dead land and apply the exception of Basra due to ijma.

Core Idea
Revived dead land takes the tax status of its adjacent land, except where Sahaba's consensus overrides.

How is revived dead land classified for tax purposes? Abu Yusuf introduces a proximity-based rule, but the famous case of Basra shows that consensus of the Companions can set aside analogy. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the passage and note that Abu Yusuf makes the classification of revived dead land dependent on the type of land it is near—kharaji or ushri.
The rule is about the tax obligation after revival, not about ownership.
2
Understand the analogy (qiyas) used
The author compares the surrounding land to the courtyard (fina') of a house—the periphery takes the ruling of the center.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy).
3
Recognize the exception: Basra
Although qiyas would make Basra kharaji (being near kharaji land), the Companions unanimously imposed ushr, creating a binding consensus that overrides qiyas.
Ijma of Sahaba is a primary source in Hanafi usul.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school
This is Abu Yusuf's view; other early Hanafi authorities (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) may have different criteria. The text does not mention them, but the dispute is known.
Later Hanafi fatwa often relies on the Zahir al-Riwayah, which may consider the potential of the land itself.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a piece of dead land revived near a known ushri village, state its classification and tax. If near a kharaji district, state the opposite.
Basra remains an exception due to historical consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ احْيا أَرْضًا مَوَاتًا فَهِيَ عِنْدَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ مُعْتَبَرَةُ بِخَيْرِهَا فَإِنْ كَانَتْ مِنْ حَيْزِ أَرْضِ الْخَرَاجِ وَمَعْنَاهُ بِقَرُبِهِ فَهِيَ خَرَاحِيَّةُ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ مِنْ خَيْرِ أَرْضِ الْعُشْرِفَهِيَ عُشْرِيَّةُ وَالْبَصْرَةُ . يَة وَالبَصْرَة عِندَهُ كُلُّها عُشْرِيَّةِ بِإِجْمَاعَ الصَّحَابَةِ لِأَنَّ خَيْرَ الشَّئُ يُعْطَى لَهُ حُكْمُهُ كَفَنَاءِ الدَّارِ يُعْطَى لَهُ حُكْمُ الدَّارِ حَتَّى يَجُوزُ لِصَاحِبِهَا الْاِنْتِفَاعُ بِهِ وَكَذَا لَا يَجُورُ أَحَدٌ مَاقَرُبَ مِنَ الْعَامِرِ وَكَانَ الْقِيَاسُ فِى الْبَصْرَةِ أَنْ تَكُونَ خَرَاحِيَّةً لِأَنَّهَا مِنْ حَيْزُ أَرْضِ الْخَرَاجِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ وَظَفُوا عَلَيْهَا الْعُشْرَ فَتَرِكَ الْقِيَاسُ لِإِجْمَاعِهِمْ ترجمہ اور جس نے کسی مردہ زمین کو زندہ کیا ۔ یعنی جنگل کی غیر مزروعہ زمین (غیر آباد ) کو مزروعہ ( آباد ) کیا تو امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک اس کا محل وقوع ( کہ کیسی جگہ میں ہے) دیکھا جائے گا۔ کہ اگر وہ زمین خرابی زمین کے قریب ہو تو وہ زمین بھی خراجی زمین ہوگی اور اگر عشری زمین کے قریب ہو تو وہ بھی عشری زمین ہوگی۔ اور ابو یوسف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک بصرہ کی زمین سب عشری ہے کیونکہ صحابہ کرام کا اس پر اجماع ہے ۔ رواہ ابن عبد البر ۔ کیونکہ جو پیر جس موقع پر ہو اسی کا حکم پاتی ہے۔ جیسے کہ فناء دار کو اس دار کا حکم دیا جاتا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس دار کے مالک کو فناء دار سے فائدہ اٹھانے کی پوری اجازت ہوتی ہے۔ اسی طرح آبادی کے قریب جو زمین ہوتی ہے اس کو لینا جائز نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ بصرہ کے بارے میں ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک قیاس کا تقاضا یہ تھا کہ وہ بھی خراجی ہو کیونکہ وہ خراجی زمین کے قریب ہے۔ لیکن صحابہ کرام نے اس پر عشر مقرر کیا تھا ان کے اس اجتماع کی وجہ سے قیاس کو چھوڑ چھپڑا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے بنجر زمین کو قابل کاشت کیا تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک قرب وجوار کے مطابق اس پر حکم نافذ کیا جائے گا۔ یعنی اگر قرب و جوار کی زمینیں عشری ہوں تو بنجر سے قابل کاشت ہونے والی زمین پر بھی عشری زمین کا اطلاق ہوگا۔ اگر آس پاس کی اراضی خراجی ہو تو پہلے غیر آباد بعد ازاں قابل کاشت زمین خراجیہ متصور ہوگی۔ جاننا چاہئے کہ مذکورہ زیر بحث مسئلہ میں پانچ امور کو واضح کیا گیا ہے۔ - ارض موات، ۲۔ ارض موات کا عشری و خراجی ہونے کا حکم، ۳۔ بصرہ کی اراضی کا حکم ۴- اجماع صحابہ ۵- قیاس
He said: Whoever revives dead land, according to Abu Yusuf, it is considered by its best [proximity]: if it is from the sphere of kharaji land, meaning near it, then it is kharaji; if from the sphere of ushri land, then it is ushri. And Basra, in his view, is entirely ushri by consensus of the Companions. Because a thing's periphery takes its ruling, like the courtyard of a house takes the ruling of the house, so its owner may benefit from it, and similarly no one may take what is near inhabited land. Qiyas would require Basra to be kharaji because it is in the sphere of kharaji land, but the Companions imposed ushr on it, so qiyas is abandoned due to their consensus.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage presents Abu Yusuf's opinion on dead land (ard mawat) revival. He rules that revived land takes the classification (kharaji or ushri) of the adjacent land. The analogy is the courtyard (fina) of a house—it follows the house's ruling. The case of Basra is an exception: although by qiyas it should be kharaji (being near kharaji territory), the Companions (Sahaba) agreed to impose ushr, creating a binding consensus (ijma) that overrides qiyas. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that ijma can supersede analogical reasoning. The Urdu commentary further explains the five issues addressed: dead land definition, its classification, Basra's land, ijma of Sahaba, and qiyas.

Key Terms
أرض موات (ard mawat): Dead, unowned, barren land that is not property of anyone and not adjacent to habitation.
إحياء الموات (ihya' al-mawat): Reviving dead land by making it cultivable, e.g., plowing, irrigating.
إجماع الصحابة (ijma' al-sahabah): Consensus of the Prophet's Companions, a binding legal proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Imam Abu Yusuf rule that Basra is ushri land despite qiyas suggesting it should be kharaji?
A) Because the people of Basra were Muslims
B) Because the Companions (Sahaba) agreed to impose ushr on it, forming an ijma
C) Because Basra is far from any kharaji land
D) Because the Prophet explicitly declared it ushri

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf's rule links revived land classification to proximity, but the Basra example shows ijma al-Sahabah can override qiyas—a key Hanafi usul principle.

Defining Dead Land (Ard Mawat): The Hanafi Criterion
Defines ard mawat and classifies barren lands into three types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of ard mawat according to Zahir al-Riwayah and explain how it differs from the definitions of Imam Tahawi and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Dead land in Hanafi law is unowned, non-beneficial land; distance from habitation is not required by the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah.

In Islamic law, the concept of 'dead land' (ard mawat) determines which unowned lands can be brought to life (ihya) and owned. This lesson unpacks its definition as transmitted in the core Hanafi texts, clarifying what makes a land 'dead' and the different views within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the lexical meaning
Find the Urdu and Arabic lexical definitions of ard mawat in the passage. Note the terms used.
Urdu: 'غیر آباد اور بنجر زمین' (uninhabited, barren). Arabic: 'أرض موات'.
2
Extract the Zahir al-Riwayah definition
Locate the definition attributed to Zahir al-Riwayah. List the three conditions mentioned.
Conditions: (1) not owned, (2) no specific right, (3) not beneficial.
3
Compare with other definitions
Note the definitions of Imam Tahawi and Imam Abu Yusuf. Identify the additional condition they include.
Both include a distance condition (near habitation or hearing range).
4
Recognize the authoritative view
See what the author of Bada'i' al-Sana'i' says about the correct view.
The correct view is Zahir al-Riwayah, which does not require distance.
5
Classify the three types
From the latter part, identify the three categories of barren land mentioned.
Permanently uncultivable, abandoned, khalisah (state-owned).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ارض موات اردو زبان میں غیر آباد اور بنجر زمین کہا جاتا ہے۔ اور عربی زبان میں ارض موات کہتے ہیں۔ ارض موات ( غیر آباد، بنجر زمین ) کو ارض خالصہ بھی کہتے ہیں۔ ظاہر روایت کے مطابق ارض موات ایسی زمین کو کہا جاتا ہے جو کسی کی ملکیت نہ ہو۔ نہ ہی کسی کا مخصوص حق ہو۔ قابل منفعت نہ ہو۔ امام طحاوی کے نزدیک ارض موات ایسی زمین کو کہتے ہیں جو آبادی کے قریب نہ ہو۔ امام ابو یوسف کا قول ہے کہ ارض موات پر زمین کے ایسے قطعہ کا متفق ہوتا ہے۔ جو آبادی سے اتنا دور ہو کہ بلند آواز سے پکارنے سے آواز سنائی نہ دے۔ ظاہر روایت میں امام طحاوی ، امام ابو یوسف کے موقف کی شرط نہیں ہے۔ ظاہر روایت کے اعتبار سے وہ زمین جو سمندر کے ہٹ جانے سے خالی ہو جائے تو وہ بھی ارض موات کا حکم رکھتی ہے۔ قطع نظر اس سے کہ وہ ( ارض موات ) شہر کے قریب ہو یا دور غیر مملوکہ بڑا جنگل بھی ارض موات کے زمرے میں آتا ہے۔ بقول صاحب بدائع الصنائع صحیح قول ظاہر روایت کا ہے۔ روایات و احادیث کی رو سے بنجر و غیر آباد اراضی کی تین اقسام ہیں۔ ا۔ دائمی طور پر نا قابل کاشت اراضی ۲ افتاده زمین ۳۔ خالصہ زمین چنانچہ ان تینوں اقسام کی اراضی کی تفصیل ملاحظہ ہو۔ وباللہ التوفیق -دائمی نا قابل کاشت زمین ایسی بنجر زمین جو ہمیشہ سے غیر آباد چلی آرہی ہو اور اس کی ویرانی دوستی کے پیش نظر عام لوگ اسے قابل کاشت کرنے سے گھبراتے اور پہلو تہی کرتے ہوں نقیع میں حضرت زبیر گو ایسی ہی زمین دی گئی تھی۔ ۲ افتاده زمین و د زمین جو کاشت کے قابل ہونے کے باوجود اس میں کسی وجہ سے نا قابل کاشت ہو ۔ مثال کے طور پر ،
Dead land in Urdu is called unhabited and barren land. In Arabic it is called ard mawat. Ard mawat (uninhabited, barren land) is also called ard khalisah. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, ard mawat is land that is not owned by anyone, nor has any specific right, nor is beneficial. According to Imam Tahawi, ard mawat is land not near habitation. Imam Abu Yusuf says ard mawat refers to a plot that is so far from habitation that a loud call cannot be heard. In Zahir al-Riwayah, the condition of Imam Tahawi and Abu Yusuf is not present. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, land that becomes empty after the sea recedes is also ruled as ard mawat, regardless of whether it is near the city or far. A large unowned forest also falls under ard mawat. According to the author of Bada'i' al-Sana'i', the correct saying is of Zahir al-Riwayah. According to traditions and hadiths, barren and uncultivated lands are of three types: 1) Permanently uncultivable land, 2) Abandoned land, 3) Khalisah land. So details of these three types of land may be seen. And with Allah is success. - Permanently uncultivable land: such barren land that has always been unhabited and due to its desolation, people are afraid to cultivate it and avoid it. In Naqi', Hazrat Zubair was given such land. 2) Abandoned land: land that is cultivable but for some reason became uncultivable. For example,
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage provides definitions and classifications of dead land (ard mawat). It begins with a lexical definition, then presents various legal definitions: Zahir al-Riwayah (land unowned, without specific right, non-beneficial), Imam Tahawi's (not near habitation), and Imam Abu Yusuf's (so far that a shout cannot be heard). The author notes that Zahir al-Riwayah does not include the condition of distance, so it includes land like seabeds. The correct view according to Bada'i' al-Sana'i' is that of Zahir al-Riwayah. Then three types of barren land are listed: 1) Permanently uncultivable (e.g., rocky land), 2) Abandoned (land that was cultivable but fell into disuse), and 3) Khalisah (state-owned land). The example of Hazrat Zubair's land in Naqi' is given for the first type. This is a conceptual clarification useful for understanding tax classification and ownership rules.

Key Terms
أرض موات (ard mawat): Dead land: unowned, uncultivated, non-beneficial land; includes various types per different scholars.
أرض خالصة (ard khalisah): State-owned land; often synonymous with dead land that has no private owner.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school from Imam Muhammad's six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, which of the following is NOT a condition for land to be considered ard mawat?
A) It is not owned by anyone
B) It is not specifically claimed by anyone
C) It is not beneficial
D) It is far from habitation such that a loud call cannot be heard

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of dead land according to Zahir al-Riwayah relies solely on lack of ownership, right, and benefit, without requiring distance from habitation.

Tax Classification of Revived Dead Land by Water Source
Imam Muhammad's ruling on classification of revived dead land by water source

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for classifying revived dead land as 'ushri or kharaji based on the water source, and apply it to given scenarios.

Core Idea
The tax status of revived dead land depends on the water source, not just the reviver's religion.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents Imam Muhammad's detailed ruling on the classification of revived dead land. While it might seem that any land revived by a Muslim becomes 'ushri, the Hanafi school looks deeper—to the water source. Understanding this distinction is crucial for land tax law in Islamic governance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its classification categories
The act is reviving dead land. The two possible tax statuses are 'ushri (tithe land) and kharaji (land tax land).
2
List water sources leading to 'ushri status
According to Imam Muhammad, 'ushri results if the land is irrigated by a personally dug well, an extracted spring, natural great rivers (Tigris, Euphrates, etc.), or rainwater.
3
List water sources leading to kharaji status
Kharaji results if the land is irrigated by rivers that non-Arabs dug, such as Nahr al-Malik and Nahr Yazdgard.
4
Understand the reasoning (dalil aqli)
Water is the cause of productivity, and kharaj cannot be forcibly imposed on a Muslim initially. Using kharaji water indicates voluntary acceptance of kharaj.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not make this water-based distinction; they classify all revived land by a Muslim as 'ushri regardless of water source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ قَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ إِنْ أَحْيَاهَا بِبِئْرٍ حَفَرَهَا أَوْ بِعَيْنٍ اِسْتَخْرَجَهَا أَوْ بِمَاءِ دِجْلَةَ وَالْفُرَاتِ وَالْأَنْهَارِ الْعِظَامِ الَّتِي لَا يَمْلِكُهَا أَحَدٌ فَهِيَ عُشْرِيَّةٌ وَكَذَا إِنْ أَحْيَاهَا بِمَاءِ السَّمَاءِ وَإِنْ أَحْيَاهَا بِمَاءِ الْأَنْهَارِ الَّتِي احْتَفَرَهَا الْأَعَاجِمُ مِثْلَ نَهْرِ الْمَلِكِ وَ نَهْرِ يَزْدَجِرْد فَهِيَ خَرَاجِيَّةٌ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا مِنَ اعْتِبَارِ الْمَاءِ إِذْ هُوَ السَّبَبُ لِلسَّمَاءِ [؟] وَلِأَنَّهُ لَا يُمْكِنُ تَوْظِيفُ الْخَرَاجِ ابْتِدَاءً عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ كُرْهًا فَيُعْتَبَرُ فِي ذَلِكَ الْمَاءُ لِأَنَّ السَّقْيَ بِمَاءِ الْخَرَاجِ دَلَالَةُ الِالْتِزَامِيَّةِ
And Muhammad said: If he revives it by a well he dug, or by a spring he extracted, or by water of the Tigris, Euphrates, and great rivers that no one owns, then it is 'ushri. Likewise if he revives it by rainwater. And if he revives it by water of rivers that the non-Arabs dug, like Nahr al-Malik and Nahr Yazdgard, then it is kharaji, because of what we mentioned regarding the consideration of water: for it is the cause for [growth?] and because it is not possible to impose kharaj initially on a Muslim by force, so water is considered in that; because irrigating with kharaji water is an indication of commitment.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This is a ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on the classification of revived dead land (ard mawat). The key factor is the water source: if the land is irrigated from a source not owned by any individual (like a personally dug well, spring, rainwater, or natural great rivers like Tigris and Euphrates), it becomes 'ushri land—subject to 'ushr (tithe) if the owner is Muslim. If irrigated from canals dug by non-Muslim rulers (like Nahr al-Malik or Nahr Yazdgard), it becomes kharaji land—subject to kharaj (land tax). The reasoning: water is the cause of productivity, and since kharaj cannot be forcibly imposed on a Muslim initially, using such water indicates voluntary acceptance of kharaj. The commentary adds that if a Muslim buys kharaji land from a non-Muslim, the kharaj remains.

Key Terms
عُشْرِيَّة ('ushriyyah): Land subject to 'ushr (tithe) tax, i.e., one-tenth of produce, typical for Muslim-owned land.
خَرَاجِيَّة (kharajiyyah): Land subject to kharaj (land tax) imposed by the imam, not fixed by shari'ah but by assessment.
أَرْض مَوَات (ard mawat): Dead land not owned by anyone and not under cultivation or habitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, if a Muslim revives dead land by irrigating it from a well he dug on site, what is the land's tax status?
A) It becomes kharaji land.
B) It becomes 'ushri land.
C) It remains dead land with no tax.
D) It becomes mixed 'ushri/kharaji.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the tax classification of revived dead land hinges on whether the irrigation water comes from an ownerless source or from a kharaji-operated canal.

Kharaj Rates Set by Umar on Sawad Lands: A Hanafi Ruling with Proof of Ijma
Details of Kharaj Rates and Proof by Ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the kharaj rates set by Umar for different types of land and explain why they are considered wajib based on ijma of the Companions.

Core Idea
Umar's kharaj rates became binding law through silent consensus of the Companions.

This passage from al-Hidayah details the specific tax rates imposed by Caliph Umar on the agricultural lands of Sawad (Iraq). It provides both the amounts for different crops and the reasoning behind the differentiation. More importantly, the passage argues that these rates are not merely historical but legally binding because they were enacted in the presence of the Companions without objection, constituting ijma.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific kharaj rates
Locate the passage that states the tax for each land type: irrigated grain (1 qafiz + 1 dirham per jarib), vegetables (5 dirhams), continuous vineyards and date palms (10 dirhams). Note the units.
Rates are given per jarib, a land area unit.
2
Examine the chain of transmission
The passage mentions that Umar sent Uthman ibn Hunayf to survey the Sawad, with Hudhayfah as supervisor. The survey resulted in 36 million jarib. This provides the factual basis for the rates.
The survey was to measure the land for tax assessment.
3
Understand the legal argument of ijma
The passage states that Umar's action was done in the presence of the Companions without any objection, thus forming a tacit ijma (ijma sukuti). In Hanafi usul, such silence is considered a valid form of consensus, making the ruling binding.
The Arabic phrase 'min ghayri nakir' (without objection) is key.
4
Analyze the rationale for varying rates
The passage explains that expenses vary: vineyards have the least maintenance, farms have the most, vegetables are in between. Therefore, the tax is adjusted accordingly: highest for vineyards, lowest for farms, medium for vegetables. This shows the ruling is based on a clear ratio legis (ta'lil).
The rationale allows for adjustment if expenses change.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab disagreement
The Hanafi school considers kharaj a fixed tax on land based on ijma. The Shafi'i school views it as a type of jizyah on land, thus not a fixed per-area tax. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
Understanding this helps appreciate the diversity within Sunni fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَالْخَرَاجُ الَّذِى وَضَعَهُ عُمَرُ عَلى أَهْلِ السَّوَادِ مِنْ كُلِّ جَرِيبٍ يَبْلُغُهُ الْمَاءُ قَفِيزٌ هَاشِمِيٌّ وَهُوَ الصَّاعُ وَدِرْهَمٌ وَمِنْ جَرِيبِ الرَّطْبَةِ خَمْسَةُ دَرَاهِمَ وَمِنْ جَرِيبِ الْكَرَمِ الْمُتَّصِلِ وَالنَّخِيلِ الْمُتَّصِلِ عَشَرَةُ دَرَاهِمَ وَهَذَا هُوَ الْمَنْقُولُ عَنْ عُمَرَ فَإِنَّهُ بَعَثَ عُثْمَانَ بْنَ حُنَيْفٍ حَتَّى يَمْسَحَ سَوَادَ الْعِرَاقِ وَجَعَلَ حُذَيْفَةَ مُشْرِفًا فَمَسَحَ فَبَلَغَ سِتَّةً وَثَلَاثِينَ أَلْفَ أَلْفِ جَرِيبٍ وَوَضَعَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ مَا قُلْنَا وَكَانَ بِمَحْضَرٍ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ نَكِيرٍ فَكَانَ إِجْمَاعًا مِنْهُمْ وَلِأَنَّ الْمُؤَنَ مُتَفَاوِتَةٌ فَالْكَرْمُ أَخَفُّهَا مَئُونَةً وَالْمَزَارِعُ أَكْثَرُهَا مَئُونَةً وَالرِّطَابُ بَيْنَهُمَا وَالْوَظِيفَةُ تَتَفَاوَتُ بِتَفَاوُتِهَا فَجُعِلَ الْوَاجِبُ فِي الْكَرِمِ أَعْلَاهَا وَفِي الزَّرْعِ أَدْنَاهَا وَفِي الرِّطْبَةِ أَوْسَطَهَا
He said: The kharaj that Umar placed on the people of Sawad: for every jarib that reaches water, a qafiz Hashimi (which is a sa') and a dirham; for a jarib of ratbah (vegetables), five dirhams; for a jarib of continuous vineyards and continuous date palms, ten dirhams. This is what is transmitted from Umar, for he sent Uthman ibn Hunayf to survey the Sawad of Iraq, and made Hudhayfah as supervisor, so they surveyed and it reached thirty-six million jarib. And he placed on that what we said, and that was in the presence of the Companions without any objection, so it was a consensus (ijma) from them. And because expenses vary: vineyards are the lightest in expense, farms are the most expensive, and vegetables are between them. And the tax varies with their variation, so the obligatory was made highest in vineyards, lowest in crops, and medium in vegetables.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage reports the kharaj rates set by Caliph Umar for the Sawad of Iraq. The rates are based on the type of cultivation: irrigated land producing grain: 1 qafiz (about 2.5 liters) of produce plus 1 dirham per jarib (a land measure). Vegetables: 5 dirhams per jarib. Continuous vineyards or date palms: 10 dirhams per jarib. This was determined by surveying the land, supervised by Uthman ibn Hunayf and Hudhayfah, leading to 36 million jarib. The Companions present did not object, forming ijma. The rationale is differing expenses: vineyards require less ongoing effort, so higher tax; farms require more effort, so lower tax; vegetables are intermediate. This ruling is part of the Hanafi reliance on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs as a source of law.

Key Terms
جَرِيب (jarib): A unit of land area, approximately 60 cubits by 60 cubits, varying by region.
قَفِيز (qafiz): A measure of volume for grain, approximately 2.5 liters. 'Hashimi' refers to the measure used by the Banu Hashim.
سَوَاد (sawad): The fertile agricultural region of Iraq around Kufa and Basra.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the kharaj per jarib for continuous vineyards according to Umar's settlement?
A) 1 qafiz and 1 dirham
B) 5 dirhams
C) 10 dirhams
D) Half the produce

Key Takeaway
Umar's kharaj rates are binding in Hanafi fiqh due to tacit ijma of the Companions, but the underlying rationale of varying expenses allows for adjustment.

Kharaj for Other Crops: Capacity (Taqah) as Standard
Rule for assessing kharaj on other crops not fixed by Umar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of taqah (capacity) to assess kharaj on crops not fixed by Umar, and state the maximum limit of half the produce.

Core Idea
For crops not fixed by Umar, kharaj is assessed by capacity (taqah) with a ceiling of half the produce.

Kharaj, the land tax on conquered lands, was set by Caliph Umar for certain crops like grain and vineyards. But what about crops like saffron or mixed gardens? Hanafi scholars extend Umar’s method by analogy (qiyas): the tax must be based on the land’s capacity to pay, ensuring justice and preventing hardship. This lesson explains the principle, its proof, and its application to diverse agricultural produce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is imposing kharaj on crops not specifically assessed by Umar (e.g., saffron, bustan). The ruling: wajib (obligatory) but amount is flexible, assessed by capacity.
The school establishes that the imam must impose kharaj, but the rate is not fixed.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is qiyas on Umar’s practice. Umar fixed rates for certain crops based on their capacity (taqah). For other crops, we analogize: they also have capacity, so the same principle applies.
The asl is Umar’s assessment; the illa is consideration of capacity.
3
Trace the Limit (Half of Produce)
The scholars state the maximum kharaj is half the produce. This is based on justice: the land could have been divided among the Muslim fighters, so taking more than half would be unjust.
This is a qat'i limit: la yuzadu alayh (not increased beyond).
4
Define Bustan (Mixed Garden)
Bustan is defined as any walled land with scattered date palms and trees. Its kharaj is assessed by capacity, not by a fixed amount per area.
Distinguish from a continuous vineyard (karm muttasil) which may have a different rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْأَصْنَافِ كَالزَّعْفَرَانِ وَالْبُسْتَانِ وَغَيْرِهِ يُوضَعُ عَلَيْهَا بِحَسْبِ الطَّاقَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ فِيهِ تَوْظِيفُ عُمَرَ وَقَدِ اعْتَبَرَ الطَّاقَةَ فِي ذَلِكَ فَتَعْتَبِرُهَا فِيمَا لَا تَوْظِيفَ فِيهِ. قَالُوا وَنِهَايَةُ الطَّاقَةِ أَنْ تَبْلُغَ الْوَاجِبُ نِصْفَ الْخَارِجِ لَا يُزَادُ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ النِّصْفَ عَيْنُ الْإِنْصَافِ لِمَا كَانَ لَنَا أَنْ نُقَسِّمَ الْكُلَّ بَيْنَ الْعَالِمِينَ. وَالْبُسْتَانُ كُلُّ أَرْضٍ يَحُوطُهَا حَائِطٌ وَفِيهَا نَخِيلٌ مُتَفَرِّقَةٌ وَأَشْجَارٌ [أَخْلَاطِ؟] فِي دِيَارِنَا وَ [يُوضَعُ] مِنَ الدَّرَاهِمِ فِي الْأَرَاضِي كُلِّهَا وَ [بِحَسَبِ الطَّاقَةِ] كَذَلِكَ لِأَنَّ التَّقْدِيرَ يَجِبُ أَنْ يَكُونَ بِقَدْرِ الطَّاقَةِ مِنْ أَيِّ شَيْءٍ كَانَ.
He said: And other than that from the categories like saffron and garden and others, kharaj is imposed on them according to capacity (taqah), because there is no fixed tax from Umar for them, and he considered capacity in that; so we consider it in what has no fixed tax. They said: The limit of capacity is that the obligatory amount reaches half of the produce, it is not increased beyond that, because half is the essence of justice, because we had the right to divide the whole land among the fighters. And bustan is any land surrounded by a wall and having scattered date palms and trees [mixed?] in our regions, and [is imposed] from dirhams on all lands, and [according to capacity] likewise because the estimation must be according to capacity from whatever it is.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage extends the principle of kharaj to crops that Umar did not specifically assess, such as saffron or mixed gardens (bustan). The imam assesses kharaj based on the land's capacity (taqah), meaning the land's ability to produce. A key limitation: the kharaj cannot exceed half of the produce, a principle derived from the fact that the land could have been divided among the Muslim conquerors. The definition of bustan is given: a walled garden with scattered trees and date palms. In later Hanafi practice, kharaj is often fixed in dirhams per area, but the underlying standard remains capacity.

Key Terms
طَاقَة (taqah): Capacity or ability of the land to bear tax; not a fixed amount but assessed relative to produce.
بُسْتَان (bustan): A walled garden with scattered fruit trees and date palms, not continuous like a vineyard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum kharaj that can be imposed on a bustan (mixed garden) according to this passage?
A) 10 dirhams per jarib
B) 5 dirhams per jarib
C) Half of the produce
D) One-third of the produce

Key Takeaway
Kharaj on unregulated crops is assessed by land capacity (taqah) with a half-produce cap, based on qiyas on Umar's practice.

Adjustment of Kharaj: Reduction and Increase
Intra-Hanafi dispute on adjustment of kharaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reduction and increase of kharaj, explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu Yusuf, and apply the principle of land capacity to taxation.

Core Idea
The imam must reduce kharaj if land cannot bear it; increasing it when produce rises is permissible by qiyas, but Abu Yusuf dissents.

In this lesson, we examine the imam's authority to adjust the land tax (kharaj) in response to changes in agricultural productivity. While reduction is agreed upon, a significant intra-Hanafi dispute arises over whether the imam may also increase the tax when yields improve. By analyzing the proofs of Muhammad al-Shaybani and Abu Yusuf, you will understand how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from precedents of the Companions and analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling
State the ruling on reduction of kharaj when the land cannot bear the tax. Note the consensus (ijma) and the evidence from Caliph Umar's inquiry.
Reduction is wajib (mandatory) on the imam, not discretionary.
2
Locate the disputed issue
Identify the point of ikhtilaf: whether the imam may increase kharaj when produce increases. Recognize that both Abu Hanifa's disciples differ.
The dispute is between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf; Abu Hanifa's own view is not recorded here.
3
Analyze each imam's dalil
For Muhammad: trace the qiyas from reduction to increase, noting the shared 'illa (change in yield). For Abu Yusuf: explain his reliance on Umar's practice as a binding precedent.
Muhammad uses qiyas jali; Abu Yusuf uses istihsan or practice of the Salaf.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: in lands with fixed kharaj per area, the imam may or may not adjust rates when productivity changes. Identify the mufta bihi position.
Later Hanafi authorities prefer Muhammad's view, allowing increase provided it remains within the land's capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ فَإِنْ لَمْ تُطِقْ مَا وُضِعَ عَلَيْهَا نَقَصَهُمُ الْإِمَامُ وَالتَّقْصَانُ عِنْدَ قِلَّةِ الرَّيْعِ جَائِزٌ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ أَلَا تَرَى إِلَى قَوْلِ عُمَرَ لَعَلَّكُمَا حَمَلْتُمَا الْأَرْضَ مَا لَا تُطِيقُ فَقَالَا بَلْ حَمَلْنَاهَا مَا تُطِيقُ وَزِدْنَاهَا لَا طَاقَةَ وَهَذَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى جَوَازِ التَّنْقِيصِ وَأَمَّا الزَّيَادَةُ عِنْدَ زِيَادَةِ الرَّيْعِ فَيَجُوزُ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ اعْتِبَارًا بِالتَّنْقِيصِ وَعِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ لَا يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّ عُمَرَ لَمْ
He said: If it (the land) cannot bear what was imposed on it, the imam reduces for them. And reduction in case of low produce is permissible by consensus (ijma). Do you not see the statement of Umar: 'Perhaps you two have loaded the land with what it cannot bear?' They said: 'No, we loaded it with what it can bear and increased it to its capacity.' And this indicates the permissibility of reduction. As for increase when produce increases: it is permissible according to Muhammad, by analogy with reduction; and according to Abu Yusuf, it is not permissible because Umar did not...
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage addresses the imam's authority to adjust kharaj rates. If land fails to produce enough to bear the tax, the imam must reduce it, a ruling confirmed by ijma. The evidence is Umar's inquiry to his surveyors, which implies that if they had exceeded the land's capacity, he would have reduced it. The dispute is about increasing kharaj when the land becomes more productive: Muhammad al-Shaybani allows it by qiyas on reduction, while Abu Yusuf disallows it, citing Umar's practice (he did not increase). The Urdu commentary states that in their regions (India), kharaj is fixed in dirhams on all lands, but the principle remains that it must be within capacity. The Hanafi position typically follows Muhammad's view on increase, but the cautious approach is to avoid increase to prevent hardship.

Key Terms
تَقْصَان / تَنْقِيص (taqsan / tanqis): Reduction of the kharaj tax by the imam when the land cannot bear it.
زِيَادَة (ziyadah): Increase of kharaj when produce increases; disputed between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.
رَيْع (ray'): Yield or produce of the land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Direct command from the Quran.
B) Consensus (ijma) of the Companions.
C) Analogy (qiyas) with the permissibility of reduction.
D) The practice of Caliph Umar.

Key Takeaway
Reduction of kharaj is wajib by consensus; increase is permissible in Hanafi fiqh by qiyas, with the condition that the land can bear it.
