Reduction of Kharaj When Land Cannot Bear It
Ruling on reducing kharaj when land is unproductive, with proof from 'Umar's practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on reduction of kharaj when land cannot bear it, identify the proof from 'Umar's practice, and apply the condition that triggers the obligation.

Core Idea
When land cannot bear its kharaj, the imam must reduce the tax — by consensus and Caliphal precedent.

This lesson examines a ruling from al-Quduri's matn on land tax (kharaj). The key question: what happens when a land's yield drops so low that paying the fixed tax leaves less than half for the farmer? The Hanafi school, citing consensus and the practice of Caliph 'Umar (ra), holds that the imam is obliged to reduce the tax. We'll unpack the proof and its implications for just governance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reducing kharaj when land cannot bear it. The hukm level is wajib (obligatory) upon the imam, not merely recommended.
The Arabic phrase 'chahiye' (should/ought) in the context of governance indicates obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of Caliph 'Umar (ra) with his officers Hudhayfah and Ibn Hanif, recorded by al-Bukhari.
This is a Sunnah ahad narration.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this narration prove the obligation? 'Umar's questioning implies that overburdening is unacceptable, and the officers' response confirms they only impose what the land can bear. This shows that if the land could not bear it, reduction would be required.
The practice of a Caliph in administrative matters is a proof in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text states this ruling is 'bilā jamā‘' (by consensus), indicating no significant disagreement among the early authorities.
This strengthens the binding nature of the ruling.
5
Evaluate the authority
The ruling comes from al-Quduri's matn, which belongs to Zahir al-Riwayah, and the hadith is from Bukhari. This gives the ruling high authority in the Hanafi school.
The authority_weight is zahir_riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اگر ایسا ہو کہ جو محصول کسی زمین پر لگایا گیا اگر وہ زمین اس کو برداشت نہ کر سکتی ہو یعنی پیداوار سے محصول نکالنے کے بعد نصف سے بھی کم بچتا ہو تو امام کو چاہئے کہ اس محصول کو کم کر دے۔ اور پیداوار کے کم ہونے کی صورت میں محصول کم کر دینا بالا جماع جائز ہے۔ اسی لئے ہم یہ دیکھتے ہیں کہ حضرت عمر نے حضرت حذیفہ وابن حنیف سے فرمایا تھا کہ کہیں ایسا تو تم نے نہیں کیا کہ اتنا محصول مقرر کر دیا ہو جسے وہ زمین برداشت نہ کر سکتی ہو تو انہوں نے جواب دیا کہ ہم نے ایسا ہر گز نہیں کیا ہے ہم نے اتنا ہی لگایا ہے جسے وہ برداشت کر سکتی ہو بلکہ اگر ہم کچھ بھی لگانا چاہتے تو وہ زمین اسے بھی برداشت کر لیتی ۔ ( کیونکہ اس کی پیداوار بہت زیادہ ہے)۔ (رواہ البخاری)
Translation of Quduri (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If the tax that was imposed on a land cannot be borne by that land, i.e., after taking the tax from the produce, less than half remains, then the imam should reduce that tax. And reducing the tax in case of low produce is permissible by consensus. For this reason, we see that 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said to Hudhayfah and Ibn Hanif: 'Have you done such that you set a tax that the land cannot bear?' They replied: 'We have never done such. We have only imposed what it can bear. In fact, if we wanted to impose something, the land would bear it (because its produce is very abundant).' (Narrated by al-Bukhari).
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Quduri’s matn, commented upon by the author. The ruling: if a land’s produce is so low that after paying the kharaj (land tax) less than half remains, the imam must reduce the tax. This is agreed upon by consensus (bilā jamā‘). The proof is the practice of Caliph 'Umar (ra), who checked with his officers to ensure they did not overburden the land. This shows that tax reduction is required when the land cannot bear it. The narration from Bukhari confirms the permissibility and necessity.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on productive land in conquered territories, distinct from 'ushr.
بالا جماع (bilā jamā‘): By consensus of scholars, indicating unanimous agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the landowner requests reduction
B) When after paying kharaj, less than half of the produce remains
C) When the land is fallow for a year
D) When the land produces more than expected

Key Takeaway
When kharaj exceeds half the produce, the imam must reduce it, a ruling established by consensus and Caliphal precedent.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Increasing Kharaj
Dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whether kharaj can be increased if land becomes more productive

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf on increasing kharaj and explain the basis of each view using qiyas and precedent.

Core Idea
Increasing kharaj after assessment is contested: Muhammad allows by analogy, Abu Yusuf prohibits by 'Umar's practice.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute between two of Abu Hanifa's foremost students: Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf. The issue is whether the imam may increase the kharaj (land tax) when the land becomes more productive than initially assessed. This dispute illustrates how different sources of evidence—analogical reasoning versus the practice of a Caliph—can lead to divergent rulings within the same school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State what each imam holds regarding increasing kharaj.
2
Extract each imam's dalil
What proof does Muhammad use? What proof does Abu Yusuf use?
3
Compare the strength of the proofs
Which is based on qiyas (analogy) and which on the practice of 'Umar (amal)?
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does this dispute make?
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which view is ultimately relied upon (mufta bihi) and why?

Source Text

اس گفتگو سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ محصول کم مقرر کرنا بھی صحیح ہے۔ اور یہ بات کہ پیداوار اگر اندازہ سے بہت زیادہ ہو جائے تو محصول کو پڑھانا بھی جائز ہے یا نہیں ۔ تو امام محمد رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک جس طرح مقرر کئے ہوئے محصول کو گھٹانا جائز ہے اسی طرح اسے بڑھا دینا بھی جائز ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک بڑھانا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر کو یہ خبر دی گئی تھی کہ وہ لگائے ہوئے محصول سے بھی زیادہ محصول برداشت کر سکتی ہے پھر بھی آپ نے محصول نہیں بڑھایا۔
From this discussion it also became known that setting a low tax is correct. And regarding the issue of when produce becomes much more than estimated, whether increasing the tax is permissible or not: According to Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), just as it is permissible to decrease the fixed tax, similarly it is permissible to increase it. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), increasing is not permissible, because Caliph 'Umar was informed that the land could bear more than the imposed tax, yet he did not increase it.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between the two major students of Abu Hanifa: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam Abu Yusuf. The issue: if a kharaj land becomes more productive than initially estimated, may the imam increase the tax? Imam Muhammad argues that since reduction is allowed, increase should also be allowed by analogy. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that increase is not allowed, because Caliph 'Umar, upon being told that the land could bear more, refrained from increasing it. This implies that once set, the tax should not be raised even if capacity increases. The passage does not give the ruling of Abu Hanifa himself, but the mufta bihi position is often that of Abu Yusuf due to the practice of 'Umar. The authority weight: this is from the commentary (sharh) of Ashraf al-Hidayah, not the original matn.

Key Terms
بڑھانا (baṛhānā): Increasing the kharaj tax amount after initial assessment.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on increasing kharaj: Imam Muhammad allows it by qiyas, but the mufta bihi is Imam Abu Yusuf's view that it is impermissible due to the practice of Caliph 'Umar.

When Calamity Strikes: Dropping Kharaj
Ruling that kharaj drops if land is flooded, dried, or crops destroyed by calamity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that kharaj drops when the land's productive capacity is lost for a full year due to calamity, and explain the qiyas to zakat that supports it.

Core Idea
Kharaj is tied to the land's potential growth for the whole year; when calamity destroys that potential, the tax drops.

This lesson examines a ruling from al-Hidayah concerning land tax (kharaj) under calamities. You will see how the Hanafi school uses the concept of 'estimated growth' (al-namā' al-taqdīrī) and draws an analogy to zakat to determine when the obligation falls.

Guided Path
1
Identify the calamities and the ruling
Note the three calamities listed: flooding, drought, and pestilence destroying crops. The ruling: no kharaj is due.
2
Understand the basis: potential for cultivation
The reason given is that the ability to cultivate (tamakkun) has ceased. This is the estimated growth (namā' taqdīrī) that kharaj is based on.
Kharaj is not on actual produce but on the land's capacity.
3
Follow the qiyas to zakat
Just as zakat requires wealth to be productive for a full lunar year (hawl), kharaj requires the land to be cultivable for a full year. If the potential is lost mid-year, the obligation drops.
The passage explicitly says 'as in the case of zakat wealth'.
4
Consider the alternative and fatwa nuance
The passage mentions that the ruling could be based on actual harvest at harvest time. Later fatwa notes add that if crops existed for three months, kharaj is not dropped, but the core reasoning stands.
This nuance shows application in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ غَلَب عَلى أَرْضِ الْخَراجِ الْمَاءُ اَوِ انْقَطَعَ الْمَاءُ عَنْهَا  َأوِ اصْطَلَمَ الزَّرْعَ افَةٌ فَلَاخَرَاجَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ فَاتَ التَّمَكُنُ مِنَ الزَّرَاعَةِ وَهُوَ السَّمَاءُ التَّقْدِيرِيُّ الْمُعْتَبَرُ فِي الْحَرَاجِ وَفِيمَا إِذَا اصْطَلَمَ الزَّرْعَ افَةٌ فَاتَ السَّمَاءُ التَّقْدِيرِيُّ فِي بَعْضِ الْحَوْلِ وَكَوْنُهُ نَامِيَّا فِي جَمِيعِ الْحَوْلِ شَرُطٌ كَمَا فِي مَالِ الزَّكوةِ أَوْيُدَارُ الْحُكْمُ عَلَى الحقيقَةِ عِندَ خُروج الخارج
And if water overwhelms a kharaj land, or water is cut off from it, or a pestilence destroys the crop, then there is no kharaj upon it, because the ability to cultivate has ceased, and that is the estimable growth (al-namā' al-taqdīrī) considered in kharaj. And in the case where the crop is destroyed by a pestilence, the estimable growth is lost for part of the year, and its being growing for the entire year is a condition, as in the case of zakat wealth. Or the ruling is based on the actual (growth) at the time of harvest.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that if a kharaj land suffers from flooding, drought, or crop destruction by pestilence, the kharaj is dropped. The reason: kharaj is imposed on the land's capacity for growth (namā' taqdīrī – potential produce). If that potential is lost due to calamity, the obligation falls. The proof is an analogy (qiyas) to zakat: just as zakat requires the wealth to be productive for a full lunar year, kharaj requires the land to be capable of cultivation for the full year. If a calamity occurs, the potential is lost, so the tax lapses. Alternatively, the ruling may be based on actual produce at harvest time. The fatwa later mentioned in the commentary states that if the crop exists for even three months, kharaj is not dropped, but the legal reasoning remains as given.

Key Terms
النماء التقديري (al-namā' al-taqdīrī): The estimated potential growth of the land; the capacity to produce crops, which is the basis of kharaj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is kharaj dropped when water overwhelms the land?
A) Because the land is flooded permanently
B) Because the ability to cultivate ceases
C) Because the government waives it
D) Because the landowner becomes poor

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is waived when the land's productive potential is absent for the entire year, by analogy to the zakat condition of a full year's growth.

Kharaj Obligation if Owner Neglects Land
Ruling that kharaj remains due if owner deliberately neglects land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that kharaj remains due if the owner deliberately neglects the land, explain the rationale of tamakkun, and distinguish the supplementary ruling that is not given as a fatwa.

Core Idea
Neglect does not cancel kharaj: the owner's ability to cultivate makes him liable, even if he wastes it.

The passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key question: if a kharaj landowner leaves his land uncultivated, is he still liable for kharaj? The answer is yes, and the reasoning reveals a principle about responsibility when one has the capacity to act. The mashā'ikh add a cautionary note: a stricter rule exists but is not used as fatwa to prevent abuse by oppressors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The owner deliberately leaves the land uncultivated (ta‘ṭīl). The ruling is: upon him is the kharaj (the tax remains due).
This applies to kharaj land, not ‘ushr land.
2
Locate the rationale
The text gives the reason: 'because the ability (tamakkun) to cultivate was present, and he is the one who wasted it.' The obligation is tied to the capacity, not actual cultivation.
Tamakkun is a key condition for liability.
3
Note the supplementary rule
The mashā'ikh add: if the owner shifts from a high-value crop to a low-value crop without excuse, he owes the higher kharaj (associated with the high-value crop), because he wasted the potential advantage.
This is an expansion of the principle: the owner is liable for the maximum value he could have produced.
4
Understand the fatwa restriction
This supplementary rule is known (yu‘raf) but not given as a fatwa (lā yuftā bihī), to prevent oppressive rulers from using it to seize people's wealth unjustly.
This shows the caution of Hanafi jurists in protecting the rights of the people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِنْ عَطَّلَهَا صَاحِبُهَا فَعَلَيْهِ الْخَرَاجُ لِأَنَّ التَّمَكُنَ كَانَ ثَابِما وَهُوَ الَّذِى فَوَّتَهُ قَالُوا مَنِ انتَقَلَ إِلَى أَخَسِ الْأَمْرَيْنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ عُذْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ الْخَرَاجُ الْأَعْلَى لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الَّذِى ضَيَّعَ الرِّيَادَةَ وَهُدَايُعْرَفُ وَلَا يُفْتَى بِهِ كَيْلَا يَتَجَرَّءَ الظَّلَمَةُ عَلَى أَحْدِ أَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ
He said: And if the owner neglects it (leaves it uncultivated), then upon him is the kharaj, because the ability (to cultivate) was present, and he is the one who wasted it. They (the mashā'ikh) said: Whoever shifts to the inferior of the two options without excuse, then upon him is the higher kharaj, because he is the one who wasted the advantage. And this is known but not given as a fatwa, lest the oppressors become audacious over people's wealth.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement: if the owner of kharaj land deliberately leaves it uncultivated, the kharaj is still due. The reasoning: the owner had the ability to cultivate (tamakkun) and chose to waste it. Thus the obligation remains. The mashā'ikh add a subsidiary ruling: if the land could grow a high-value crop (like saffron) but the owner chooses to grow a low-value crop (like millet) without excuse, he is liable for the higher kharaj associated with the high-value crop, because he wasted the potential. However, this latter ruling is not given as a fatwa (it is only for knowledge) to prevent oppressive rulers from seizing people's wealth under this pretext. This reflects the caution of Hanafi jurists in protecting the rights of the people.

Key Terms
تعطيل (ta‘ṭīl): Deliberately leaving land uncultivated or unused.
تمكن (tamakkun): Ability or capacity to act; here, the ability to cultivate the land.
الخراج الأعلى (al-kharāj al-a‘lā): The higher kharaj, levied on high-value crops.
لا يفتى به (lā yuftā bihī): Not given as a fatwa; known but not operative in practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a kharaj landowner deliberately leaves the land uncultivated?
A) The kharaj is dropped.
B) The kharaj remains due.
C) The kharaj is halved.
D) The land is confiscated.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is due on neglected land because the owner had the ability to cultivate; supplementary stricter rule is not used as fatwa to protect against oppression.

Kharaj on a Muslim Who Was Originally a Dhimmi
Ruling that kharaj continues after a dhimmi's conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kharaj for a Muslim who was originally a dhimmi and explain the rationale that kharaj is a land tax (mu'nah).

Core Idea
Kharaj is attached to the land, not the owner's religion, so conversion does not remove it.

A common assumption is that conversion to Islam removes all obligations owed by a dhimmi. However, the Hanafi school distinguishes between personal taxes (jizya) and land taxes (kharaj). This lesson examines a concise passage from al-Hidayah that clarifies why kharaj remains due even after a dhimmi embraces Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Read the passage and determine exactly who is affected and what the ruling is. The subject is a person from 'ahl al-kharaj' (dhimmi landowners) who becomes Muslim. The ruling is that kharaj is taken from him as before.
2
Extract the rationale (talil)
Find the reason given in the text: 'because in it is the meaning of mu'nah (maintenance)'. Understand that this rationale positions kharaj as a tax on land that covers communal expenses, not a personal religious tax.
The word mu'nah is key – it shifts the obligation from person to property.
3
Distinguish from jizya
Contrast kharaj with jizya (poll tax). Jizya drops upon conversion because it is a personal obligation tied to non-Muslim status. Kharaj does not drop because its basis is the land itself.
This distinction is essential for correct application.
4
Apply the principle to analogous situations
Consider other scenarios: a Muslim inherits kharaj land, or kharaj land is sold to a Muslim. The principle that kharaj is a mu'nah on the land means it continues regardless of the owner's faith.
The ruling is consistent: the land bears the tax.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَسْلَمَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرَاحِ أُخِذَمِنَهُ الْحَرَاجِ عَلَى حَالِهِ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ مَعْنَى الْمُؤْنَةِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ مَؤُنَةٌ فِي حَالَةِ الْبَقَاءِ فَأَمْكَنَ إبْقَاؤُهُ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ
And whoever from the people of kharaj becomes Muslim, kharaj is taken from him as before, because in it is the meaning of maintenance (mu'nah). So maintenance is considered in the state of continuation, and it is possible to keep it (the kharaj) upon the Muslim.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement: if a dhimmi who owns kharaj land converts to Islam, the kharaj continues to be taken from him. The reason: kharaj has the meaning of mu'nah (maintenance, expense) – it is a tax on the land for the benefit of the community, not a personal tax like jizya. Since the land remains productive, the tax remains. The key point is that the kharaj is attached to the land (as a land tax), not to the religious status of the owner. Therefore, conversion to Islam does not remove the obligation. This distinguishes kharaj from jizya, which drops upon conversion.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on conquered agricultural land; a mu'nah (maintenance) for public expenses.
مؤنة (mu'nah): Maintenance, expense, or cost; used in the text to describe kharaj as a land tax covering communal needs.
جزية (jizyah): Poll tax on free non-Muslims (dhimmis) in exchange for protection; drops upon conversion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does kharaj continue to be taken from a Muslim who was originally a dhimmi landowner?
A) Because he is still a dhimmi
B) Because kharaj is attached to the land, not the person's religion
C) Because Muslims are not allowed to own kharaj land
D) Because he must pay both kharaj and jizya

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is a land tax (mu'nah), not a personal religious tax, so it remains due from a Muslim who inherits or owns kharaj land, even after conversion.

Muslim Purchasing Kharaj Land from a Dhimmi
Ruling with proof (dalil naqli from Companions' practice).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Muslim purchasing kharaj land from a dhimmi and identify the evidence from the Companions' practice.

Core Idea
A Muslim may buy kharaj land from a dhimmi and pay kharaj; the Companions' practice proves permissibility without dislike.

This lesson addresses a specific transaction: a Muslim purchasing land that is subject to kharaj tax from a dhimmi (a non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state). The Hanafi school rules that this is permissible and not disliked, based on the established practice of the Companions. We will examine the ruling, its evidence, and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
State what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm (legal classification) is: It is permissible (ja'iz) for a Muslim to purchase kharaj land from a dhimmi.
The term 'kharaj land' refers to land conquered by Muslims but left in the hands of the original owners, subject to a land tax (kharaj).
2
Locate the Dalil (Evidence)
Find the proof cited in the passage. The text mentions that it is authentically established that the Companions (Sahaba) bought such lands and paid kharaj on them.
This is an evidence of practice (sunnah 'amaliyyah) and tacit consensus (ijma sukuti).
3
Understand the Nature of Kharaj
Understand why paying kharaj is not considered humiliating for a Muslim. Kharaj is a land tax (mu'nah), not a personal penalty, so it is permissible.
This explains why the Companions paid it without objection.
4
Note the Absence of Karahah
The passage explicitly states that this is permitted 'without dislike' (min ghayri karahah). Thus, it is not makruh.
Some earlier scholars may have disliked it, but the Hanafi position rejects that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَشْتَرِى الْمُسْلِمُ أَرْضَ الْحَرَاجِ مِنَ الَّذِى يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ الْحَرَاجُ لِمَا قُلْنَا وَقَدْ صَحَ أَنَّ الصَّحَابَةُ اشْتَرَوا اَرَاضِى الْخَرَاجِ وَكَانُوا يُؤَدُّونَ خَرَاجَهَا فَدَلَ عَلَى جَوَازِ الشِّرَاءِ وَأَخْذِ الْخَرَاجِ وَأَدَائِهِ لِلْمُسْلِمِ مِنْ غَيْرِ كَرَاهَةٍ
And it is permissible that a Muslim buy a kharaj land from the one from whom kharaj is taken (i.e., a dhimmi), due to what we have said. And it is authentically established that the Companions bought kharaj lands and used to pay their kharaj. So that proves the permissibility of purchase and taking of kharaj and its payment by a Muslim without dislike.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that a Muslim may purchase kharaj land from a dhimmi and will be liable to pay kharaj on it. The proof: the practice of the Companions (Sahaba) who bought such lands and paid kharaj without any disapproval. This demonstrates that there is no general prohibition on Muslims owning kharaj land and being subject to kharaj. The reasoning (based on the previous lesson) is that kharaj is a land tax (mu'nah) and not a personal penalty, so it is permissible for a Muslim to be charged it.

Key Terms
أرض الخراج (arḍ al-kharāj): Land subject to kharaj tax, typically conquered lands left in the hands of the original owners but taxed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence cited in al-Hidayah for the permissibility of a Muslim buying kharaj land from a dhimmi?
A) A direct Quranic verse
B) The practice of the Companions who bought such lands and paid kharaj
C) A hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him)
D) Consensus of later Hanafi scholars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a Muslim may purchase kharaj land from a dhimmi and pay kharaj, and this is not disliked, as proven by the practice of the Companions.

The Incompatibility of 'Ushr and Kharaj and Non-Repeatability of Kharaj
Explaining the Hanafi position and refuting Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that 'ushr and kharaj cannot combine and that kharaj is not repeated, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ushr and kharaj share a single cause, making them mutually exclusive; kharaj is a fixed annual levy, not per harvest.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two related rulings: the incompatibility of 'ushr (tithe) and kharaj (land tax) on the same land, and the non-repeatability of kharaj within a single year. The Hanafi school relies on the practice of Caliph ‘Umar and the principle that both taxes share the same underlying cause (‘illa)—the existence of productive land. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that they are distinct rights with different causes. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi land taxation operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds: 'ushr and kharaj cannot combine on the same land, and kharaj is not repeated if the land produces multiple harvests in a year.
This is the default ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the two taxes are different rights with different causes, so combining them is permissible. Also, he may hold that kharaj is repeated with each harvest.
Shafi'i's view is based on the idea that the two rights arise from different obligations.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is that the obligation of 'ushr arises from the land being owned by a Muslim, while kharaj arises from conquest. Since the causes are different, they can coexist.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the cause of obligation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the 'illa is one: the existence of productive land itself. Therefore, having both taxes on the same land would be doubling the tax on the same cause. For kharaj non-repeatability, the practice of ‘Umar is cited.
Hanafis use the principle of tahqiq al-manat: the effective cause is verified as one.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis collect only one tax per land (either 'ushr or kharaj, not both), and kharaj is a fixed annual sum regardless of multiple harvests. Shafi'is could collect both, leading to double taxation, and may repeat kharaj with each harvest.
This has implications for land revenue policy in Muslim states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ختم
ضرور رکھتا ہے۔ اسلئے مملکت اسلامیہ کے ظالم حکمران بھی عشر و خراج کو جمع نہیں کرتے تھے۔ چنانچہ درمیں صورت عادل و ظالم حکمران کا متفقہ فیصلہ ( عشر و خراج کا جمع نہ ہونا ) قابل حجت ہے۔ عشر کا تعلق نفس زمین کے ساتھ ہے پیداوار ضروری نہیں ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مسلمان سے ہر پیداوار پر عشر وصول کیا جاتا ہے بخلاف خراج کے کہ اس کا تعلق محض پیداوار کے ساتھ ہے اگر پیداوار موجود ہے تو خراج ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ اسی امر کو ہدایہ کے متن میں واضح کیا گیا ہے کہ عشر میں تحقیقی پیداوار معتبر ہے اور خراج میں تقدیری پیداوار کا اعتبار ہے۔ جوز مین قہر و غلبہ سے حاصل کی جائے اس پر خراج لاگو ہوتا ہے اور جس زمین کا مالک مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس پر عشر واجب ہوتا ہے ایک ہی زمین میں یہ دونوں وصف جمع نہیں ہو سکتے ۔
اس توجیہ میں صاحب ہدایہ نے امام شافعی کے استدلال کا جواب دیا ہے۔ ان کا استدلال یہ ہے کہ یہ دونوں حق مختلف ہیں ۔ اور یہ دو محل میں مختلف سبب سے واجب ہوتے ہیں۔ لہذا عشر و خراج کا جمع ہو نا منافی نہیں۔ امام شافعی کے اس استدلال کے جواب میں کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ دونوں وصف ایک جگہ جمع نہیں ہو سکتے اور ان دونوں کا سبب مختلف نہیں بلکہ ایک ہے اور وہ پیداوار والی زمین کا وجود ہے لہذا عشر و خراج جمع کرنے کے منافی ہونے کا تحقق ہو گیا۔ اختلاف زکوۃ کے حوالے سے بھی احناف کا موقف قوی ہے۔ کیونکہ جس عشری یا خراجی زمین کو تجارت کی نیت سے خریدا جاتا ہے اس پر تجارت پر مبنی زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اگر وہ (زمین ) تجارت کی نیت سے نہ خریدی جائے تو اس پر زکوۃ تجارت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ بخلاف عشر و خراج کے کہ زمین کے عشری ہونے پر عشر واجب ہوتا ہے اور خراجی ہونے کی صورت میں اس پر خراج عائد ہوتا ہے خواہ اسے (زمین کو ) مزارعت و مشارکت ، مستاجری کی نیت سے خریدا جائے۔ کیونکہ عشر وخراج و جوبی وظیفہ ہیں جو زمین کی موجودگی میں کسی بھی صورت میں مالک سے ساقط نہیں ہوتے جبکہ تجارت کی نیت سے زمین نہ خریدنے کی صورت میں زکوۃ تجارت ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا اختلاف زکوۃ کے حوالے سے بھی امام شافعی کا قول محل نظر ہے۔ چنانچہ اس پوری بحث سے باور ہوا که امام ابو حنیفہ و احناف کا قول رائج ہے اور امام شافعی کا موقف مرجوح متصور ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
پیداوار کے مکرر ہونے سے خراج مکرر نہیں ہوگا
وَلَا يَتَكَرَّرُ الْخَرَاجُ بِتَكَرُّرِ الْخَراجِ فِي سَنَةٍ لأَنَّ عُمَرَ لَمْ يُوَقِّقَهُ مُكَرَّر بِخِلَافِ الْعُشْرِأُ نَّهُ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ عُشُرًا إِلَّا بِوُجُوبِهِ فِي كُلّ خَارِج
ترجمه ولا يتكرر الخ اور ایک ہی سال میں زمین میں دوبار پیداوار ہو جانے سے دوبارہ خراج نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حضرت عمر نے خراج دوبارہ مقرر نہیں کیا تھا۔ برخلاف عشر کے کیونکہ عشر اسی وقت لازم آئے گا کہ اس زمین کی پیداوار سے دسواں حصہ لیا جائے ۔ تاکہ زمین میں جتنی پیداوار ہوئی ہے اس میں سے دسواں حصہ لینا ثابت ہو ۔ واللہ تعالیٰ اعلم
Book of Siyar. Commentary: It is necessary... (explanation that 'ushr and kharaj cannot be combined, refuting Imam Shafi'i). Then the matn: 'And kharaj is not repeated by the repetition of the produce in a year, because 'Umar did not fix it as repeated, unlike 'ushr, because 'ushr is only realized by its obligation on every output.' Translation: 'And it is not repeated...' Kharaj will not be taken again if land produces twice in one year, because Hadrat 'Umar did not fix it as repeated. Contrary to 'ushr, because 'ushr is only due by taking one-tenth from the produce of that land, so it is established that one-tenth is taken from every produce.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute followed by a ruling statement. The author begins by explaining the Hanafi position that 'ushr (tithe) and kharaj (land tax) cannot be combined on the same land. The cause ('illa) for both is the existence of productive land; since they share the same cause, they are mutually exclusive. The author then presents Imam al-Shafi'i's argument that they are different rights with different causes, so combination is possible. The Hanafi response is that the cause is one: the land itself. The discussion extends to zakat: if land is bought for trade, zakat on trade is payable, but 'ushr and kharaj remain due regardless of intention. Finally, the author cites the matn that kharaj is not repeated with multiple harvests in a year, based on the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, unlike 'ushr which is due on every harvest. This ruling is specific to Hanafi fiqh and is based on the precedent of the Caliph 'Umar.

Key Terms
العشر (al-‘ushr): A 10% tax on the produce of land owned by Muslims or land that has come into Muslim ownership through peaceful means.
الخراج (al-kharāj): A land tax imposed on land conquered by force and left in the hands of the original owners; a fixed annual amount based on productive capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kharaj not repeated with repeated produce in a year according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the land is only productive once a year
B) Because 'Umar did not fix it as repeated
C) Because it is a fixed annual tax like 'ushr
D) Because the Prophet prohibited it

Key Takeaway
Ushr and kharaj are mutually exclusive because they share the same 'illa, and kharaj is an annual levy not tied to each harvest.

Jizyah Not Accepted from Arab Polytheists and Apostates
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizyah for Arab polytheists and apostates, explain the reasoning based on severity of disbelief, and distinguish the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Jizyah is not accepted from Arab polytheists or apostates; only Islam or the sword.

Jizyah is a poll tax levied on protected non-Muslim subjects. However, Hanafi law excludes certain groups from this option due to the severity of their disbelief. In this passage, al-Marghinani explains that Arab polytheists (those among whom the Prophet lived and the Quran was revealed) and apostates (who rejected Islam after knowing it) are not eligible for jizyah; they must either accept Islam or face execution. This ruling is defended against Imam al-Shafi'i's view that Arab polytheists may be enslaved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is accepting jizyah from Arab polytheists and apostates. The Hanafi ruling is that it is not permissible (haram). The only alternatives are Islam or the sword.
This is a ruling of total exclusion.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the reasoning (qiyas) that their disbelief has become severe (taqhalusdh). The severity is due to the manifest miracle of the Prophet's raising among the Arabs and the Quran in their language for Arab polytheists, and for apostates, their rejection after clear guidance.
The 'illa is severity of disbelief.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
The severity of disbelief makes jizyah—a lesser option—inadequate. Jizyah is normally accepted as a sign of humility and protection; but for these groups, only the maximum punishment (death or conversion) suffices.
The link is between severity and denial of jizyah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute)
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that Arab polytheists can be enslaved, implying jizyah could be accepted as an alternative. The Hanafi response is that their severity overrides that option.
The dispute is about the scope of jizyah eligibility.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah affirms the Hanafi position as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view, based on the stronger 'illa.
This is the authoritative view in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا تُؤْخَذُ عَلَى عَبَدَةِ الْأَوْثَانِ مِنَ الْعَرَبِ وَلَا الْمُرْتَدِّينَ لِأَنَّ كُفْرَهُمَا قَدْ تَغَلَّظَ؛ أَمَّا مُشْرِكُو الْعَرَبِ فَلِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَشَأَ بَيْنَ أَظْهُرِهِمْ وَالْقُرْآنُ نَزَلَ بِلُغَتِهِمْ فَالْمُعْجِزَةُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ أَظْهَرُ، وَأَمَّا الْمُرْتَدُّ فَلِأَنَّهُ كَفَرَ بِرَبِّهِ بَعْدَ مَا هُدِيَ لِلْإِسْلَامِ وَوَقَفَ عَلَى مَحَاسِنِهِ فَلَا يُقْبَلُ مِنَ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ إِلَّا الْإِسْلَامُ أَوِ السَّيْفُ زِيَادَةً فِي الْعُقُوبَةِ. وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ يُسْتَرَقُ مُشْرِكُو الْعَرَبِ وَجَوَابُهُ مَا قُلْنَا.
Jizyah is not taken from the idol worshippers of the Arabs nor from apostates, because their disbelief has become severe. As for the polytheists of the Arabs, it is because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was raised among them and the Quran was revealed in their language, so the miracle is more manifest in their case. As for the apostate, it is because he disbelieved in his Lord after being guided to Islam and became aware of its beauties. So from both groups, nothing is accepted except Islam or the sword, as an increase in punishment. According to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), the polytheists of the Arabs may be enslaved. And the answer to him is what we have said.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Kitab al-Siyar stating that jizyah (poll tax) is not to be levied upon Arab polytheists (those who worship idols among the Arabs) nor upon apostates (those who leave Islam). The reason is that their disbelief is of the most severe kind. For the Arab polytheists, the severity is due to the fact that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) lived among them, the Quran was revealed in their language, and miracles were manifest to them, so their rejection is graver. For apostates, the severity is because they experienced the guidance of Islam and chose to reject it. Therefore, the only options for such people are conversion to Islam or execution by the sword; jizyah is not permitted as an alternative. This serves as an intensified punishment. The text then notes that Imam al-Shafi'i holds a different view: according to him, Arab polytheists can be enslaved (i.e., taken as captives). The Hanafi response to this is simply 'what we have said', referring back to the reasoning that their disbelief is too severe to allow jizyah or enslavement—only Islam or death.

Key Terms
جِزْيَة (jizyah): A poll tax levied on non-Muslim subjects of an Islamic state in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
مُرْتَدّ (murtadd): A person who was Muslim and then renounces Islam.
عَبَدَةُ الْأَوْثَان (abada al-awthan): Idol worshippers; those who worship idols or other objects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the only option given to an Arab polytheist or an apostate?
A) They may pay jizyah to avoid military service.
B) They must accept Islam or be put to the sword.
C) They can be enslaved and sold.
D) They are allowed to remain as dhimmis upon payment of jizyah.

Key Takeaway
Jizyah is not a universal option; Hanafi law excludes Arab polytheists and apostates, offering them only Islam or death due to the severity of their disbelief.

Women and Children of Arab Polytheists and Apostates as Spoils
Ruling on the status of women and children after victory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the enslavement of women and children of defeated Arab polytheists and apostates, and identify the precedent from the practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq.

Core Idea
The women and children of defeated Arab polytheists and apostates are lawful spoils, distributed as slaves.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a clear ruling: when Muslims overcome Arab polytheists or apostates in battle, the women and children become part of the fay' (spoils) and are distributed among the warriors. The ruling is supported by the precedent of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq during the Ridda Wars, specifically with the tribe of Bani Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The text states that women and children become part of the fay' (spoils). This means they are enslaved and divided among the fighters.
The term fay' here is synonymous with ghanimah (war booty).
2
Locate the proof
The author cites the action of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, who enslaved the women and children of Bani Hanifa after their apostasy.
This is a practice of a Companion (Amal al-Sahabi) and considered a source of law in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the scope
The ruling applies specifically to Arab polytheists and apostates. It is not extended to all non-Muslims without further evidence.
Other schools may differ on the inclusion of apostates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا ظَهَرَ عَلَيْهِمْ فَنِسَاؤُهُمْ وَصِبْيَانُهُمْ فِي الْفَيْءِ لِأَنَّ أَبَا بَكْرٍ الصِّدِّيقَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ اسْتَرَقَ نِسْوَانَ بَنِي حَنِيفَةَ وَصِبْيَانَهُمْ لَمَّا ارْتَدُّوا وَقَسَّمَهُمْ بَيْنَ الْغَانِمِينَ.
And when [the Muslims] overcome them, then their women and children are in the fay' (spoils), because Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) enslaved the women of Bani Hanifa and their children when they apostatized, and he distributed them among the warriors.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that if Muslims defeat and overcome Arab polytheists or apostates, the women and children of the defeated become part of the fay' (spoils of war). This means they are considered ghanimah (war booty) and are distributed among the Muslim warriors as slaves. The proof cited is the action of the first Caliph Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, who, after the Ridda Wars (wars against apostates), specifically with the tribe of Bani Hanifa (followers of the false prophet Musaylimah), enslaved their women and children and distributed them as spoils. This establishes a precedent that is followed in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
فَيْء (fay'): Property taken from non-Muslims without active warfare (like jizyah or land tax) or sometimes spoils generally. In this context, it refers to war booty (ghanimah).
غَانِمِين (ghanimin): The warriors who participate in the battle and are entitled to a share of the spoils.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the basis for the ruling that women and children of apostates become spoils?
A) A direct Quranic verse.
B) The practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq with Bani Hanifa.
C) A hadith from the Prophet.
D) Analogy with jizyah.

Key Takeaway
The precedent of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq establishes that the women and children of apostates become spoils, a ruling specific to Arab polytheists and apostates.

Ruling on Apostate Men and Jizyah Exemption for Women and Children
Ruling on apostasy and jizyah exemption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on unrepentant apostate men and explain the reason jizyah is not required from women and children.

Core Idea
Jizyah replaces killing or fighting; women and children neither fight nor are executed, so no jizyah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two related rulings: the capital punishment for apostate men who refuse to return to Islam, and the exemption of women and children from jizyah. The reasoning (ta'lil) ties both rulings to the nature of jizyah as a substitute for the life spared or the obligation to fight. Understanding this rationale clarifies the legal capacity (ahliyyah) required for military obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two distinct but connected rulings: (1) apostate men who do not repent are killed; (2) jizyah is not imposed on women or children. Identify each ruling and its subject.
The first ruling is about adult male apostates; the second precludes jizyah on women and minors.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The sole proof is a rational explanation (ta'lil): 'because jizyah is obligated as a substitute for killing or fighting'. This is the 'illa for the obligation of jizyah.
The proof is not a text but a causal reasoning. The author assumes the first ruling (killing) is already established.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The 'illa works as follows: if jizyah is a substitute for killing or fighting, then those who are not subject to killing or fighting (women and children) should not be required to pay jizyah. The absence of the replaced obligation removes the substitute.
Women and children are not killed because they lack legal capacity (ahliyyah) for combat, and they are not required to fight by the enemy.
4
Examine any implicit condition
The ruling on men applies specifically to those who 'do not accept Islam'. This implies an opportunity to repent; the killing is only after refusal. For women and children, the exemption stands regardless of conversion status.
This passage does not discuss women apostates; in Hanafi law, women apostates are imprisoned, not killed.
5
Consider the legal consequences
The practical outcome: in a territory of apostates, only adult men face execution; women and children are neither killed nor taxed with jizyah. They may be enslaved or set free, depending on further rulings.
The ruling prevents jizyah from being a burden on those who cannot be fought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ لَّمْ يُسْلِمْ مِنْ رِجَالِهِمْ قُتِلَ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَلَا جِزْيَةَ عَلَى امْرَأَةٍ وَلَا صَبِيٍّ لِأَنَّهَا وَجَبَتْ بَدَلًا عَنِ الْقَتْلِ أَوْ عَنِ الْقِتَالِ وَهُمَا لَا يُقْتَلَانِ وَلَا يُقَاتِلَانِ لِعَدَمِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ.
And whoever among their men does not accept Islam is killed, for what we have mentioned; and there is no jizyah on a woman nor on a child, because jizyah is obligated as a substitute for killing or for fighting, and they [women and children] are not killed nor do they fight, due to lack of legal capacity.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage clarifies the fate of apostates. Among the men (i.e., adult male apostates who are capable of fighting), if they refuse to return to Islam, they are killed. This is based on the earlier reasoning that only Islam or the sword is accepted from apostates. The text then addresses women and children: jizyah is not levied on them. The reason given is that jizyah is a substitute for either execution or fighting (i.e., it spares the life of the person who would otherwise be killed or would be required to fight). Since women and children are not subject to execution or to fighting for the enemy (due to their legal incapacity or protected status), jizyah does not apply to them. Thus, their status is different from that of apostate men.

Key Terms
أَهْلِيَّة (ahliyyah): Legal capacity; women and children lack full capacity for military obligations, so they are not subject to execution or fighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is jizyah not required from women and children according to this passage?
A) Because they are financially unable to pay.
B) Because jizyah is a substitute for killing or fighting, and women and children are not subject to those.
C) Because they are protected by their husbands.
D) Because they are not considered enemies.

Key Takeaway
Jizyah is a substitute for combat; those who cannot be fought or executed (women and children) are exempt from jizyah.

Jizyah Exemption for the Disabled and Elderly: The Hanafi Ruling and Abu Yusuf's View
Ruling on jizyah for disabled and elderly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories exempt from jizyah in the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a wealthy disabled person.

Core Idea
A disabled person unable to fight is exempt; but if wealthy and can advise, jizyah may be imposed according to Abu Yusuf.

In this passage, the author lists categories of dhimmi individuals who are exempt from paying jizyah—the chronically ill, blind, paralyzed, and very old. While the general reason is inability to fight, Imam Abu Yusuf introduces a nuance: if such a person has wealth and can offer strategic advice in war, jizyah becomes obligatory. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the internal Hanafi difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exempt categories
List the categories mentioned: zamin (chronically ill), ama (blind), mafluj (paralyzed), and shaykh kabir (very old). Understand each term's scope.
These are all individuals who cannot physically fight.
2
Note the general basis for exemption
The text says 'for what we have explained' – referring to the earlier principle that jizyah is in exchange for protection; those who cannot fight are not targets of killing, so no jizyah.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's differing view
Abu Yusuf holds that if the disabled person possesses wealth (mal) and has an opinion (ra'y) useful in war, jizyah is obligatory. He argues that such a person may be killed by the enemy for his counsel, so protection is still provided.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon view) maintains exemption. Al-Hidayah prefers this over Abu Yusuf's view. Thus, the operative ruling today is exemption.
Abu Yusuf's view is a minority within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا زَمِنَ وَلَا أَعْمَى وَكَذَا الْمَفْلُوجُ وَالشَّيْخُ الْكَبِيرُ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا. وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ تَجِبُ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ لِأَنَّهُ يُقْتَلُ فِي الْجُمْلَةِ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ رَأْيٌ. وَلَا عَلَى فَقِيرٍ غَيْرِ مُعْتَمِلٍ خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِيِّ لَهُ إِطْلَاقُ حَدِيثِ مُعَاذٍ عَنْهُ. وَلَنَا أَنَّ عُثْمَانَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ لَمْ يُوَظِّفْهَا عَلَى فَقِيرٍ غَيْرِ مُعْتَمِلٍ وَذَلِكَ بِمَحْضَرٍ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ وَأَنَّ خَرَاجَ الْأَرْضِ لَا يُوَظَّفُ عَلَى أَرْضٍ لَا طَاقَةَ لَهَا فَكَذَا هَذَا الْخَرَاجُ وَالْحَدِيثُ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى الْمُعْتَمِلِ.
He said: And no [jizyah] on a chronically ill person, nor on a blind person, and likewise on a paralyzed person and a very old man for what we have explained. And from Abu Yusuf: that it (jizyah) is obligatory if he has wealth, because he may be killed in general if he has an opinion (i.e., can give counsel). And there is no jizyah on a poor person who does not work, contrary to al-Shafi'i who has the absolute hadith of Mu'adh (in this regard). And our proof is that Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) did not impose it on a poor person who does not work, and that was in the presence of the Companions; and the land tax (kharaj) is not imposed on land that has no capacity, so similarly this tax (jizyah); and the hadith is interpreted to refer to one who works.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage addresses categories of people exempt from jizyah. According to the Hanafi school (as stated by the author), jizyah is not required from: a 'zamin' (chronically ill or paralyzed person), a blind person, a paralyzed person (mafluj), and a very old man (shaykh kabir). The reason, as previously explained, is that these individuals are incapable of fighting and are not subject to killing by the enemy (since they are non-combatants). The text then notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Abu Yusuf reports that if such a person possesses wealth (mal), jizyah is obligatory for him because even a disabled person might be killed in war if he has useful opinions (i.e., can serve as a counselor to the enemy). The Hanafi ruling then proceeds to another category: a poor person who is not employed (ghayr mu'tamil) is exempt from jizyah. This is in opposition to Imam al-Shafi'i, who relies on the general hadith of Mu'adh (when he was sent to Yemen) that jizyah is to be taken from every adult male. The Hanafi response is that the practice of Caliph Uthman did not impose jizyah on such poor people, and this was done in the presence of Companions, implying consensus. Additionally, they draw an analogy with the land tax (kharaj), which is not imposed on barren land; similarly, jizyah should not be imposed on a person with no earning capacity. The hadith of Mu'adh is interpreted to apply to those who are capable of work (mu'tamil), not the poor who cannot work.

Key Terms
زَمِن (zamin): A person suffering from a chronic illness or physical defect that prevents movement and fighting.
أَعْمَى (a'ma): A blind person, unable to see.
مَفْلُوج (mafluj): A paralyzed person, often half-body paralysis.
شَيْخ كَبِير (shaykh kabir): A very old man, too old to fight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT exempt from jizyah?
A) A blind man who is poor.
B) A paralyzed man who is wealthy.
C) A very old man who gives military advice.
D) A chronically ill man who has no opinion.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts the disabled and elderly from jizyah, with a minority view (Abu Yusuf) that jizyah applies if they have wealth and can offer counsel in war.

Jizyah Exemption for the Poor Non-Worker: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on jizyah for poor non-worker

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on jizyah for a poor non-working dhimmi and explain the evidence used against the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A poor person who cannot work is exempt from jizyah, as established by Companion practice and analogy with land tax.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: Should jizyah be collected from a dhimmi who is so poor that he cannot work? The Hanafi school says no, based on the practice of Caliph Uthman and an analogy with the land tax (kharaj). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing a general hadith. This lesson dissects the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject: faqir ghayr mu'tamil
Understand the term: a poor person who does not engage in any work or profession and cannot earn a living.
This is different from a poor person who works (mu'tamil) – the latter is liable.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that such a person is exempt from jizyah.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Two proofs: 1) The practice of Uthman (radiAllahu anhu) who did not impose jizyah on such a person, and this was in the presence of Companions, indicating consensus. 2) Qiyas (analogy) with land tax (kharaj): just as kharaj is not imposed on barren land, jizyah is not imposed on a person with no earning capacity.
The dalil naqli (practice of Uthman) precedes the qiyas.
4
Examine the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the general hadith of Mu'adh (when he was sent to Yemen) which commands taking jizyah from every adult male, without exception.
This hadith is general (amm) in their view.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by interpreting the hadith to apply only to those who are capable of working (mu'tamil). The general text is restricted (takhsis) by the practice of Uthman and the qiyas.
This shows how Hanafi usul uses Companion practice for takhsis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا زَمِنَ وَلَا أَعْمَى وَكَذَا الْمَفْلُوجُ وَالشَّيْخُ الْكَبِيرُ لِمَا بَيَّنَّا. وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ تَجِبُ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ لِأَنَّهُ يُقْتَلُ فِي الْجُمْلَةِ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ رَأْيٌ. وَلَا عَلَى فَقِيرٍ غَيْرِ مُعْتَمِلٍ خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِيِّ لَهُ إِطْلَاقُ حَدِيثِ مُعَاذٍ عَنْهُ. وَلَنَا أَنَّ عُثْمَانَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ لَمْ يُوَظِّفْهَا عَلَى فَقِيرٍ غَيْرِ مُعْتَمِلٍ وَذَلِكَ بِمَحْضَرٍ مِنَ الصَّحَابَةِ وَأَنَّ خَرَاجَ الْأَرْضِ لَا يُوَظَّفُ عَلَى أَرْضٍ لَا طَاقَةَ لَهَا فَكَذَا هَذَا الْخَرَاجُ وَالْحَدِيثُ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى الْمُعْتَمِلِ.
He said: And no [jizyah] on a chronically ill person, nor on a blind person, and likewise on a paralyzed person and a very old man for what we have explained. And from Abu Yusuf: that it (jizyah) is obligatory if he has wealth, because he may be killed in general if he has an opinion (i.e., can give counsel). And there is no jizyah on a poor person who does not work, contrary to al-Shafi'i who has the absolute hadith of Mu'adh (in this regard). And our proof is that Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) did not impose it on a poor person who does not work, and that was in the presence of the Companions; and the land tax (kharaj) is not imposed on land that has no capacity, so similarly this tax (jizyah); and the hadith is interpreted to refer to one who works.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage addresses categories of people exempt from jizyah. According to the Hanafi school (as stated by the author), jizyah is not required from: a 'zamin' (chronically ill or paralyzed person), a blind person, a paralyzed person (mafluj), and a very old man (shaykh kabir). The reason, as previously explained, is that these individuals are incapable of fighting and are not subject to killing by the enemy (since they are non-combatants). The text then notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Abu Yusuf reports that if such a person possesses wealth (mal), jizyah is obligatory for him because even a disabled person might be killed in war if he has useful opinions (i.e., can serve as a counselor to the enemy). The Hanafi ruling then proceeds to another category: a poor person who is not employed (ghayr mu'tamil) is exempt from jizyah. This is in opposition to Imam al-Shafi'i, who relies on the general hadith of Mu'adh (when he was sent to Yemen) that jizyah is to be taken from every adult male. The Hanafi response is that the practice of Caliph Uthman did not impose jizyah on such poor people, and this was done in the presence of Companions, implying consensus. Additionally, they draw an analogy with the land tax (kharaj), which is not imposed on barren land; similarly, jizyah should not be imposed on a person with no earning capacity. The hadith of Mu'adh is interpreted to apply to those who are capable of work (mu'tamil), not the poor who cannot work.

Key Terms
فَقِير غَيْر مُعْتَمِل (faqir ghayr mu'tamil): A poor person who does not work and cannot earn a living.
خَرَاج الْأَرْض (kharaj al-ard): Land tax imposed on agricultural land. Used by analogy: just as kharaj is not imposed on unproductive land, jizyah is not imposed on those who cannot work.
مُعْتَمِل (mu'tamil): A person who works or is capable of working.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for exempting a poor non-working dhimmi from jizyah?
A) The general hadith of Mu'adh
B) The practice of Uthman and analogy with kharaj
C) The principle that no tax is on the poor
D) Consensus of all scholars

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts a destitute dhimmi who cannot work from jizyah, based on Companion practice and analogy with the land tax, restricting the general hadith of Mu'adh.

Jizyah Drops with Islam or Death: Hanafi Position vs. Shafi'i View
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on jizyah falling upon Islam or death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizyah dropping upon Islam or death, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the strength of the Hanafi proofs.

Core Idea
Jizyah falls with Islam or death because it is a punishment for kufr, not a rental fee.

The obligation of jizyah on a dhimmi raises a critical question: what happens if the dhimmi becomes Muslim or dies? The Hanafi school rules that jizyah drops entirely, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. This lesson examines the proofs behind each position and why the Hanafi view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: jizyah drops when a dhimmi becomes Muslim or dies as a kafir.
The matn says 'wa man aslama wa 'alayhi jizyah saqatat, wa kadhalika idha mata kafiran'.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that jizyah does not drop in either case.
The text says 'khilafan li al-Shafi'i fihima'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument: jizyah is a substitute (badal) for protection and residence already received, so it remains like rental fees or blood money settlements.
The text says 'annahu wajabat badalan 'an al-'ismah aw 'an al-sukna wa qad wasala ilayhi al-mu'awwad'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi proofs: (1) hadith 'There is no jizyah upon a Muslim'; (2) jizyah is punishment for kufr, which ends with Islam or death; (3) the purpose of punishment (daf' al-sharr) ceases; (4) jizyah is a substitute for aid (nusrah) which the Muslim can now provide; (5) refutation of the substitute claim: protection is inherent and residence is privately owned.
The text lists multiple proofs; focus on the hadith as primary and the rational arguments as supportive.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: for Hanafis, no jizyah is collected after conversion or death; for Shafi'is, jizyah remains due for the period before conversion or is an obligation on the estate.
This affects actual collection and estate settlement.

Source Text

وَمَنْ أَسْلَمَ وَعَلَيْهِ جِزْيَةٌ سَقَطَتْ وَكَذَالِكَ إِذَامَاتَ كَافِرًا خِلَاقًا لِلشَّافِعِي فِيْهِمَا لَهُ أَنَّهَا وَجَبَتْ بَدَلًا عَنِ الْعِصْمَةِ أَوْعَنِ السُّكْنى وَقَدْ وَصَلَ إِلَيْهِ الْمُعَوَّضُ فَلَا يَسْقُطُ عَنْهُ الْعِوَضُ بِهَذَا الْعَارِضِ كَمَا فِى الْأُجُرَةِ وَالصُّلْحِ عَنْ دَمِ الْعَمَد وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَيْسَ عَلى مُسْلِمٍ جِزْيَةَ وَلأَنَّهَا الدُّنْيَا لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا لِدَفْعِ الشَّر وقد انفَعَ بِالْمَوتِ وَ الإسلام وَلِأَنَّهَا وَجَبَتْ بَدَلَا عَنِ النُّصُرَةِ فِى حَقِنَارَ قَدْ قَدَرَ عَلَيْهَا بِنَفْسِهِ بَعْدَ الإِسْلَامِ وَالْعِصْمَةُ تَنبت يكَونِهِ الحَمِيَّا وَ الدِّتِي يَسْكُنُ مِلْكَ نَفْسِهِ فَلَا مَعْنَى لا يُجَابِ بَدَلِ الْعِصْمَةِ وَالسُّكنى ترجمہ اگر ایساز می جس پر جزیہ باقی ہر وہ اسلام لے آیا تو اس کا جزیہ ختم ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر وہ حالت کفر میں مر گیا تو بھی جزیہ ختم ہو جائے گا۔ ان دونوں صورتوں میں امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جزیہ تو اس کی جان کی حفاظت یا سکونت کے بدلے واجب ہوا تھا ۔ اس طرح اس نے جب اپنے لئے حفاظت اور سکونت حاصل کر لی تو اس کے عوض جو چیز ( جزیہ) واجب ہوئی تھی وہ اس کے اسلام لانے یا اس کے مرجانے سے ساقط نہیں ہوگی ۔ جیسے کہ اگر اس نے کوئی چیز کسی مسلمان پر جزیہ نہیں ہے ۔ (اس کی روایت ابوداؤ د والترندی واحمد اور دار قطنی نے کی ہے ) اور ابوداؤد نے سفیان ثوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے اس کے معنی یہ بتائے ہیں کی ذمی جب مسلمان ہو جائے تو اس پر جزیہ کوئی سزا اس لئے ثابت ہے کہ حالت کفر میں رہنے کی وجہ سے جو شرارتیں وہ کر سکتا ہو وہ نہ کر سکے اور یہ بات اس کے مرجانے یا مسلمان ہو جانے سے ختم ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور اس وجہ سے بھی کہ جزیہ واجب ہونا ہمارے حق میں اس کی نصرت کا دعوض ہے۔ یعنی وہ اپنے کفر کی وجہ سے کوئی مدد نہیں کر سکتا ہے اس لئے اس پر جزیہ لازم کر دیا گیا ہے۔ جبکہ اس کے عوض وہ مسلمان ہوکر خود ہر طرح سے مدد کرنے پر قادر ہو گیا ہے اور یہ بات کہ امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے اس جزیہ کو حفاظت و سکونت کا عوض قرار دیا ہے تو بات یہ ہے کہ اس کے محض آدمی ہونے کی وجہ سے خواہ وہ کچھ بھی ہو اس کی حفاظت ثابت ہے۔ اور اس کی سکونت کا وہ خود مالک ہے یعنی اس کی اپنی ذاتی ملک میں ہے لہذا اس کی حفاظت اور سکونت کے عوض جز یہ واجب کرنے کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں۔
Whoever becomes Muslim while jizyah is upon him, it falls. Similarly, if he dies as a kafir. Contrary to al-Shafi'i in both. For him, it became due as a substitute for protection or residence, and the compensated thing has reached him, so the substitute does not fall due to this occurrence, like in rental and compromise for intentional blood. For us, his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no jizyah upon a Muslim.' And because it became due as a punishment for kufr, therefore it is called jizyah, and it and 'jaza' are one. Punishment for kufr falls with Islam and is not carried out after death. And because legislation of punishment in the world is only to repel evil, and it ends with death and Islam. And because it became due as a substitute for aid in our right, and he became capable of it by himself after Islam. Protection is established by his being human, and residence he owns by his own property, so there is no meaning to obligate a substitute for protection and residence. Translation: If a person upon whom jizyah is due becomes Muslim, his jizyah falls. Similarly, if he dies in a state of kufr, jizyah falls. Imam Shafi'i disagrees in both cases. His proof: Jizyah was due as a substitute for protection of life or residence. Since he obtained protection and residence, the substitute should not fall due to this incident, like in rental or settlement for blood money. Our proof: The Prophet ﷺ said there is no jizyah upon a Muslim. Also, jizyah is a punishment for kufr, so it falls with Islam or death. Also, the purpose of punishment is to prevent harm, which ceases with Islam or death. Also, jizyah is a substitute for aid (nusrah) which he can now provide himself after Islam. The idea of substitute for protection and residence is baseless because protection is inherent to being human, and residence is his own property.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with an inter-madhhab dispute regarding jizyah when a dhimmi becomes Muslim or dies in kufr. The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, is that jizyah drops in both cases. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that jizyah is a substitute (badal) for protection and residence, which the dhimmi has already received, so it remains obligatory. The Hanafi response provides multiple proofs: a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ that there is no jizyah upon a Muslim, and rational arguments—jizyah is a punishment for kufr, and punishment ends when the cause ends by Islam or death; the worldly purpose of punishment (daf' al-sharr) ceases; jizyah is a substitute for aid (nusrah) which the Muslim can now provide himself; and the Shafi'i claim of substitute for protection is invalid because protection is inherent for any human and residence is privately owned. Thus the Hanafi position is that jizyah drops.

Key Terms
جزیہ (jizyah): Poll tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in an Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what happens to jizyah when a dhimmi dies in a state of kufr?
A) It must be collected from his estate.
B) It falls and is not collected.
C) It is reduced by half.
D) It is transferred to his heirs.

Key Takeaway
Jizyah drops upon Islam or death because it is a punishment for kufr, not a substitute for ongoing services.

Jizyah Not Taken from a Dhimmi Who Dies
Ruling on jizyah when dhimmi dies, with intra-Hanafi debate on nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on jizyah when a dhimmi dies and explain the Hanafi ta'lil and the intra-madhhab disagreement on the nature of jizyah.

Core Idea
Jizyah ends with the dhimmi's death; it is a punishment for kufr, not a debt.

This lesson examines a clear consensus ruling: if a dhimmi dies during the year, no jizyah is taken from him. The passage then delves into the rationale behind this ruling, revealing a fundamental disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two students on whether jizyah is a punishment or a substitute. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping other rules of jizyah.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the ruling
Read the first line: 'If he dies at the completion of the year, it is not taken from him... Similarly, if he dies during some part of the year.' This is the straightforward ruling.
Note the agreement: 'fi qawlihim jami'an' (in all their opinions).
2
2. Understand the debate on tadakhul (overlap)
The text introduces an analogy with kharaj (land tax). The Sahibayn treat jizyah as a substitute (iwad), so it does NOT overlap. Abu Hanifa treats it as a punishment (uqubah), so it DOES overlap like hudud.
The death ruling itself is not affected by this debate—both sides agree jizyah is not taken upon death.
3
3. Examine the evidence for it being a punishment
Abu Hanifa points to the humiliating method of collection (standing, shaking by collar, saying 'O enemy of Allah'). This shows it is a punishment.
This is a key ta'lil (rational proof) from the school.
4
4. Compare with the substitute view
The Sahibayn argue that since jizyah can be collected after successive years, it does not overlap, like kharaj.
5
5. Conclude the ruling and its basis
The ruling that jizyah is not taken upon death is agreed, but the underlying reason differs. The Hanafi school typically prefers Abu Hanifa's view that it is a punishment.
This distinction matters for cases of overlap (e.g., multiple years unpaid).

وَإِنْ مَاتَ عِندَ تَمَامِ السَّنَةِ لَمْ يُؤْخَذَ مِنْهُ فِى قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا وَكَذَالِكَ إِنْ مَاتَ فِى بَعْضِ السَّنَةِ أَمَّا مَسْأَلَة الْمَوْتِ فَقَدْ ذَكَرُنَاهَا وَقِيلَ خَرَاجُ الْأَرْضِ عَلى هَذَا الخِلافِ وَقِيلَ لَا تَدَاجُلَ فِيهِ بِالْاتِفَاقِ لَهُمَا فِى الخِلافِيَّةِ أَنَّ الخَراج وَجَبَ عِوَضًا وَلَاعْوَاضُ إِذَا اجْتَمَعْتُ وَامْكَنَ اسْتِيفَاءُ هَا تُستَوفِى وَقَدْ أَمْكَنَ فِيمَا نَحْنُ فِيهِ بَعْدَ تَوَالِي السِّنِينَ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا أَسْلَمَ لَانَّهُ تَعَذَّرَ اسْتِيفَاؤُهُ وَلَابِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهَا وَجَبَتْ عُقُوبَةٌ عَلَى الإِصْرَارِ عَلَى الْكُفْرِ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ وَلِهَذَا لَا تُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ لَوْبَعَتَ عَلَى يَدِنَائِبِهِ فِي أَصَحَ الرِّوَايَاتِ بَلْ يُكَلِّفُ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِهِ بِنَفْسِهِ فَيُعْطِي قَائِمًا وَالقَابِضُ مِنْهُ قَاعِدٌ وفِي رِوَايَةٍ يَأْخُذُ بِتَلْبِيه وَيَهُزُّهُ هذَا وَيَقُولُ اَعْطِنِى الْجِزْيَةَ يَاذِمِّيُّ وَقِيلَ عَدُوَّ اللَّهِ فَثَبَتَ أَنَّهُ عُقُوْبَةٌ وَالْعُقُوبَاتُ إِذَا اجْتَمَعَتْ تَدَاخَلَتْ كَالْحُدُودِ وَلَانَّهَا وَجَبَتْ بَدَلَاعَنِ الْقَتْلِ فِي حَقِّهِمْ وَعَنِ النُّصْرَةِ فِي حَقِنَا كَمَا ذَكَرُ نَا لَكِنْ فِي الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ لَا فِي الْمَاضِي لَأَنَّ الْقَتْلَ إِنَّمَا يُسْتَوُ فِى لِحِرَابِ قَائِمٍ فِي الْحَالِ لَا لِحِرَابِ مَاضٍ وَكَذَا النُّصْرَةُ فِي الْمُسْتَقَبَلِ لأَنَّ الْمَاضِي وَقَعَتِ الْغُ عَنهُ ثُمَّ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٌ فِي الْحِزْيَةِ فِي الْجَامِعِ
If he dies at the completion of the year, it is not taken from him in all their opinions. Similarly, if he dies during some part of the year. As for the question of death, we have mentioned it. And it was said that kharaj al-ard (land tax) is upon this disagreement, and it was said there is no tadakhul in it by agreement. For them (Sahibayn) in al-Khilafiyyah that kharaj is due as a substitute, and substitutes, when they accumulate and collection is possible, are collected. And it is possible in our case after successive years, unlike the case of Islam because collection is prevented. For Abu Hanifa, it became due as a punishment for persistence in kufr as we explained, and for this it is not accepted if he sends it by his deputy in the soundest narrations; rather he is required to bring it himself and give it standing while the collector sits. And in a narration, he takes him by his collar and shakes him and says: 'Give the jizyah, O dhimmi'—and it was said 'O enemy of Allah'. So it is established that it is a punishment, and punishments when they accumulate overlap, like hudud. And because it became due as a substitute for killing regarding them and for aid regarding us as we mentioned, but for the future, not the past, because killing is only exacted for ongoing hostility, not past, and likewise aid is for the future because the past has been waived. Then the statement of Muhammad about jizyah in al-Jami'.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on jizyah when a dhimmi dies. The matn states that if a dhimmi dies at the end of the year or during the year, jizyah is not taken from him, and this is agreed upon by all. The commentary then discusses an analogy with kharaj al-ard (land tax) and the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on tadakhul. It explains the rationale: Abu Hanifa holds that jizyah is a punishment (uqubah) for persistence in kufr, and punishments overlap (tadakhul) like hudud. The humiliating method of collection (standing while paying, shaking by collar) confirms it is a punishment. The Sahibayn view jizyah as a substitute (iwad) that does not overlap. The passage concludes with a distinction: jizyah is a substitute for killing (in their right) and for aid (in our right), but only for the future, not for the past.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax on agricultural land, distinguished from jizyah in this passage as a substitute (iwad) that does not overlap.
عقوبة (uqubah): Punishment; legal classification of jizyah according to Abu Hanifa.
عوض (iwad): Substitute or compensation; legal classification of jizyah according to the Sahibayn.
تداخل (tadakhul): Overlap or merging of obligations or penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a dhimmi dies during the year before paying his annual jizyah?
A) His heirs must pay the full year's jizyah.
B) He must pay a prorated amount for the months he lived.
C) No jizyah is taken from him.
D) He must pay jizyah only if he died at the end of the year.

Key Takeaway
Jizyah is a personal obligation that ceases with the dhimmi's death; it is not a debt that can be inherited or prorated.

Intercalation of Jizya: When Multiple Years Accumulate
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jizya intercalation with talil arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on intercalation of jizya and evaluate the competing proofs from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Jizya intercalates as a punishment; the earlier year's payment drops. Sahibayn disagree.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario: a dhimmi fails to pay jizya for two years. Must he pay both years or only one? The answer hinges on whether jizya is a punishment (uquba) or compensation (iwad). Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students diverge, and we will trace the legal reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fact pattern and the ikhtilaf
The passage begins: if two years pass without collection, the two jizyas intercalate (only one due). Then it states that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree, holding that both years must be collected. Identify the core disagreement.
Fact pattern: jizya unpaid for two consecutive years.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Abu Hanifa holds that jizya is a punishment (uquba) for persistence in kufr. Punishments intercalate like hudud. The harsh collection method (standing, shaking, rebuking) supports this classification.
Dalil: analogy to hudud and manner of collection.
3
State the Sahibayn/Shafi'i position and its basis
The Sahibayn (and Shafi'i) argue jizya is compensation (iwad) for protection and exemption from fighting. Compensations do not intercalate; each year's payment must be collected if possible.
Dalil: jizya as iwad, no tadakhul for compensations.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response regarding future vs past
Abu Hanifa responds that compensation is for future protection, not past. The past year has lapsed; collection for it is impossible. Also, the punitive elements show it is not mere compensation.
Key point: obligation at beginning of year, not end.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Under Abu Hanifa, only one year's jizya is collected; under the Sahibayn, both years. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as reflected in Al-Hidayah.
Practical consequence: difference in amount collected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
