يُؤْخَذْ وَهَذَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةً وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يُؤْخَذْمِتُهُ وَهُوَقُوْلُ الشَّافِعِي . وَلِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهَا وَجَبَتْ عُقُوبَةٌ عَلَى الإِصْرَارِ عَلَى الْكُفْرِ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ وَلِهَذَا لَا تُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ لَوْبَعَتَ عَلَى يَدِنَائِبِهِ فِي أَصَحَ الرِّوَايَاتِ بَلْ يُكَلِّفُ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِهِ بِنَفْسِهِ فَيُعْطِي قَائِمًا وَالقَابِضُ مِنْهُ قَاعِدٌ وفِي رِوَايَةٍ يَأْخُذُ بِتَلْبِيه وَيَهُزُّهُ هذَا وَيَقُولُ اَعْطِنِى الْجِزْيَةَ يَاذِمِّيُّ وَقِيلَ عَدُوَّ اللَّهِ فَثَبَتَ أَنَّهُ عُقُوْبَةٌ وَالْعُقُوبَاتُ إِذَا اجْتَمَعَتْ تَدَاخَلَتْ كَالْحُدُودِ وَلَانَّهَا وَجَبَتْ بَدَلَاعَنِ الْقَتْلِ فِي حَقِّهِمْ وَعَنِ النُّصْرَةِ فِي حَقِنَا كَمَا ذَكَرُ نَا لَكِنْ فِي الْمُسْتَقْبَلِ لَا فِي الْمَاضِي لَأَنَّ الْقَتْلَ إِنَّمَا يُسْتَوُ فِى لِحِرَابِ قَائِمٍ فِي الْحَالِ لَا لِحِرَابِ مَاضٍ وَكَذَا النُّصْرَةُ فِي الْمُسْتَقَبَلِ لأَنَّ الْمَاضِي وَقَعَتِ الْغُ عَنهُ ثُمَّ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٌ فِي الْحِزْيَةِ فِي الْجَامِعِ لصَّغِيرِ وَجَاءَتْ سَنَةً أُخْرَى حَمَلَهُ بَعْضُ الْمَشَائِحِ عَلَى الْمُضِي مَجَازًا وَقَالَ الْوُجُوبُ بِاخِرِ السَّنَةِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ المُضِي لِيَتَحَقَّقَ الْإِجْتِمَاعُ فَيَتَدَاحَلُ وَعِندَ الْبَعْضِ هُوَ مَجْرِي عَلَى حَقِيقَتِهِ وَ الْوُجُوبُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ بِأَوَّلِ [?] الجماعُ بِمُجَرَّدِ الْمَجِى وَالْأَصَحُ أَنَّ الْوُجُوبَ عِندَنَا فِي ابْتِدَاءِ الْحَوْلِ وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِي فِي فَيَتَحَقَّقُ الْإِجْتِمَاعُ جبَارًا بِالزَّكوة وَلَنَا أَنَّ مَا وَجَبَ بَدَلًا عَنْهُ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ إِلَّا فِى الْمُسْتَقْبَل عَلَى مَا قَرَّرْنَاهُ فَتَعَدَّرَ إِيجَابُهُ بَعْدَ مُضِي الْحَوْلِ فَأَوْجَبْنَا هَا فِي أَوَّلِهِ وَإِنْ مَاتَ عِندَ تَمَامِ السَّنَةِ لَمْ يُؤْخَذَ مِنْهُ فِى قَوْلِهِمْ جَمِيعًا وَكَذَالِكَ إِنْ مَاتَ فِى بَعْضِ السَّنَةِ وَقِيلَ خَرَاجُ الْأَرْضِ عَلى هَذَا الخِلافِ وَقِيلَ لَا تَدَاجُلَ فِيهِ بِالْاتِفَاقِ لَهُمَا فِى الخِلافِيَّةِ أَنَّ الخَراج وَجَبَ عِوَضًا وَلَاعْوَاضُ إِذَا اجْتَمَعْتُ وَامْكَنَ اسْتِيفَاءُ هَا تُستَوفِى وَقَدْ أَمْكَنَ فِيمَا نَحْنُ فِيهِ بَعْدَ تَوَالِي السِّنِينَ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا أَسْلَمَ لَانَّهُ تَعَذَّرَ اسْتِيفَاؤُهُ
If two years accumulate on him, the two jizyas intercalate. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whoever is not taken jizya from him until the year passes and another year comes, it is not taken. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is taken from him, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i. And for Abu Hanifa: It is obligated as a punishment for persistence in kufr, as we have explained. For this reason, if he sends it by his deputy, it is not accepted in the most sound narrations; rather he is required to bring it himself and give it while standing, and the receiver takes it while sitting. In one narration: The taker grabs his collar and shakes him saying, 'Give the jizya, O dhimmi!' and some say, 'O enemy of Allah!' So it is established that it is a punishment. And punishments, when they accumulate, intercalate like the hadd penalties. And because it is obligated in lieu of killing for them and in lieu of assistance for us, as we mentioned, but for the future, not the past. Because killing is only exacted for ongoing antagonism, not past; likewise, assistance is for the future because the past has lapsed regarding it. Then the saying of Muhammad concerning jizya in al-Jami': 'and another year came' – some mashayikh interpreted it metaphorically as passing, saying obligation is at the end of the year so passage is necessary for accumulation and intercalation. According to some, it is literal; obligation according to Abu Hanifa is at the beginning of the year, so accumulation happens merely by arrival. The more correct view: obligation according to us is at the beginning of the year, and according to al-Shafi'i at the end, so accumulation is realized. By analogy to zakat. And for us: what is obligated as a substitute for something else cannot be realized except in the future, as we established, so its obligation becomes impossible after the year passes; thus we make it obligatory at its beginning. If he dies at the completion of the year, it is not taken from him in the saying of all of them. Likewise if he dies in part of the year. And it is said that kharaj of land follows this disagreement. And it is said that there is no intercalation in it by consensus. For them in the Khilafiyyah: Kharaj is obligated as compensation, and compensations when they accumulate and it is possible to collect them, they are collected. And it is possible in our case after successive years, unlike when he becomes Muslim because collection becomes impossible.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah's commentary presents two rulings on jizya. First: if two years pass without collection, the jizya for the earlier year is dropped (tadakhul) according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold it must be collected for both years. The author then explains Abu Hanifa's reasoning: jizya is a punishment (uquba) for persistently remaining in kufr, not a compensation. As a punishment, it behaves like hudud—if multiple penalties arise from the same cause, they merge. The manner of collection also shows its punitive nature: the dhimmi must bring it in person, standing, while the collector sits, and in some narrations the collector shakes him and addresses him harshly. The Sahibayn view jizya as compensation (iwad) for protection and exemption from fighting, so like any debt, multiple years' amounts accumulate and must be collected. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that the compensation intended is for future protection, not past, so collection for a past year is impossible. A related point: Muhammad's statement in Al-Jami' al-Saghir is interpreted by some scholars as referring to two full years passing; others take it literally. Second ruling: if the dhimmi dies at the end of the year or during it, the jizya for that year is dropped unanimously. The text also notes a parallel disagreement regarding kharaj (land tax) but says some consider it different by consensus because kharaj is a compensation.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): Intercalation: when multiple obligations of the same type accumulate, they merge into one obligation.
جزیہ (jizyah): A head tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in an Islamic state as a condition of their protection and exemption from military service.
عقوبہ (uqubah): Punishment; here specifically a penal payment designed to deter or penalize the continued state of kufr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens if a dhimmi does not pay jizya for two consecutive years and the second year ends?
A) He must pay jizya for both years.
B) He must pay jizya for only the second year; the first year's jizya is dropped.
C) He is executed.
D) He is given a choice to pay or convert.

Key Takeaway
Jizya intercalates in the Hanafi school because it is classified as a punishment; if multiple years pass without collection, only the most recent year's jizya is due.

What Does Not Break the Dhimmi Covenant
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute on four actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a dhimmi's covenant is broken by four specific actions and distinguish the Shafi'i objection regarding insulting the Prophet.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's covenant is not broken by refusing jizya, killing a Muslim, insulting the Prophet, or adultery with a Muslim woman.

This passage presents a clear Hanafi position on the stability of the dhimmi covenant. While common sense might suggest that serious crimes or insults would void the agreement, the Hanafi school argues that the covenant is grounded in the original undertaking of jizya, not subsequent actions. The text also engages with Imam al-Shafi'i's counterargument that insulting the Prophet should break the covenant, using a detailed qiyas that highlights key differences in usul between the schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the four actions listed in the text and the ruling: the covenant is not broken by any of them.
The four actions are: refusing jizya, killing a Muslim, insulting the Prophet, and adultery with a Muslim woman.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees specifically on the action of insulting the Prophet; he holds that it does break the covenant.
He does not object to the other three actions – his ikhtilaf is limited.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i uses an analogy: just as a Muslim's faith is broken by insulting the Prophet, so too a dhimmi's aman (covenant) should break because it stands in place of faith.
The phrase in the text: 'since the covenant of dhimma stands in place of it (faith)'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the dhimmi's original disbelief (kufr) did not prevent the covenant; therefore, a new act of disbelief (like insult) also does not void it.
Key insight: the covenant is built despite kufr, so subsequent kufr cannot destroy what already existed.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafis do not consider the covenant invalid; but they may execute the dhimmi for public cursing as a separate punishment. Shafi'is consider the covenant automatically broken.
The Urdu commentary elaborates on execution for public cursing, citing hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و مَنِ امْتَنَعَ مِنَ الجزيةِ أوْقَتَلَ مُسْلِمًا أَوْسَب النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ اَوْزَنَى بِمُسْلِمَةٍ لَمْ يَنْتَقِضُ عَهْدُهُ لِأَنَّ الْغَايَةَ الَّتِي يَنتَهِي بِهَا الْقِتَالُ الْتِرَامُ الْجِزْيَةِ لَا أَدَاؤُهَا وَالالْتِرَامُ بَاقِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ سَبُّ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ يَكُونُ نَقُضًا لأنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَ مُسْلِمًا يَنقُضُ إِيْمَانُهُ فَكَذَا يَنقُضُ اَمَانُهُ إِذْهَقُدُ الدَّمَّةِ خَلْفٌ عَنْهُ وَلَنَا أَن سَب النَّبِي عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ كَفَرمَنَهُ وَالْكُفْرُ المُقَارِنُ لا يَسُعُهُ فَالطَّارى لا يَرْفَعُهُ.
ترجمہ اور جس ذمی نے جزیہ دینے سے انکار کیا یا اس نے کسی مسلمان کو قتل کیا یا رسول اللہ کو برا کہا یا کسی مسلمان عورت سے زنا کیا تو ان کاموں سے اس کے ذمی ہو کر رہنے کا معاہدہ ختم نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قتال کی آخری حد یہ ہو جاتی ہے کہ وہ کافرسرنگوں ہو کر اپنے اوپر جزیہ دینے کو لازم کر لے۔ اس کا ادا کرنا اس کی آخری حد نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے جس جزیہ کے دینے کو اس نے اپنے اوپر لازم کیا ہے وہ ابھی باقی ہے۔ اور امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ رسول اللہ کو برا کہنا اس ذمی کی طرف سے وعدہ خلافی اور عہد شکنی ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اگر وہ مسلمان ہو کر ایسی بات کرتا ہے تو اس کا ایمان ختم ہو جاتا ۔ پس اسی طرح اس ذمی کا بھی امان ختم ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ امان کا عہد ایمان کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ کو برا کہنا اس کی جانب سے کفر ہے اور ذمی بنانے کے وقت جو کفر اس کے اندر تھا وہ اس کے ذمی بنے میں حائل نہیں ہوا تو یہ کفر جو اس کو بعد میں لگا ہے وہ بھی اس کے ذمہ کے وعدہ کو ختم نہیں کرے گا۔ تشريح وَ مَنِ امْتَنَعَ مِنَ الْجِزْيَة .. الخ مذکورہ باتوں سے بھی کا معاہدہ ختم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس سے معاہدہ ختم ہو جائے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ کو برا کہنے سے جس طرح ایک مسلمان کا ایمان ختم ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح ذمی کالامان بھی ختم ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ امان کا عہد ایمان کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو برا کہنا اس کی جانب سے کفر ہے۔ اور ڈمی بنانے کے وقت جو کفر اس کے اندر لگا تھا وہ ذمی بننے کے لئے مانع نہیں ہوا تو یہ کفر جو بعد میں اس پر طاری ہوا ہے وہ ذمی کے معاہدہ کو ختم نہیں کرے گا۔ میں متر جم کہتا ہوں کہ ذمی کا معاہدہ کرتے وقت جو کفر تھا وہ اس کے اعتقاد کی وجہ سے تھا۔ مگر موجودہ کفر مسلمانوں کے اعتقاد کی تو میں کرنے سے ہے۔ لہذا ایسے موذی شخص کو قتل کرنا ہی اولی ہے اور در امنفی میں ہے کہ یہ حکم اس صورت میں ہے کہ وہ رسول اللہ کے متعلق برے کلمات کو علانیہ نہ کہے۔ کیونکہ اگر اس نے اعلانیہ کہایا اس کی عادت بنالی تو اسے قتل کر دینا چاہئے ۔ اگر چہ وہ عورت ہی ہو ۔ اسی حکم پر اس زمانہ میں فتوی دیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ ردالمختار میں ہے اور حدیث میں ہے کہ جب کعب بن اشرف نے رسول اللہ کی ہجو کی جو کہ مدینہ کا یہودی تھا تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ کعب بن اشرف کے واسطے کون ہے۔ یہ سن کر محمد ابن مسلمہ نے عرض کیا کہ یا رسول اللہ اس کے لئے میں کافی ہوں ۔ بالآ خر اسے قتل کر دیا۔ جیسا کہ اس کی روایت بخاری نے کی ہے۔ اس طرح ابورافع کے قتل کا قصہ بھی بخاری نے روایت کیا ہے۔ اسی طرح ابن الخطل کو اس کے ہجو کرنے کے جرم میں آپ نے قتل کرا دیا۔ اسی طرح ایک زبر دست شخص رسول اللہ کی برائی کرتا پھرتا تھا تو اسے حضرت خالد بن ولید نے قتل کر دیا۔ اور عبدالرزاق رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے روایت کی ہے کہ ایک شخص آپ کی برائی کرتا تھا اسے حضرت زبیر نے قتل کر دیا۔ اسی طرح رسول اللہ نے حضرت علی وزبیر کو ایک ہجو کرنے والے کی طرف بھیجا۔ انہوں نے اسے قتل کر دیا اور ابن سعد وابن عسا کرنے روایت کی ہے کہ مہاجر بن ابی امیہ جو حضرت ابو بکر کی طرف سے یمن کا حاکم تھا اسے خبر ملی کہ یہاں ایک عورت ایسی ہے جو رسول اللہ کی ہجو کا گیت گاتی ہے۔ اس پر مہاجر نے اسے پکڑ کر اس کا ہاتھ کاٹ لیا اور اس کے دانت تو ز دیے۔ جب یہ خبر حضرت ابوبگر کو پہنچی تو فرمایا کہ اگر تم ایسا کر کے نہ آتے تو میں تم کو ہی یہ حکم دیتا کہ اس عورت کو قتل کر دو۔ اور ابوداؤ دو النسائی نے ابو برزہ الاسلمی سے روایت کی ہے کہ میں حضرت ابو بکڑ کے پاس آیا۔ اس وقت آپ نے ایک شخص سے کچھ پختی سے کلام کیا تھا۔ اس نے جواب میں آپ کو برا بھلا کہا تو میں نے عرض کیا اے خلیفہ رسول اللہ آپ مجھے اجازت دیں کہ میں اس منافق کی گردن ماردوں۔ تو فرمایا کہ تم بیٹھے جاؤ کہ رسول اللہ کے سوا کسی دوسرے کو اس کا حق نہیں ہے یہ اور بیہقی نے اس کی روایت اور اس کی تصیح بھی کی ہے۔ اور معینی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ جو شخص رسول اللہ کی بد گوئی کرے میں اس کے قتل کا فتوی دوں گا اور اس کے قریب ابن الہام رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا قول ہے اور یہی قول امام مالک واحمد و احمق و شافعی و غیر هم رحمہم اللہ کا ہے۔ اور ابن المنذر نے کہا ہے کہ عامہ علماء کا یہی قول ہے۔ شیخ ابن الہام رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ ذمی سے جزیہ لے کر اس کا قتل اس وقت تک نہیں ہو گا جب تک کہ وہ عاجزی کے ساتھ ادا کرتار ہے۔ اور جیسے ہی وہ برائی اور بد گوئی کرے گا تو اس کا یہ عمل مسلمانوں کے خلاف سرکشی و تکبر ہو گا۔ اس لئے اس کا قتل مباح ہو جائے گا۔ وطن اھوالحق واللہ تعالی اعلم۔
And whoever refuses jizya, or kills a Muslim, or insults the Prophet (peace be upon him), or commits adultery with a Muslim woman, his covenant is not broken, because the goal that ends fighting is the undertaking of jizya, not its payment, and the undertaking remains. And al-Shafi'i said: Insulting the Prophet (peace be upon him) is a breach, because if he were a Muslim, it would break his faith, so likewise it breaks his aman, since the covenant of dhimma stands in place of it (faith). And our proof is that insulting the Prophet (peace be upon him) is disbelief from him, and the original disbelief did not prevent him (from being a dhimmi), so the subsequent one does not remove it.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with inter-madhhab dispute. The text states the Hanafi position that four actions by a dhimmi do not invalidate his covenant of protection (ʿahd al-dhimma): (1) refusing to pay jizya, (2) killing a Muslim, (3) insulting the Prophet ﷺ, and (4) committing adultery with a Muslim woman. The reasoning for jizya refusal is that the purpose of fighting is the dhimmi's undertaking to pay jizya, not the actual payment; his undertaking remains valid. Imam al-Shafiʿī disagreed specifically on insulting the Prophet, arguing that just as a Muslim's insult breaks his faith (imān), a dhimmi's insult breaks his amān (covenant of security), since the dhimmi covenant substitutes for faith. The Hanafi response is that the dhimmi's original disbelief (kufr) when the covenant was made did not prevent the covenant; therefore, any new disbelief (like insulting the Prophet) also does not break it. The Urdu commentary adds that although the covenant technically remains, if the dhimmi publicly curses the Prophet habitually, he should be executed, citing numerous hadith and later fatwa positions from al-Radd al-Mukhtar. This highlights the complexity: the original ruling preserves the covenant, but later jurisprudence allows execution for public insolence to prevent fitna.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection of an Islamic state with a covenant of security.
جزية (jizya): A tax levied on dhimmis in return for protection and exemption from military service.
عهد (ʻahd): The covenant of protection granted to a dhimmi, synonymous with amān.
نقض (naqḍ): Breach or invalidation of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in this passage, what happens if a dhimmi refuses to pay jizya?
A) His covenant is immediately broken and he becomes a harbi.
B) His covenant is not broken because the undertaking to pay remains.
C) He is killed immediately.
D) He is imprisoned until he pays.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a dhimmi's covenant is not invalidated by any of the four listed actions, including insulting the Prophet, though public cursing warrants execution.

When the Dhimmi Covenant Is Broken
Ruling on the only conditions that void the dhimmi's covenant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two exclusive conditions that break a dhimmi's covenant and explain the legal rationale (ʿillah) based on the contract's purpose.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's covenant is void only by joining Dar al-Harb or fighting Muslims; lesser acts do not break it.

This lesson examines the precise limits of the dhimmi contract. The matn lays down an exclusive list: only relocation to hostile territory or taking up arms nullifies the covenant. The Hanafi proof uses the contract's purpose—preventing war—to argue that these two actions render the contract futile. Understanding this ruling prevents overextension: not every crime or sin voids the pact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exclusive conditions
The matn states that the covenant 'is not broken except' by two specific acts. List them: joining Dar al-Harb or fighting Muslims. Note that the language implies exclusivity (إِلَّا).
The word 'يَنقُصُ' in the OCR is likely 'يَنْتَقِضُ' (broken).
2
Understand the legal rationale (ʿillah) from the text
The text says the dhimmi becomes harbī, and the contract's benefit (repelling war) is lost. This is a qiyās: the covenant ceases because its purpose is defeated.
The ʿillah is the dhimmi's transformation into an enemy, making the contract's objective unachievable.
3
Apply the exclusivity principle
Since the ruling is exhaustive, any other act (e.g., insulting Islam, refusing jizya, murder) does not break the covenant. Distinguish between voiding the covenant and other legal consequences.
A dhimmi may be punished for crimes, but his protected status remains unless one of the two conditions is met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالَ وَلَا يَنقُصُ الْعَهْدُ إِلَّا وَأَنْ تَلْتَحِقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ أَوْ يَعْلَمُونَ عَلَى مَوْضِعِ فَيُحَارِ بُوْنَنَا لِأَنَّهُمْ صَارُ وَ احَرُبًا عَلَيْنَا فَيَعْرُى عَقْدُ الزِّمَّةِ عَنِ الْفَائِدَةِ وَهُوَ دَفَعُ شَرِ الْحِرَابِ
ترجمہ ... قال ولا ينقض العهد..... الخ اور ذمی کا عہد ختم نہیں ہو گا مگر صرف اسی صورت میں کہ و ہ دار الحرب میں واپس چلا جائے یا ذمیوں کی حمایت کے ساتھ کسی علاقہ میں جتھا بندی کر کے مسلمانوں سے لڑے ۔ وہ جب ہمارے مقابلہ میں آگئے تو ان کے ذمی بن کر رہنے کارندہ بے فائدہ ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ یہ معاہدہ تو اس لئے کیا گیا تھا کہ لڑائی کی برائی اور اس کا فتنہ ختم ہو۔
He said: The covenant is not broken except that he joins Dar al-Harb, or they [the dhimmis] take up a position and fight against us, because they become harbi against us, so the contract of dhimma becomes devoid of benefit, and it is to repel the evil of war.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This is a ruling stating the exclusive conditions for the termination of a dhimmi's covenant. The text, from the matn, states two scenarios: (1) the dhimmi physically relocates to Dar al-Harb (territory of war), effectively abandoning the protection of the Islamic state; (2) the dhimmis collectively organize and take up arms against Muslims. In either case, they become harbi (enemy combatants), rendering the dhimma contract useless because its entire purpose was to prevent the harm of warfare. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the covenant is not broken by any lesser act; only these two situations nullify it. Note that the verb in the Arabic is likely 'yanquḍu' (is broken) though written as 'yanquṣu' (decreases) in the OCR; the meaning is clear from the context. The legal rationale (ʿillah) is that these actions make the dhimmi a de facto enemy, so the contract loses its benefit.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory not under Muslim rule and with which a state of war exists.
حربي (ḥarbī): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims, not protected by a covenant.
عقد الذمة (ʻaqd al-dhimma): The contract of protection granted to dhimmis, obligating them to pay jizya and obey Islamic law in exchange for safety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is necessary for a dhimmi's covenant to be broken?
A) He commits a major sin like murder.
B) He refuses to pay jizya.
C) He joins Dar al-Harb or fights against Muslims.
D) He insults the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's covenant is only void by physically joining enemy territory or engaging in armed combat against Muslims; all other offenses leave the covenant intact.

Kharaj on Clients of Banu Taghlib: Single or Double?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on double vs. single kharaj for a client of Banu Taghlib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the kharaj of a client of Banu Taghlib, explain Zufar's opposing argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response distinguishing between leniencies and prohibitions.

Core Idea
A client is not joined to his original in leniencies; double kharaj is a leniency, so single applies.

This passage addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: does a client (mawla) of a Taghlibi pay double or single kharaj? The ruling hinges on whether the double tax is a leniency (takhfif) and whether clientship transfers leniencies. We'll follow the Hanafi reasoning and its rejection of Zufar's analogy to the Hashimi client's prohibition of sadaqa.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the client of a Taghlibi pays single kharaj, like the client of a Qurayshi.
The Hanafi school holds that the double is not imposed.
2
Identify Zufar's opposing view and proof
Zufar argues for double, citing the hadith 'The client of a people is from among them' and analogizing to the Hashimi client joined in sadaqa prohibition.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Zufar (a Hanafi) disagrees with Abu Hanifa.
3
Extract the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the double tax is a leniency (takhfif) — it lacks the humiliation of regular jizya. In leniencies, the client is not joined to the original. Evidence: jizya is imposed on a Muslim's Christian freed slave, showing no joining.
Leniencies are not transferred through clientship.
4
Distinguish between leniencies and prohibitions
Prohibitions (like sadaqa) transfer due to shubha (doubt) and honor. The Hashimi client joins in the sadaqa prohibition because prohibitions are established by doubt, not because of leniency. This does not apply to financial obligations like kharaj.
This distinction is key: prohibitions transfer, leniencies do not.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: single vs. double tax. The mufta bihi position is single, as preferred by the majority of Hanafis and Al-Hidayah.
Tarjih: the Hanafi position (single) is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُوضَعُ عَلَى مَوْلَى التَّغْلِبِي الْخَرَاجُ أَي الْجِزْيَةُ وَخَرَاجُ الْأَرْضِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ مَوْلَى الْقُرَشِي وَقَالَ زُفَرُ يُضَاعَفْ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَام إِنَّ مَوْلَى الْقَوْمِ مِنْهُمُ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ مَوْلَى الْهَاشِمِي يُلْحَقُ بِهِ فِي حَقِّ حُرْمَةِ الصَّدَقَةِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ هَذَا تَخْفِيفٌ وَالْمَوْلَى لَا يُلْحَقُ بِالْأَصْلِ فِيهِ وَلِهَذَا تُوضَعُ الْجِزْيَةَ عَلَى مَوْلَى الْمُسْلِمِ إِذَا كَانَ نَصْرَانِياً بِخِلَافٍ حُرْمَةِ الصَّدَقَةِ لِأَنَّ الْحُرُمَاتِ تَنْبُتُ بِالشُّبُهَاتِ فَالْحِقَ الْمَوْلَى بِالْهَاشِمِي فِى حَقِّهِ وَلَا يَلْزَمُ مَوْلَى الْغَنِيّ لَا حُرْمَةَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّدَقَةُ لِأَنَّ الْغَنِي مِنْ أَهْلِهَا وَإِنَّمَا الْغِنَى مَانِعُ وَلَمْ يُوْجَدْ فِي حَقِّ الْمَوْلَى أَمَّا الْهَاشِمِي فَلَيْسَ بِأَهْل لِهَذِهِ الصَّلَةِ أَصْلًا لِأَنَّهُ صِينَ لِشَرَفِهِ وَكَرَامَتِهِ عَنْ أَوْسَاخِ النَّاسِ فَالْحِقَ بِهِ مَوْلَاهُترجمہ اور تغلبی کے غلاموں پر بھی جزیہ و زمین کا خراج مقرر کیا جائے گا۔ جیسے ہاشمی کے غلاموں پر مقرر کیا جاتا ہے (یعنی اگر ہاشمی نے کسی کافر غلام کو آزاد کیا تو اس پر جزیہ وخراج مقرر کیا جائے گا۔ اس طرح تغلبی کے غلاموں سے دو گنا نہیں بلکہ صرف جزیہ و خراج لیا جائے گا اور امام زفر رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ تغلبی کے مولی سے دو گنا لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ قوم کا آزاد کیا ہوا بھی اسی قوم میں سے ہوتا ہے۔ (ابوداؤد و ترمذی نے اس کی روایت کی ہے) جیسا کہ ہم یہ دیکھتے ہیں کہ صدقہ حرام ہونے میں ہاشمی کا مولی ہاشمی کے ساتھ ملا لیا جاتا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دو گنا لینے میں تخفیف ہے (یعنی اس میں ذلت کا وصف نہیں ہے بخلاف جزیہ کے کہ اس کی ادائیگی میں ذلت ہوتی ہے ) اور آزاد کیا ہوا انسان اس تخفیف میں اپنے آزاد کرنے والے کے ساتھ نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے مسلمان کے آزاد کئے ہوئے پر جبکہ وہ مثلاً نصرانی ہو جزیہ مقرر کیا جاتا ہے۔ بخلاف صدقہ حرام ہونے کے (کہ جس طرح ہاشمی پر صدقہ حرام ہوتا ہے اس کے آزاد کردہ پر بھی صدقہ حرام ہوتا ہے) کیونکہ شبہ ہو جانے سے حرمت کا ثبوت ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے حرمت کے معاملہ میں ہاشمی کے ساتھ اس کے آزاد کئے ہوئے غلام کو بھی ملا لیا گیا ہے ۔ (اب اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ مالدار شخص کے آزاد کئے ہوئے پر بھی صدقہ لینا حرام ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ اس میں بھی شبہ موجود ہے۔ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ ) مالدار کے غلام سے مقابلہ نہیں کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ در اصل مالدار پر صدقہ لینا حرام نہیں ہوتا ہے کیونکہ مالدار شخص میں صدقہ لینے کی صلاحیت موجود ہے۔ اگر چہ فی الحال اس کی مالداری کی وجہ سے اس کے لئے ممنوع ہے پس نگرمی اس کے لئے مانع ہے۔ اور اس کے آزاد کئے ہوئے میں مالداری بھی موجود نہیں ہے۔ لیکن ہاشمی میں صدقہ لینے کی صلاحیت ہی نہیں ہوتی ہے اگر چہ وہ ہاشمی بالکل ہی فقیر کیوں نہ ہو ۔ کیونکہ ہاشمی اس کی اپنی شرافت و کرامت کی وجہ سے لوگوں کے میل و کچیل سے محفوظ رکھا گیا ہے تو اس کی ساتھ اس کا آزاد کردہ غلام بھی ملا لیا گیا ہے۔
And the kharaj (jizya and land tax) is placed on the client of the Taghlibi, like the client of the Qurayshi. Zufar said: It is doubled, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'The client of a people is from among them.' Do you not see that the client of the Hashimi is joined to him in the matter of the prohibition of sadaqa? Our proof is that this is a leniency (takhfif), and the client is not joined to the original in it. Therefore, jizya is placed on the client of a Muslim if he is a Christian, unlike the prohibition of sadaqa, because prohibitions are established by doubts (shubuhat). So the client is joined to the Hashimi in that right. And it does not apply to the client of a wealthy person: there is no prohibition of sadaqa on him, because the wealthy person is a potential recipient; only wealth prevents it. But in the case of the client, that prevention does not exist. As for the Hashimi, he is not a potential recipient at all, because he is preserved from the impurities of people due to his nobility and honor. So his client is joined to him. Translation: And kharaj (jizya and land tax) will be imposed on the clients of Taghlib, just as it is imposed on the clients of Hashim (i.e., if a Hashimi frees a Christian slave, jizya and kharaj are imposed on him). Similarly, from the clients of Taghlib, double is taken, but Imam Zufar said: double will be taken from the client of Taghlib. Because the Messenger of Allah said: 'The client of a people is from among them.' As we see that the client of a Hashimi is joined to him in the prohibition of sadaqa. Our proof is that in taking double there is leniency (i.e., it does not have the attribute of humiliation, unlike jizya where there is humiliation). The freed person is not joined to his manumitter in this leniency. Therefore, jizya is imposed on a Muslim's freed slave if he is Christian. Unlike the prohibition of sadaqa (just as sadaqa is prohibited on a Hashimi, it is also prohibited on his client), because prohibitions are established by doubts. So in the matter of prohibition, the client is joined to the Hashimi. (But if it is said: it should also be prohibited to take sadaqa from the client of a wealthy person because there is a doubt, then the answer is:) The client of a wealthy person is not analogous, because taking sadaqa from a wealthy person is not inherently prohibited; he is a potential recipient, only wealth prevents it. That prevention does not exist in his client. But the Hashimi is not a potential recipient at all, even if he is poor, because he is protected from the filth of people due to his honor and nobility. So his client is joined to him.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage discusses the kharaj (land tax and jizya) rate for a client (mawla) of Banu Taghlib. The Hanafi position states that such a client pays single kharaj, not double, analogous to the client of a Qurayshi. Zufar argues for double, using the hadith that a client is from among his people, citing that a client of a Hashimi is treated like Hashimi regarding the prohibition of sadaqa. The Hanafi response distinguishes between leniencies (takhfif) and prohibitions. The double tax is a leniency (it lacks the humiliation of jizya), and in leniencies, the client is not joined to the original. However, prohibitions (like sadaqa) are established by doubts, so the client is joined to the Hashimi in prohibition. Thus, the client of Taghlibi pays single, not double.

Key Terms
مولى (mawla): Client or freed slave; here specifically a non-Muslim freed by a Taghlibi.
خراج (kharaj): Land tax and poll tax combined, imposed on non-Muslims.
تخفيف (takhfif): Leniency; absence of humiliation in the payment.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity; used here to explain why prohibitions transfer through clientship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key principle that leads the Hanafi school to rule that a client of a Taghlibi pays single kharaj instead of double?
A) The client is not considered part of the tribe for any ruling.
B) The double tax is a leniency, and leniencies are not transferred through clientship.
C) The hadith about clientship is weak and cannot be used.
D) The client is a Muslim and thus exempt from kharaj.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, leniencies (takhfif) are not transferred through clientship, unlike prohibitions (hurmat) which are transferred due to doubt (shubha).

Expenditure of Public Treasury Funds on Muslim Welfare
Ruling on spending kharaj, jizya, and gifts from enemies on the interests of Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories of public treasury revenue and explain how the Imam must spend them on specified welfare projects.

Core Idea
Public treasury funds from kharaj, jizya, and gifts must be spent on Muslim welfare; stipends are gifts, not debts.

This passage from Al-Hidayah specifies the mandatory expenditures from bayt al-mal revenues. It lists which funds are included, how they must be spent, and why stipends (ata') are considered gifts rather than debts, with important practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify revenue sources
Locate the four categories of revenue mentioned: kharaj (land tax), wealth of Banu Taghlib, gifts from enemies (ahl al-harb), and jizya (poll tax). These all enter the public treasury.
Banu Taghlib is a Christian Arab tribe; their tax is double jizya but treated like kharaj.
2
List mandated expenditures
Read the list: strengthening frontiers (sadd al-thughur), building bridges and canals, salaries for judges, officials, and scholars, and stipends for combatants and their children.
The list is not exhaustive but indicates categories of public welfare.
3
Understand the rationale
The passage argues that if these essential workers are not paid, they would neglect their duties to seek livelihood. The wealth came without fighting, so it is reserved for public welfare.
This is a rational (aqli) proof for mandatory allocation.
4
Analyze the nature of 'ata' (stipend)
Notice that the stipend is called a gift (silat) not a debt (dayn). Therefore, it is not owed; if the recipient dies mid-year, no payment is made to heirs.
This differentiates a stipend from a salary or wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَا جَبَاهُ الْإِمَامُ مِنَ الْخَرَاجِ وَمِنْ أَمْوَالِ بَنِى تَغْلِبِ وَمَا أَهْدَاهُ أَهْلُ الْحَرْبِ إِلَى الْإِمَامِ وَالْجِزْيَةِ يُصْرَفُ فِى مَصَالِحِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ كَسَدِّ التُّعُورِ وَبِنَاءُ الْقَنَاطِيرِ وَالْجُسُورِ وَيُعْطَى قُضَاةُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَعُمَّالُهُمْ وَعُلَمَانُهُمْ مِنْهُ مَا يَكْفِيهِمْ وَيُدْفَعُ مِنْهُ أَرْزَاقُ الْمُقَاتِلَةِ وَذَرَارِيهِمْ لِأَنَّهُ مَالُ بَيْتِ الْمَالِ فَإِنَّهُ وَصَلَ إِلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ مِنْ غَيْرِ قِتَالٍ وَهُوَ مَعَدُّ لِمَصَالِحِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَهَؤُلَاءِ عُمَّالُهُمْ وَنَفَقَةُ الذَّرَارِي عَلَى الْآبَاءِ فَلَوْ لَمْ يُعْطَوْا كِفَايَتَهُمْ لَاشْتَغَلُوا بِالْإِحْسَابِ وَلَا يَفْرُغُونَ لِلْقِتَالِوَ مَنْ مَاتَ فِي نِصْفِ السَّنَةِ فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُ مِنَ الْعَطَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ نَوْعُ صِلَةٍ وَلَيْسَ بِدَيْنٍ وَلِهَذَا سُمِّيَ عَطَاءً فَلَا يُمْلَكُترجمہ کہا اور امام المسلمین نے جو کچھ کہ خراج و اموال بنی تغلب اور ہدیہ اہل حرب سے اور جزیہ سے جمع کیا ہے۔ اسے وہ امام عام مسلمانوں کی مصلحتوں میں خرچ کرے جیسے دار الاسلام کی سرحدوں کو شکروں سے مضبوط کرنا ، اور دریاؤں و نہروں کے پل بنانا اور مسلمانوں کے قاضیوں و عاملوں اور علماء کو ان کی ضرورت کے مطابق دینا۔ کیونکہ یہ سب بیت المال کا مال ہے۔ اور مسلمانوں کو کسی جہاد اور قتال کے بغیر حاصل ہوا ہے۔ (بیت المال کا انتظام اس لئے کیا جاتا ہے اور اس قسم کا مال وہاں رکھا جاتا ہے کہ تمام مسلمانوں کی مصلحتوں میں کام آئے۔ اوپر میں جتنے کام اور مدیں ذکر کی گئیں یہ سب مسلمانوں کے ہی کام میں آتی ہیں اور مسلمانوں کے واسطے وہ کام کرتے ہیں ۔ چونکہ کام کرنے والوں کے بال بچوں کا خرچ بھی ان کے باپ پر لازم ہوتا ہے۔ اب اگر ان لوگوں کو بیت المال سے ان کے ضروری اخراجات کیلئے نہ دیا جائے تو وہ اپنی ضرورت پوری کرنے کے لئے آمدنی کی دوسری صورتیں اختیار کرنے میں مشغول ہوں گے اور قتال و جہاد کیلئے فارغ نہ ہو سکیں گے ۔ اور مصنف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کی تجنیس کی روایت کے مطابق طالب علم بھی اس میں داخل ہیں)۔ جو سال کے درمیان فوت ہو جائے اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں
He said: And what the Imam collects from kharaj, from the wealth of Banu Taghlib, and what the people of war give as gifts to the Imam, and the jizya, is spent on the interests of the Muslims, such as strengthening the frontiers, building bridges and aqueducts. And the judges of the Muslims, their officials, and their scholars are given from it what suffices them. And from it are given the stipends of the combatants and their children, because it is the wealth of the treasury; indeed it came to the Muslims without fighting, and it is reserved for the interests of the Muslims. And these are their workers, and the expenses of the children are on the fathers; if they were not given their sufficiency, they would busy themselves with earning a livelihood and would not be free for fighting. And whoever dies in the middle of the year, he has nothing from the stipend, because it is a type of gift and not a debt. Therefore it is called 'ata' (gift), so it is not owned. Translation: He said: And whatever the Imam of the Muslims collects from kharaj, the wealth of Banu Taghlib, the gifts from the people of war, and from jizya – the Imam should spend it on the general welfare of the Muslims, like strengthening the borders of Dar al-Islam with forts, building bridges over rivers and canals, and giving to the judges, officials, and scholars of the Muslims according to their need. Because all this is wealth of the treasury. And it came to the Muslims without any jihad and fighting. (The treasury is managed and this type of wealth is placed there so that it may be used for the welfare of all Muslims. The works and expenditures mentioned above are all for the benefit of Muslims and for those who work for them. Since the expenses of the children of the workers are also obligatory on the fathers, if these people are not given from the treasury for their essential expenses, they will occupy themselves with other means of income to fulfill their needs and will not be free for fighting and jihad. According to the author's narration from Tajnis, scholars are also included in this.) And whoever dies in the middle of the year has nothing due from the stipend.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage lists the categories of revenue that belong to the public treasury (bayt al-mal) and specifies their expenditure. The funds include kharaj (land tax), jizya (poll tax), the special tax from Banu Taghlib, and gifts from hostile non-Muslims to the Imam. These are to be spent on the interests of Muslims: maintaining forts (thughur) on the frontiers, building bridges, paying salaries for judges, government officials, and scholars, and providing stipends for fighters and their dependents. The reasoning is that this wealth is acquired without fighting and is designated for public welfare. If these essential functionaries are not paid, they would have to seek livelihoods instead of focusing on their duties, including jihad. Additionally, if a stipend recipient dies mid-year, the stipend is not paid for the remainder, as it is a gift (ata') not a debt.

Key Terms
خراج (kharaj): Land tax collected from non-Muslims and also from conquered lands.
جزیہ (jizya): Poll tax on non-Muslim dhimmis.
عطاء ('ata'): Stipend given to combatants and officials from the treasury; considered a gift, not a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a combatant dies in the middle of the year, what happens to his stipend according to this passage?
A) It is given to his heirs.
B) It is not paid because it is a gift, not a debt.
C) It is paid for the full year.
D) It is given to his family.

Key Takeaway
Public treasury funds from non-combat sources must be spent on Muslim welfare, and stipends are discretionary gifts, not debts.

The Earnings of a Male Apostate: Inheritance or Fay'?
States the rulings on a male apostate's earnings before and after apostasy with tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the earnings of a male apostate, distinguish between pre- and post-apostasy property, and evaluate the evidence from the Companions and the hadith.

Core Idea
A male apostate's earnings are split: pre-apostasy wealth is inherited, post-apostasy wealth is fay' for the treasury.

When a Muslim man apostatizes and dies or is executed in that state, what happens to his property? Is it inherited by his Muslim family, or does it go to the state as spoils? The Hanafi school, through Imam Abu Hanifa, makes a crucial distinction based on when the property was earned. This lesson unpacks that ruling, the disagreements within the school and with Imam al-Shafi'i, and the reasoning that makes Abu Hanifa's view the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the two categories of property: earnings before apostasy (inheritance for Muslim heirs) and earnings after apostasy (fay' for the treasury). Understand the key principle: attribution to the period of Islam is only possible for pre-apostasy earnings.
This is the mufta bihi view.
2
Identify the opposing views
Know that Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold all property is inherited, and Imam al-Shafi'i holds all property becomes fay'. Understand their respective bases: Sahibayn rely on continued ownership despite apostasy; Shafi'i relies on the hadith 'A Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever' and the fact that the apostate dies in kufr.
Sahibayn's view is intra-Hanafi; Shafi'i is inter-madhhab.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to Shafi'i's proof
See how the Hanafi school reconciles the conflicting evidence: the ijma' of the Companions (based on Ali's action) applies to pre-apostasy earnings, while Shafi'i's hadith applies to post-apostasy earnings. This removes contradiction while respecting both proofs.
Each proof is assigned to its proper domain.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Compare the outcomes: Abu Hanifa gives Muslim heirs only the pre-apostasy wealth; Sahibayn give them all; Shafi'i gives none. Understand how this affects estate distribution.
The difference is significant for heirs.
5
Apply the tarjih reasoning
Explain why Abu Hanifa's view is preferred: it reconciles all evidence, avoids contradiction, and is supported by the practice of the Companions. This tarjih establishes the mufta bihi position.
Tarjih is based on synthesis, not rejection of other proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب السير
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد ہفتم تو اس کے مرتد ہونے سے پہلے موجود تھی ۔ اور ارتداد کی کمائی کو اس طرح منسوب کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ اس کے مرتد ہونے سے پہلے موجود نہ تھی۔ حالانکہ منسوب اور مستند ہونے کے لئے یہ شرط ہے کہ اس وقت بھی موجود ہو۔
تشریح اگر کسی مرتد کو حالت ارتداد میں موت آگئی یا وہ ( مرتد ) بوجہ ارتداد کے قتل کیا گیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے موقف کے بموجب حالت اسلام میں بذریعہ اکتساب ( کمائی) حاصل شدہ مال مسلمان ورثاء کو بطور وراثت ملے گا۔ جب کہ حالت ارتداد میں کمایا ہوا مال مال غنیمت متصور ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ حالت اسلام کی کمائی حالت ارتداد سے پہلے کی طرف منسوب ہوگی اور یہ ممکن ہے اور بعد از ارتداد کی کمائی کو پہلے کی طرف منسوب کرنا ممکن نہیں اس لئے بعد از ردت کمایا ہوا مال غنیمت ہوگا ۔ صاحبین کے ہاں مرتد کا مال میراث متصور ہوگا کہ یہ مال مرتد کی ملکیت میں ہے امام شافعی کے ہاں مرتد کا کمایا ہوا مال بصورت موت یا قتل مال غنیمت شمار ہوگا اس لئے کہ مرتد کی موت حالت کفر میں ہوئی ہے۔
مرتد کے کمائے ہوئے مال کے بارے میں صاحبین (امام ابو یوسف ، امام محمد ) کا موقف ہو یا امام شافعی کی رائے امام ابو حنیفہ کے موقف کے مد مقابل مرجوح ہیں۔ کیونکہ مرتد کے مال پر زوال ملکیت کا تحقق ( ثبوت) ہوتا ہے ، چنانچہ مرتد نے بحالت اسلام اور قبل از ارتداد جو مال بذریعہ اکتساب ( کمائی ) حاصل کیا وہ مسلمان ورثاء کے لئے میراث متصور ہوگا۔ اور حضرت علی کے اقدام پر مبنی اجماع صحابہ کو اسی ( قبل از ارتداد کمائے ہوئے مال ) پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ اور امام شافعی کی مستدلہ روایت ( مسلمان کافر کا وارث نہیں ) کو بعد از ارتداد بذریعہ اکتساب ( کمائی) حاصل شدہ مال پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔ اس طرح کرنے سے حضرت علی کے اقدام پر مبنی صحابہ کرام کے اجتماع اور امام شافعی کی مستدلہ روایت کے مابین تعارض رفع ہو جائے گا اور اس پر عمل کرنے میں تشابہ بھی پیدا نہ ہوگا۔ ایس ثابت ہوا کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کا موقف قابل ترجیح ہے۔
If an apostate dies in apostasy or is killed for apostasy, according to Abu Hanifa the wealth earned in Islam is inherited by Muslim heirs, while wealth earned in apostasy is considered fay'/ghanimah. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say all wealth of the apostate is inherited because it remains his property. Al-Shafi'i says all wealth earned by the apostate becomes fay' upon death or execution because he died in kufr. The positions of the two companions and al-Shafi'i are outweighed by Abu Hanifa's view because the apostate's ownership ceases. The ijma' of the Sahaba based on the action of Ali is applied to pre-apostasy earnings, while al-Shafi'i's proof (a Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever) is applied to post-apostasy earnings. Thus Abu Hanifa's view is preferable.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage discusses the fate of a male apostate's earnings. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, there is a distinction: property acquired during Islam (before apostasy) passes to his Muslim heirs as inheritance, while property acquired during apostasy becomes fay' (spoils of war) for the Muslim treasury. The reason is that the former can be attributed to his period of Islam, but the latter cannot. The two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that all property remains in his ownership and thus is inherited. Imam al-Shafi'i also disagrees, considering all property as fay' because the apostate dies in a state of disbelief. The text then provides a tarjih (preference) for Abu Hanifa's view, arguing that it reconciles the conflicting evidence: the ijma' of the Companions (based on Ali's action) is applied to pre-apostasy earnings, while the hadith 'a Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever' is applied to post-apostasy earnings. Thus Abu Hanifa's position is preferred.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who abandons Islam (apostate) by word or deed, subject to execution in Hanafi fiqh.
مال غنیمت (mal ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from enemy combatants; here applied to post-apostasy earnings of a male apostate.
صاحبین (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two principal disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens to the property earned by a male apostate after his apostasy?
A) It goes to his Muslim heirs as inheritance.
B) It goes to his non-Muslim heirs as inheritance.
C) It becomes fay' (spoils) for the Muslim treasury.
D) It remains in abeyance until he repents.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's ruling on an apostate's earnings, distinguishing pre- and post-apostasy property, harmonises the Companions' practice and the hadith, making it the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Rulings on the Female Apostate's Earnings and Inheritance
States rulings on murtaddah's earnings and when Muslim husband inherits from her.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the female apostate's earnings and inheritance, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind the difference between male and female apostates.

Core Idea
A female apostate's earnings belong to her heirs; her Muslim husband inherits only if she apostatized while ill.

This lesson examines two specific rulings from the Hanafi school regarding a woman who leaves Islam (murtaddah). The first concerns her earnings during apostasy: do they go to the state treasury or to her heirs? The second concerns whether her Muslim husband can inherit from her after her apostasy. The answers depend on a careful consideration of the sabab (cause) of fay' and the presence or absence of bad faith intent. We will explore the ta'lil (effective cause) that distinguishes the female apostate from the male.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two distinct rulings: (a) earnings of the murtaddah go to her heirs, not fay'; (b) her Muslim husband inherits from her only if she apostatized while ill (marad al-mawt). If she was healthy, he does not inherit.
The first ruling is based on absence of harb (combat), the second on intent to defraud.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof for both rulings is not a textual quote but rational reasoning (ta'lil): for earnings, because the female apostate is not a combatant (muharib), her earnings do not become fay' unlike the male apostate. For inheritance, the proof is her intent to nullify her husband's right when ill; if healthy, no right attaches because she is not executed.
The male apostate is executed, making his apostasy like death, which triggers inheritance rights.
3
Understand the ta'lil (causation)
The difference between male and female apostates lies in execution: the male is killed, so his property becomes fay' and his heirs' rights attach immediately. The female is not killed, so her property remains hers and her husband's right only attaches if she acted with bad faith (illness indicates intent to disinherit).
The illa (effective cause) for fay' is being a combatant; for inheritance it is the combination of apostasy and bad faith.
4
Apply to scenarios
Test the rulings: (a) If a healthy woman apostatizes, her husband does not inherit; (b) if a terminally ill woman apostatizes, her husband inherits despite her apostasy because the law nullifies her legal stratagem.
The ruling prevents hiyal (legal tricks) to disinherit spouses.
5
Note the thamarah (practical consequence)
The practical effect is that a Muslim husband cannot be deprived of inheritance by his wife's apostasy unless she was healthy at the time, which does not attach his right. This protects the husband's inheritance right against bad-faith apostasy.
The male apostate's property is treated as fay' and goes to the state, not his heirs, unless he reverts or is executed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُرْتَدَّةُ كَسْبُهَا وَرَتَتِهَا لِأَنَّهُ لَاحَرَابَ مِنْهَا فَلَمْ يُوجَدُ سَبَبُ الفَيِّي بِخِلَافِ الْمُرْتَدِ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ
ترجمہ اور اب مردہ عورت کا مسئلہ یہ ہوگا کہ اس کی کمائی اس کے وارثوں کی ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس کی طرف سے جنگ نہیں ہوئی ہے اس لئے ایسا کوئی سبب نہیں پایا گیا جس سے اس کی کمائی مال غنیمت ہو جائے ۔ بخلاف مرتد مرد کے کہ اس کی روت[؟] کی حالت کی کمائی امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک مال غنیمت ہے۔
حالت مرض میں عورت مرتد ہو جائے تو مسلمان خاوند وارث ہوگا
وَيَرِثُهَا زَوْجُهَا الْمُسْلِمُ إِنِ ارْتَدَّتْ وَهِيَ مَرِيضَةً لِقَصْدِهَا إِبْطَالُ حَقِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ صَحِيْحَةً لَا يَرِثُهَا لِأَنَّهَا لَا تُقْتَلُ فَلَمْ يَتَعَلَّى حَقَّهُ بِمَالِهَا بِالرِّدَّةِ بِخِلَافِ الْمُرْتَدِ
ترجمہ اور مرتدہ کا مسلمان شوہر اس کا وارث ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ یہ مرتد ہونے والی مرتد ہونے کے وقت بیمار ہو ۔ کیونکہ اس طرح اس نے اپنے شوہر کی میراث کے حق کو مٹانا چاہا ہے۔ اور اگر وہ مرتد ہونے کے وقت بیمار نہ ہو تو اس کا مسلمان شوہر اس کا وارث نہ ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ عورت قتل نہیں کی جاتی ہے۔ تو اس کے مرتد ہو جانے سے اس کے مال کے ساتھ اس کے شو ہر کا کوئی حق متعلق نہیں ہوا۔ بخلاف مرتد مرد کے یعنی چونکہ وہ مرتد ہونے سے قتل کر دیا جاتا ہے تو اس کا مرتد ہونا گو یا مر جانا ہی ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے مال سے اس کے وارثوں کا حق متعلق ہو جاتا ہے۔
And the female apostate: her earnings are for her heirs because there is no hostility from her, so the cause of fay' is not found, unlike the male apostate according to Abu Hanifa. Translation: And the matter of the female apostate is that her earnings will be for her heirs, because no war has occurred from her side, so there is no cause found by which her earnings become booty. Unlike the male apostate, because his earnings during the state of apostasy are booty according to Imam Abu Hanifah. If a woman apostatizes while ill, the Muslim husband will inherit. And her Muslim husband inherits from her if she apostatizes while she is ill, due to her intent to nullify his right. And if she was healthy, he does not inherit from her, because she is not killed, so his right does not attach to her property by apostasy, unlike the male apostate. Translation: And the Muslim husband of the female apostate will be her heir, provided that she was ill at the time of apostasy, because in this way she intended to nullify her husband's inheritance right. And if she was not ill at the time of apostasy, then her Muslim husband will not inherit from her, because women are not killed. So by her apostasy, her husband's right does not attach to her property. Unlike the male apostate, because since he is killed due to apostasy, his apostasy is like death, so the right of his heirs attaches to his property.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings concerning the female apostate (murtaddah) under Hanafi law. First: The earnings she acquires during apostasy belong to her heirs, not the state, because she is not a combatant (muharib) and thus the cause for considering them fay' (spoils) is absent. According to Abu Hanifa, this contrasts with the male apostate, whose earnings during apostasy are deemed fay' and go to the state treasury. Second: Regarding inheritance, if a woman apostatizes while she is healthy, her Muslim husband does not inherit from her. However, if she apostatizes while terminally ill (marad al-mawt), the husband does inherit, because her apostasy at that time is considered a legal stratagem (hila) to deprive him of inheritance, which Islamic law nullifies. The 'illa (effective cause) for the difference between male and female apostates is that a male apostate is executed by the state, making his apostasy akin to death, which immediately transfers rights to his estate. A female apostate is not executed, so her apostasy does not trigger similar inheritance consequences unless she is ill, indicating bad faith.

Key Terms
مُرْتَدَّة (murtaddah): A female apostate from Islam; her rulings differ from a male apostate in matters of earnings and inheritance.
فَيْء (fay'): Spoils taken from enemies without direct warfare; the male apostate's earnings are considered fay' according to Abu Hanifa.
رِدَّة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam, which triggers specific legal consequences including execution for males and loss of inheritance rights in certain cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the Muslim husband inherit from his wife who has apostatized?
A) Always, because apostasy severs marital ties.
B) Only if she apostatized while in good health.
C) Only if she apostatized while ill, to prevent a legal stratagem.
D) Never, because a female apostate's property goes to the state.

Key Takeaway
The female apostate's earnings go to her heirs, and her Muslim husband inherits only if she apostatized while ill, preventing bad-faith deprivation of inheritance.

The Apostate Who Joins Dar al-Harb: Legal Consequences and Disputes
Legal consequences of an apostate joining Dar al-Harb with inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on an apostate who joins Dar al-Harb, identify the Shafi'i objection, and distinguish between the views of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the timing of inheritance.

Core Idea
Joining Dar al-Harb transforms an apostate into a legal corpse, but only upon the qadi's decree.

The Hanafi school treats an apostate who flees to enemy territory as legally dead: his slaves are freed, debts discharged, and property given to Muslim heirs. However, this transformation is not automatic—it hinges on the qadi's confirmation. Moreover, the Shafi'i school disagrees, arguing that property should remain in suspense. Within the Hanafi school, there is further disagreement on exactly when the heirs are determined. This lesson guides you through the arguments and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the legal consequences when an apostate joins Dar al-Harb and the qadi decrees his joining: mudabbar slaves and umm walad are freed, term debts are discharged, and his property is transferred to Muslim heirs.
This ruling is from the matn of al-Hidayah.
2
Examine the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that the apostate's property should remain suspended (mawquf) because his joining is merely a prolonged absence, not death.
The Shafi'i view is based on the principle that absence does not trigger inheritance until death is confirmed.
3
Follow the Hanafi response and qiyas
The Hanafi school responds using qiyas: a harbi (enemy combatant) is like a dead person in Islamic rulings because Islamic authority (wilayat al-ilzam) is cut off. Therefore, the apostate, by becoming a harbi, is analogized to a dead person.
The qiyas is considered jali (clear) because the illa (cutting off of authority) is manifest.
4
Note the requirement of the qadi's decree
The analogy does not apply automatically; the qadi's decree is necessary because there is a possibility that the apostate may return. The decree eliminates that possibility and establishes the legal death.
Thus, without the decree, the apostate's status remains uncertain.
5
Differentiate between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf
Imam Muhammad considers the time of joining as the moment for determining heirs, while Abu Yusuf considers the time of the qadi's decree. This affects who inherits if heirs are born or die between joining and decree.
The text does not prefer one view, so both are considered transmitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب چلا گیا یا قاضی نے لحوق کا فیصلہ کر دیا تو اسکے مد بڑا مہات الا ولاداور دیون کا حکم
قَالَ وَإِن لَحِقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ مُرتَداوَ حَكَمَ الْحَاكِمُ بِلِحَاقِهِ عُتَقَ مُدَبَّرُوهُ وَامَّهَاتُ أَوْلَادِهِ وَحَلَّتِ الديونُ الَّتِي عَلَيْهِ وَ نُقِلَ مَا اكْتَسَبَهُ فِي حَالِ الْإِسْلامِ إِلَى وَرَثَتِهِ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ قَالَ الشَّافِعَى يَبْقَى مَالُهُ مَوْفُوْفًا كَمَا كَانَ لِأَنَّهُ تَرْعُ غَيْبَةٍ فَاشْةَ الْغَيْبَةَ فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلامِ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ صَارَ مُرْتَا بِاللَّحَاقِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْحَرْبِ وَهُمْ أَمْوَاتُ فِي حَقِّ أَحْكَامِ الْإِسْلامِ لِانْقِطَاعِ وِلَايَةِ الْإِلْزَامِ كَمَاهِيَ مُنقَطِعَةٌ عَنِ الْمَوْتَى فَصَارَ كَالْمَوْتِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا يَسْتَقِرُّ لِحَاقُهُ إِلَّا بِقَضَاءِ الْقَاضِي لِاِحْتِمَالِ الْعُودِ إِلَيْنَا فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ الْقَضَاءِ وَإِذَا تَقَرَّ رَمَوْتُهُ ثَبَتَ الْأَحْكَامُ الْمُتَعَلَّقَةُ وَهِيَ مَا ذَكَرْنَا هَا كَمَا فِى الْمَوْتِ الْحَقِيقِى ثُمَّ يُعْتَبَرُ كَوْنُهُ وَإِرثًا عِندَ لِحَاقِةٍ فِي قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدَ لِأَنَّ اللحَاقَ هُوَ السَّبَبُ وَالْقَضَاءُ لِتَقَرُّرِهِ لِقَطْعِ الإِحْتِمَالِ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ وَقْتُ القَضَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ مَوْنَا بِالْقَضَاءِ وَالْمُرْتَدَّةُ إِذَ الْحِقَتْ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ فَهَى عَلَى هَذَا الْخِلَاف
ترجمہ کہا اگر کوئی مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب پہنچ گیا۔ اور حاکم نے بھی اس کے پہنچ جانے کا حکم دے دیا تو اس کے مد بر غلام اور ام ولد سب آزاد ہو گئے ۔ اور اس پر جتنے (میعادی قرضے ( وقت معین تک کے ) تھے وہ اسی وقت فی الفوقا بل ادا ہو گئے ۔ اور اس نے جو کچھ حالت اسلام میں کمایا تھا وہ سب اس کے مسلمان وارثوں کی طرف منتقل ہو گئے ( اور صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک حالت ردت کی کمائی بھی وارثوں کی ہو جائے گی ۔ مف ) اور شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس کا مال اس کے ملک ہی میں رہے گا مگر بطور توقف ۔ جیسے دارالحرب میں جانے سے پہلے یہی حکم تھا ۔ کیونکہ دارالحرب میں پہنچ جانا گویا سفر میں غائب ہو جانے کے مشابہ ہے تو ایسا ہوا گویا دار الاسلام میں سفر کے لئے جاتے ہوئے غائب ہوا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ حربیوں سے مل کر مرتد ہو گیا۔ اور اسلامی احکام کے معاملہ میں حربی لوگ مردہ کے حکم میں ہوتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ ان پر کوئی بات لازم کرنے کا حق نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ کوئی بات ان پر لازم نہیں کی جاسکتی ہے۔ جیسے کہ یہ حق ایک مردہ سے ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ مگر فورا ہی اس کے دار الحرب پہنچ جانے اور وہاں کے لوگوں میں گھل مل جانے کا حکم نہیں دیا جائے گا مگر اس وقت جبکہ قاضی اس کا فیصلہ سادے اور اعلان کر دے کیونکہ اس بات کا احتمال باقی رہتا ہے کہ وہ دوبارہ واپس آ جائے ۔اس لئے قاضی کا فیصلہ ضروری ہوا۔اور جب اس کی موت یعنی دار الحرب میں منتقل ہونے کا فیصلہ اس نے سنا دیا تو اس کے مرنے پر جو احکام متعلق تھے وہ سب ثابت ہو گئے یعنی اس کے مدبر اور ام ولد کے آزاد ہونے وغیرہ کے جو احکام اوپر بیان کئے جاچکے ہیں۔ جیسے حقیقتا مر جانے میں ہوتا ہے۔ پھر امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک وارث ہونے کا اعتبار اس وقت ہوگا جبکہ وہ دار الحرب پہنچ چکا ہو ۔ کیونکہ یہی پہنچنا میراث کا سبب ہے۔ اور قاضی کا فیصلہ ہی اسے پورے طور پر ثابت کرتا ہے۔ تا کہ وہاں پہنچنے اور نہ پہنچنے کا احتمال بالکل ختم ہو کر یقین ہو جائے ۔ (حاصل یہ ہوا کہ دارالحرب میں پہنچ جانے کے وقت جو وارث پیدا ہوگا وہ بھی وارث ہوگا۔ ) اور قاضی ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ کے وقت وارث ہونے کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس مرتد کا حربیوں کے درمیان پہنچ جانا ہی قاضی کے فیصلہ سے اس کی موت کے حکم میں ہوگا۔ (اس بناء پر اس کے حربیوں کے درمیان پہنچ جانے کے بعد قاضی کے فیصلہ سے پہلے جو بچہ پیدا ہوگا وہ بھی وارث ہوگا ۔ اور اگر مردہ عورت بھاگ کر دار الحرب میں پہنچ گئی تو اس کے بارے میں بھی ایسا ہی اختلاف ہے۔ یعنی امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک قاضی کا حکم ہونے تک جو موجود ہو گا اس کا بھی وارث ہونا معتبر ہوگا۔
Ruling on an apostate who joins Dar al-Harb or the qadi decrees his joining: his mudabbar slaves and umm walads are freed, the debts due upon him are discharged, and what he earned during Islam is transferred to his Muslim heirs. Al-Shafi'i said: his wealth remains in suspense as before, because it is like absence in Dar al-Islam. Our proof: he has become a harbi (enemy combatant) by joining, and harbis are like dead in the rulings of Islam because the authority to enforce obligations is cut off from them, just as it is cut off from the dead. So it becomes like death, except that his joining is not established except by the qadi's decree due to the possibility of return. So the decree is necessary. When his death (i.e., joining) is established, the related rulings apply as in actual death. Then for inheritance, the time of joining is considered according to Muhammad, because joining is the cause, and the decree only confirms it. Abu Yusuf said: the time of the decree, because he becomes dead by the decree. If a female apostate joins Dar al-Harb, the same disagreement applies.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage deals with the legal status of an apostate who escapes to Dar al-Harb (enemy territory). The Hanafi position: once the qadi confirms his joining (lahaq), the apostate is treated like a deceased person. His mudabbar slaves (those promised freedom upon his death) and umm walads (slave mothers of his children) are freed immediately, his term debts are discharged (as they would be at death), and his wealth earned during Islam is distributed to his Muslim heirs. The Shafi'i school disagrees, holding that the apostate's property remains in abeyance (mawquf) because his absence is simply a prolonged journey, not death. The Hanafi response: a harbi is like a dead person because Islamic authority cannot enforce obligations upon him, so by analogy (qiyas), joining Dar al-Harb is like death. However, this status is not automatic; the qadi's decree is required because there is a possibility the apostate may return. Once the decree is issued, the rulings take effect retroactively? Or not? There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) considers the time of the actual joining as the moment for determining heirs, because the joining itself is the cause (sabab) of inheritance, and the qadi's decree merely confirms it. Therefore, any heir existing at the time of joining inherits. Abu Yusuf, however, considers the time of the qadi's decree as the critical moment, because the apostate legally becomes dead only by the decree. Thus, heirs existing at the time of the decree inherit even if born after the joining. The same disagreement applies if the apostate is female (murtaddah). This difference has practical implications for determining who inherits.

Key Terms
لحاق (lahaq): The act of an apostate joining Dar al-Harb; once confirmed by qadi, triggers legal consequences like death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has promised freedom upon the master's death; such slaves are freed when the apostate is deemed dead.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears her master's child; she becomes free upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, at what point are the heirs of an apostate who joins Dar al-Harb determined?
A) At the time of the qadi's decree.
B) At the time of joining Dar al-Harb.
C) At the time of apostasy.
D) At actual death.

Key Takeaway
An apostate who joins Dar al-Harb is treated as legally dead by Hanafi law, but only after the qadi's decree, and the timing of inheritance is disputed among Hanafi masters.

Paying the Apostate's Debts: Three Hanafi Narrations
Intra-Hanafi dispute on payment of apostate's debts from earnings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three narrated positions of Abu Hanifa regarding payment of an apostate's debts and apply the principle of al-ghurm bi al-ghunm to distinguish between them.

Core Idea
An apostate's debts are tied to the earnings of the same period: Islam debts from Islam earnings, apostasy debts from apostasy earnings.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a unique intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where three different narrations are attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa himself regarding how to pay an apostate's debts. The central issue is whether each debt should be paid from the earnings of the period in which it was incurred, or whether one type of earnings takes priority. Understanding this dispute sharpens our appreciation of how multiple valid proofs can coexist within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three narrations
List the three positions: (1) each debt from its period's earnings; (2) begin with Islamic earnings; (3) begin with apostasy earnings.
All three are attributed to Abu Hanifa.
2
Analyze the basis of the first narration
The text states that the first narration is based on the maxim al-ghurm bi al-ghunm (liability is tied to profit). Each debt is paid from earnings acquired during the same period as the debt, because the claimants differ and each earning is tied to the cause of the debt.
This is the most detailed explanation in the passage.
3
Analyze the basis of the second narration
The second narration begins with Islamic earnings, because those earnings are considered his property until he leaves (apostatizes).
The text cuts off here, but the reasoning is that Islamic earnings have a stronger claim as his own property.
4
Consider the third narration
The third narration reverses the order, starting with apostasy earnings.
The text does not provide its basis, but it is a valid narrated position.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi nature
This is not a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his students, but between different riwayat (narations) attributed to Abu Hanifa himself.
This shows the richness of Hanafi transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرتد مقروض کا قرض کس طرح ادا کیا جائے گا
وَ تُقْضَى الدُّيُونُ الَّتِي لَزِمَتُهُ فِي حَالِ الْإِسْلامِ مِمَّا اكْتَسَبَهُ فِي حَالِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَمَا لَزِمَتَهُ فِي حَالِ رِدَّتِهِ مِنَ الديون تُقْضَى مِمَّا اكْتَسَبَهُ فِي حَالٍ رِدَّتِهِ قَالَ الْعَبْدُ الضَّعِيفُ عَصَمَهُ اللهُ هَذِهِ رِوَايَةً عَنْ أبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَعَنْهُ أنْ تُبْدَ بِكَمْ نَهُ بِكَسْبِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَ إِنْ لَمْ يَفِ بِذَالِكَ يُقضى مِنْ كَسْبِ الرِّدَّةِ وَعَنْهُ عَلَى عَكْسِه وَجُهُ الْأَوَّلِ أَنَّ الْمُسْتَحِقَ يا مُخْتَلِفْ وَحُصُولُ كُلّ وَاحِد مِّنَ الْكَبَيْنِ بِإِعْتِبَارِ السَّبَبِ الَّذِى وَجَبَ لَهُ الدَّيْنُ فَيُقْضَى كُلُّ دَينِ مِّنَ الْمُكْتَبِ الَّذِي فِي تِلْكَ الْحَالَةِ لِيَكُونَ الْغُرُمُ بِالغَنَمِ وَجْهُ الثَّانِى أَنَّ كَسْبَ الْإِسْلَامِ مِلْكَهُ حَتَّى يُخْلِفُهُ
How the debts of an insolvent apostate will be paid: The debts that were binding upon him in the state of Islam are paid from what he earned in the state of Islam, and the debts that were binding upon him in the state of apostasy are paid from what he earned in the state of apostasy. Al-'Abd al-Da'if (may Allah protect him) said: This is a narration from Abu Hanifa. And from him (another narration): that one begins with his earnings from Islam, and if that does not suffice, then from the earnings of apostasy. And from him the opposite. The basis of the first is that the claimants are different, and the acquisition of each earning is considered according to the cause for which the debt became due, so each debt is paid from the earning of that state so that liability corresponds to gain (al-ghurm bi al-ghunm). The basis of the second: that the earnings from Islam are his property until he leaves it...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage addresses how debts of an apostate are paid when he has earnings from both the period of Islam and the period of apostasy. The text presents three positions, all attributed to Abu Hanifa (rh). The first narration: Debts incurred during Islam are paid from Islamic earnings; debts incurred during apostasy are paid from apostasy earnings. The 'illa is 'al-ghurm bi al-ghunm' (liability is tied to profit) – each debt is paid from the earnings corresponding to the period in which it was incurred. The second narration: Payment begins with Islamic earnings; if insufficient, then from apostasy earnings. The third narration: The opposite order, starting with apostasy earnings. The text then provides the wajh (basis) for the first view: the claimants are different and the earnings are tied to the cause of the debt. For the second view, it states that Islamic earnings are his property until he leaves (presumably until apostasy changes their status). The passage is incomplete at the end. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf within the narrations of Abu Hanifa himself, not between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf. The commentator notes this as a dispute and provides reasoning for each view.

Key Terms
الغرم بالغنم (al-ghurm bi al-ghunm): A legal maxim meaning 'liability is tied to profit' or 'one who bears the risk receives the gain'. Used here to justify paying debts from earnings of the same period.
كسب الإسلام (kasb al-Islam): Earnings acquired by the apostate during his state of being a Muslim.
كسب الردة (kasb al-riddah): Earnings acquired by the apostate after his apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first narration attributed to Abu Hanifa, how are debts incurred during Islam and during apostasy paid?
A) All debts are paid from Islamic earnings first.
B) Debts from Islam are paid from Islamic earnings; debts from apostasy from apostasy earnings.
C) All debts are paid from apostasy earnings first.
D) Debts are paid proportionally from all earnings.

Key Takeaway
The first Hanafi narration ties each debt to its corresponding earnings, applying the maxim al-ghurm bi al-ghunm.

The Apostate's Debts: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Payment from Earnings
Intra-Hanafi dispute on debt payment from separate earnings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the payment of an apostate's debts and explain the reasoning behind each, as well as the position of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Core Idea
An apostate's debts are tied to the cause of earnings — each narration reflects a different priority between debt, inheritance, and ownership.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over how an apostate's debts should be paid from his earnings during Islam and apostasy. Imam Abu Hanifa has three different narrations on the priority, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold a unified view. Understanding these positions reveals how Hanafi jurists balance ownership, debt obligation, and inheritance rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two periods and their earnings
The apostate has earnings during Islam and during apostasy, and may have debts incurred in each period. These earnings are distinct in terms of ownership and inheritance rights according to Abu Hanifa.
The key distinction is that earnings during apostasy are not owned by the apostate in Abu Hanifa's view, while Islamic earnings are owned.
2
State the first narration (Imam Zafar from Abu Hanifa)
Debts are paid separately from the earnings of the same period: Islamic debts from Islamic earnings, apostasy debts from apostasy earnings. The rationale is that each debt is tied to its specific cause (sabab).
This treats the two sets of earnings as completely separate pools.
3
State the second narration (Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa)
Priority is given to Islamic earnings over apostasy earnings. If Islamic earnings are sufficient, all debts are paid from them. If not, the remainder is paid from apostasy earnings. Rationale: Islamic earnings are owned by the apostate, so debt must be settled before inheritance can take effect.
Debt takes precedence over inheritance (haqq al-mawarith).
4
State the third narration (Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa)
Priority is given to apostasy earnings over Islamic earnings. If apostasy earnings are sufficient, all debts are paid from them. If not, the remainder is paid from Islamic earnings. Rationale: Islamic earnings are the right of the heirs, while apostasy earnings are purely the apostate's own right; using his own right first is more appropriate.
This reverses the priority because the apostate's own right (apostasy earnings) should be used before the heirs' right (Islamic earnings).
5
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that both earnings are owned by the apostate, so inheritance applies to both. Therefore, debts are paid from the entire property without distinguishing between periods. This is because both sets of earnings are his property and debts are paid from it.
The Sahibayn do not differentiate between the two periods; all property is treated equally.
