ترجمہ اور مرتد پر جتنے قرضے حالت اسلام میں لازم ہوئے تھے وہ اس کے اسلام کی حالت کی کمائی سے ادا کئے جائیں گے اور جو قرضے اس کے مرتد ہونے کی حالت میں لازم ہوئے تھے وہ اس کے مرتد ہونے کے زمانہ کی کمائی سے ادا کئے جائیں گے ۔ اس عبد ضعیف (مصنف) نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ ایک روایت امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے منقول ہے ( زفر رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے روایت کی ہے۔ اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ پہلے حالت اسلام کی کمائی سے ادا کرنا شروع کیا جائے ۔ پھر اگر پورے قرضوں کی ادائیگی کے لئے یہ کمائی کافی نہ ہو تب اس کی حالت ارتداد کی کمائی سے ادا کئے جائیں۔ ( یہ روایت حسن رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے ہے ) اور تیسری روایت ابوحنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے اس کے برعکس ہے۔ یعنی پہلے ارتداد کے زمانہ کی کمائی سے شروع کیا جائے ۔ پھر اگر پورے قرضے ادا نہ ہوں تو حالت اسلام کی کمائی سے ادا کئے جائیں۔ (یہ روایت امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے ہے۔ ) پہلی روایت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس پر جو کچھ دین اور باقی ہے وہ دو مختلف سببوں سے مختلف ہے۔ یعنی اسلام کے زمانہ کی کمائی کے سبب سے ان زنا اسلام لم قر ضہ واجب ہے ۔ اور ارتداد کے زمانہ کی کمائی سے ردت کا قرض باقی اور واجب الاداء ہے اس طرح دو مختلف سبوں سے اس پر دو طرح کے قرضے واجب الادا ہیں اور حالت اسلام کی کمائی اور ردت کی کمائی دونوں میں سے ہر ایک اس کو بہ اعتبار ایسے سبب کے حاصل ہوئی جس کے لئے قرض واجب ہوا ( مثلاً اسلام کی حالت میں اس نے کوئی چیز ادھار لے کر نفع سے بیچی اور حالت ردت میں اس نے مثلا شراب ادھار لے کر نفع کمایا۔ پس دونوں کمائیاں اپنے اپنے ادھار سے حاصل ہوئیں۔ جس کے سبب سے اس پر قرض لازم ہوا ) اس لئے ہر ایک قرض اس کمائی سے ادا کیا جائے گا۔ جو قرض کے وقت اس کی حالت کی کمائی ہے تا کہ قرض ادا کرنا اس کے نفع کے اعتبار سے ہو۔ اور دوسری روایت کی وجہ یہی ہے کہ حالت اسلام کی کمائی اس کی ملک ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کمائی میں اس کا وارث اس کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے یعنی میراث پاتا ہے ۔ اور ایسی قائم مقامی کی شرط یہ ہے کہ مورث ( جائیداد اور مال کے مالک) کے حق سے فارغ ہو لہذا قرض اس پر مقدم ہوگا ۔ اور حالت ارتداد کی کمائی تو وہ مرتد کی مملوک نہیں ہے کیونکہ امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک اس کے مرتد ہو جانے کی جد سے مالک ہونے کی قدرتی صلاحیت باطل ہوگئی۔ لہذا اس کی کمائی سے اس کا قرض ادا نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ البتہ اس صورت میں ادا کیا جائے گا جبکہ حالت اسلام کی کمائی سے اس قرض کو ادا کرنا ممکن ہو جائے ۔ تو اس وقت ردت کی کمائی سے ادا کیا جائے گا۔ جیسے اگر ذمی مر گیا اور اس کا کوئی بھی وارث نہ ہو تو اس کا تمام مال عام مسلمانوں کے لئے ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس پر قرض ہو تو اس مال سے ادا کیا جائے گا۔ پس اس مقام میں بھی ایسا ہی ہوگا ۔ اور تیسری روایت کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس کی حالت اسلام کی کمائی اس کے وارثوں کا حق ہے۔ اور ردت کی کمائی خالص اسی کا حق ہے اس لئے روت کی کمائی سے قرض کی ادائیگی مقدم ہوگی ۔ لیکن اگر اس سے قرض پورا ادانہ ہو سکے بلکہ یہ کم ہو جائے تو ایسی صورت میں اس کی حالت اسلام کی کمائی سے ادا کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ قرض کی ادائیگی میراث سے مقدم ہوتی ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف ومحمد ( اور مالک و شافعی واحمد) رحمه اله علیم نے کہا ہے کہ دونوں میں میراث جاتی ہے۔ واللہ تعالیٰ اعلم ۔ تشریح مرتد کے واجب الادا قرضہ جات کے بارے میں امام ابو حنیفہ کی تین روایات ہیں۔ اول . امام زفر نے ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کی ہے کہ مرتد کے حالت اسلام کے قرضہ جات حالت اسلام کی کمائی سے ادا کریں گے اور حالت روت کے قرضہ جات حالت ردت کی کمائی سے ادا کئے جائیں گے وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہاں پر دو سبب ہیں جن کی وجہ سے مرتد پر قرضہ واجب ہے۔ دوم دوسری روایت حسن بن زیاد کی ہے کہ حالت اسلام میں کمایا ہوا مال مرتد کی ملکیت ہے اس لئے زمانہ اسلام کی کمائی سے مرتد کے قرضہ جات ادا کریں گے اس لئے کہ انسان پر جو قرضہ ہوتا ہے اس کے مال سے ادا کیا جاتا ہے نہ کہ وارث کو تر کہ سے حاصل ہونے والے مال سے۔ سوم امام ابو یوسف نے یہ روایت کی ہے کہ واجب الادا قرض کی ادائیگی کا آغاز حالت ارتداد کی کمائی سے کریں گے اور نا کافی ہونے کی صورت میں حالت اسلام میں کمائے ہوئے مال سے بقیہ قرض ادا کریں گے اس لئے کہ حالت اسلام کی کمائی ورثاء کا حق ہے اور حالت ردت کا کمایا ہوا مال خالص مرتد کا حق ہے لہذا اسی مال سے مرتد کا قرضہ ادا کیا جائے گا۔
And from the condition of this inheritance is freeing from the right of the testator, so debt is given priority over it. As for the earning of apostasy, it is not owned by him due to the nullification of the capacity for ownership by apostasy according to him, so his debt is not paid from it except if its payment from another source is impossible, then it is paid from it, like the one who dies and has no heir, his wealth goes to the Muslim community, and if there is a debt upon him, it is paid from it. Similarly here. The aspect of the third is that the earning of Islam is the right of the heirs, and the earning of apostasy is purely his right, so paying the debt from it is more appropriate, unless it is insufficient, then it is paid from the earning of Islam, giving priority to the right. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: his debts are paid from both because both are his property, so inheritance runs in both. And Allah knows best. Translation: The debts that were incurred by the apostate during Islam will be paid from his earnings during Islam, and the debts incurred during apostasy will be paid from his earnings during apostasy. This weak servant (the author) said that this is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa (Zafar narrated from him). The second narration is that first payment is made from the earnings of Islam, then if insufficient, from the earnings of apostasy (narrated by Hasan). The third narration is the opposite: first from earnings of apostasy, then from Islam (narrated by Abu Yusuf). The reason for the first narration is that the debts are due from two different causes. The second narration's reason is that the earnings of Islam are his property, so debt is given priority over inheritance. The third narration's reason is that the earnings of Islam are the right of the heirs, and the earnings of apostasy are purely his right.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary discusses the treatment of an apostate's debts accrued during his time as a Muslim and during his apostasy. It presents three different narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa on how to pay these debts, along with the opinion of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The first narration (from Imam Zafar) treats each set of debts separately: debts from Islam are paid from Islamic earnings, debts from apostasy from apostasy earnings, because each debt is tied to its specific earning cause. The second narration (from Hasan ibn Ziyad) prioritizes Islamic earnings, because that property is owned by the apostate and debt must be settled before inheritance. The third narration (from Abu Yusuf) prioritizes apostasy earnings, because Islamic earnings are considered the right of the heirs, while apostasy earnings are purely the apostate's own right. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad themselves hold that both types of earnings are owned by the apostate, so debts are paid from both collectively, and inheritance applies to both. The commentary elaborates on the reasoning behind each narration, using analogies such as a dhimmi dying without heirs.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A person who leaves Islam and apostatizes.
كسب (kasb): Earnings acquired by the apostate during a specific period (Islam or apostasy).
سبب (sabab): Cause or legal reason – each debt is tied to the reason it was incurred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second narration from Imam Abu Hanifa (narrated by Hasan ibn Ziyad), from which earnings should the debts be paid first?
A) Apostasy earnings
B) Islamic earnings
C) Both earnings equally proportionally
D) Earnings from whichever period has more money

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers multiple valid narrations on the apostate's debt payment, each based on a different rationale about ownership and inheritance.

Transactions of an Apostate: Suspended or Valid?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on apostate transactions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an apostate's transactions during apostasy and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Core Idea
An apostate's transactions are suspended — neither immediately valid nor void — pending his fate.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the legal status of an apostate's financial transactions during the period of apostasy. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such acts are suspended (mawquf), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani consider them valid. Understanding the reasoning behind each view sharpens your ability to analyze how legal capacity and presumption shape rulings in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling of Abu Hanifa
Read the opening sentence: the apostate's sales, purchases, gifts, etc. are mawquf (suspended). Validity depends on future event: return to Islam (valid) or death/joining enemy (void).
This is the core position of the Hanafi school's founder.
2
Understand the three categories of apostate acts
The passage divides acts into: (1) effective by consensus (e.g., divorce), (2) void by consensus (e.g., marriage), (3) suspended by consensus (mufawada), (4) disputed (the subject of the ikhtilaf).
This taxonomy helps isolate where the ikhtilaf actually lies.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning: harbi analogy
He analogizes the apostate to a harbi (enemy combatant) taken under Muslim control without aman. Such a person's status is uncertain, so transactions are suspended. The lack of civil immunity (isma) is key.
The apostate faces execution, so his property rights are not secure.
4
Contrast the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Both consider transactions valid, but differ in presumption: Abu Yusuf expects return to Islam (like a healthy person), Muhammad expects persistence in apostasy (like a sick person whose transactions are from two-thirds). Both agree the act is valid, not suspended.
Their ikhtilaf is on the underlying presumption, not the outcome.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a practical scenario
If an apostate sells an item and then dies (killed), per Abu Hanifa the sale is void; per the two companions it is valid and the buyer keeps it.
This directly impacts inheritance and contractual rights.

مرتد کی حالت ردت میں خرید وفروخت اور لین دین کا حکم
قَالَ وَمَابَاعَهُ أَوِ اشْتَرَاهُ أَوْ اعْتَقَهُ أَوْ وَهَبَهُ أَوْرَهَنَهُ أوْ تَصَرَّفَ فِيهِ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِ فِى حَالٍ رِدَّتِهِ فَهُوَ مَوْقُوفُ فَإِنْ أَسْلَمَ صَحَتْ عُقُودُهُ وَإِنْ مَاتَ أَوْ قُتِلَ أوْ لَحِقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ بَطَلَتْ وَهَذَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَة وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ وَ مُحَمَّد يَجُوزُ مَا صَنَعَ فِى الْوَجْهَيْنِ إِعْلَمُ أَنَّ تَصَرُّفَاتِ الْمُرْتَةِ عَلَى أَقْسَامِ نَافِذُ بِالْاَنْفَاقِ كَالْاسْتِيلاد و الطَّلَاقِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَفْتَقِرُ إلى حَقِيقَةِ الْمِلْكِ وَ تَمَامَ الْوِلَايَةِ وَبَاطِلُّ بِالاتِّفَاقِ كَالنَّكَاحِ وَالنَّبِيحَةِ لأَنه يَعتمد للة وَلَا مِلَّةَ لَهُ وَمَوْقُوفٌ نَ اللَّةَ وَلَامِلَّةَ بِالْإِتِفَاقِ كَالْمُفَاوَضَةِ لِأَنَّهَا تَعْتَمِدُ المَسَاوَاةَ وَلَا مَسَاوَاةَ بَين الْمُسْلِمِ وَالْمُرْتَدِ مَالَمْ يُسْلِمُ وَمُخْتَلَفُ فِى تَوَقِفِه وَهُوَ مَا عَدَدْنَاهُ لَهُمَا أَنَّ القِحَةَ تَعْتَمِدُ الأهْلِيَّةَ وَالنّفَاذُ يَعْتَمِدُ الْمِلْكَ وَلَا خِفَاء فِي وُجُودِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ لِكَوْنِهِ مُخَاطَبًا وَكَذَا الْمِلْكُ لِقِيَامِهِ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ عَلَى مَاقَرَرْ نَاهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ وَلِهَذَا الوَوَلَدَ لَهُ وَلَدُ بَعْدَ الرّدَّةِ لِسِيَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ مِن امرأةٍ مُسْلِمَةٍ يَرِثُهُ وَلَوْ مَاتَ وَلَدُهُ بَعْدَ الرِّدَّةِ قَبْلَ الْمَوْتِ لَا يَرِتُهُ فَيَصِحُ تَصَرُّفَاتُهُ قَبْلَ الْمَوْتِ إِلَّا أَنْ عِنْداً بِى يُوسُف تَصِحُ كَمَا تَصَحُ مِنَ الصَّحِيحِ لِأَنَّ الظَّاهِرَ عَودُهُ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ إِذِ الشَّهَةُ تَرَاحُ فَلَا يُقَتَل وَصَارَ كَالْمُرْتَدَّةِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ تَصِحُ كَمَاتَصِحُ مِنَ الْمَرِيضِ لِأَنَّ مَنِ انْتَحَلَ إلى نَحْلَةٍ لَا سِيَّمَا مُعْرِضًا عَمَّا نَشَأَ عَلَيْهِ قَلَّمَا يَتْرُكُ فَيُفْضِى إِلَى الْقَتْلِ ظَاهِرُ الخِلَافِ الْمُرْتَدَّةِ لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَقْتَلَ وَلا بِي حَنِيفَةِ أَنَّهُ حَرْبِيُّ مَقْهُورٌ تَحْتَ أَيْدِينَا عَلَى مَا فَرَّرْنَاهُ فِي تَوَفَّفِ التَّصَرَّفَاتِ بِنَاءً عَلَيْهِ وَصَارَ كَالْحَرِي يَدْخُلُ دَارَنَا بِغَيْرِ أَمَانٍ فَيُؤْخَذُ وَيَظْهَرُ وَيَتَوَفَّفُ تَصَرَفَاتُهُ لَتَوقَفِ حَالِهِ وَكَذَا الْمُرْتَدُّ وَاسْتِحْفَاقَهُ الْقَتلَ لِبُطَلَانِ سَبَبِ الْعِصْمَةِ فِى الْفَصْلَيْنِ فَأَوْجَبَ خَلَا فِى الْأَهْلِيَّةِ بِخِلَافِ الزَّانِى وَقَاتِلِ الْعَمَدِ لِأَنَّ الْإِسْتِحْفَاقَ فِي ذَالِكَ جَزَاء عَلَى الْجِنَايَةِ وَبِخِلَافِ الْمَرْأَةِ لأَنَّهَا
The ruling on buying, selling, and transactions of the apostate during apostasy: He said: Whatever he sold, bought, freed a slave, gave as gift, pawned, or transacted with his property during his apostasy, it is suspended. If he becomes Muslim, his contracts become valid; if he dies, is killed, or joins the abode of war, they become void. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: What he did is valid in both cases. Know that the apostate's transactions are of types: (1) Effective by consensus, like istilad (seeking to have a child from a slave woman) and divorce, because they do not require actual ownership or full authority; (2) Void by consensus, like marriage and sacrifice, because they depend on a religion and he has no religion; (3) Suspended by consensus, like mutual partnership (mufawada), because it requires equality and there is no equality between Muslim and apostate; (4) Disputed as to suspension, which is what we have mentioned. According to Abu Hanifa, he is a belligerent under our control, so his transactions are suspended like the case of a hostile who enters our land without aman. According to Abu Yusuf, they are valid like those of a healthy person because he is expected to return to Islam; according to Muhammad, they are valid like those of a sick person because he is unlikely to repent.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling on an apostate's financial transactions during his apostasy. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, all such transactions are suspended (mawquf): if he returns to Islam, they become valid; if he dies or is executed or leaves for enemy territory, they are void. The two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, hold that these transactions are valid in both outcomes. The passage then categorizes the apostate's actions: some are immediately effective (like freeing a slave for a child or divorcing) because they don't require full ownership; some are void (like marriage and animal sacrifice) because they require a valid religion; some are suspended by consensus (like mufawada partnership) because it requires equality between Muslim and apostate; and the remaining transactions are the subject of the dispute. The reasoning for Abu Hanifa's view is that the apostate is like a hostile (harbi) captured in our land—his status is uncertain, so his transactions are suspended. Abu Yusuf considers him likely to return to Islam, so his transactions are like those of a healthy person. Muhammad considers him unlikely to repent, so his transactions are like those of a sick person (i.e., valid but from two-thirds of property if he dies in apostasy? Actually the text says 'like a sick person' in terms of validity, but the implication is that they are valid subject to the death condition. The text then discusses inheritance implications: a child born to the apostate after apostasy inherits from him, but if the child dies before the apostate, the apostate does not inherit from the child, illustrating the suspension of property rights.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): A legal act that is not immediately effective; its validity depends on a future event (return to Islam or death of the apostate).
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with the Muslims, not under Islamic rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what happens to an apostate's sale of property if he is later killed for apostasy?
A) The sale becomes valid after his death.
B) The sale becomes void.
C) The sale remains valid but the property goes to the state.
D) The sale is upheld only if the buyer was a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
An apostate's transactions are suspended pending his fate, a ruling debated within the Hanafi school based on different presumptions about his future.

intermediate
8 min
Rulings on an Apostate's Transactions During Ridda
Intra-Hanafi dispute on apostate's transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the validity of an apostate's transactions and distinguish the rulings of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
An apostate's transactions are either suspended, valid, or void depending on which Hanafi imam you follow.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens to the contracts of a person who apostatizes? Does he lose legal capacity for transactions, or can he still buy, sell, and dispose of property? The ruling of Abu Hanifa and his two students, the Sahibayn, differ crucially, and the practical consequences affect both the apostate's estate and the counterparties to his contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the positions
Identify the two main positions: Abu Hanifa holds that all transactions during apostasy are suspended (mawquf) — valid only if he returns to Islam. The Sahibayn hold they are immediately valid.
2
Categorize the dispositions
The text divides an apostate's acts into four categories: effective by consensus, void by consensus, suspended by consensus, and those whose suspension is disputed. Note which category the transactions in the main ruling fall into.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Examine how Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that the apostate retains legal capacity (ahliyyah) and ownership (milk), supported by the inheritance of a child born within six months.
Note further sub-difference: Abu Yusuf says transactions valid like a healthy person; Muhammad says like a sick person (restricted to one-third).
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Understand Abu Hanifa's analogy to a harbi captured without aman: the uncertainty of his fate suspends his transactions. The loss of inviolability (isma) creates a defect in capacity.
Distinguish from adulterer/murderer where expectation of death is a punishment.
5
Identify the practical difference
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, if the apostate dies as an apostate, his transactions are void; under the Sahibayn, they are valid and binding on his estate.

مرتد کی حالت ردت میں خرید وفروخت اور لین دین کا حکم
قَالَ وَمَابَاعَهُ أَوِ اشْتَرَاهُ أَوْ اعْتَقَهُ أَوْ وَهَبَهُ أَوْرَهَنَهُ أوْ تَصَرَّفَ فِيهِ مِنْ أَمْوَالِهِ فِى حَالٍ رِدَّتِهِ فَهُوَ مَوْقُوفُ فَإِنْ أَسْلَمَ صَحَتْ عُقُودُهُ وَإِنْ مَاتَ أَقْسَامِ نَافِذُ بِالْاَنْفَاقِ كَالْاسْتِيلاد و الطَّلَاقِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَفْتَقِرُ إلى حَقِيقَةِ الْمِلْكِ وَ تَمَامَ الْوِلَايَةِ وَبَاطِلُّ بِالاتِّفَاقِ كَالنَكَاحِ وَالنَّبِيحَةِ لأَنه يَعتمد للة وَلَا مِلَّةَ لَهُ وَمَوْقُوفٌ نَ اللَّةَ وَلَامِلَّةَ بِالْإِتِفَاقِ كَالْمُفَاوَضَةِ لِأَنَّهَا تَعْتَمِدُ المَسَاوَاةَ وَلَا مَسَاوَاةَ بَين الْمُسْلِمِ وَالْمُرْتَدِ مَالَمْ يُسْلِمُ الشَّهَةُ تَرَاحُ فَلَا يُقَتَل وَصَارَ كَالْمُرْتَدَّةِ وَعِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ تَصِحُ كَمَاتَصِحُ مِنَ الْمَرِيضِ لِأَنَّ مَنِ انْتَحَلَ إلى نَحْلَةٍ لَا سِيَّمَا مُعْرِضًا عَمَّا نَشَأَ عَلَيْهِ قَلَّمَا يَتْرُكُ فَيُفْضِى إِلَى الْقَتْلِ ظَاهِرُ الخِلَافِ الْمُرْتَدَّةِ لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَقْتَلَ وَلا بِي حَنِيفَةِ أَنَّهُ حَرْبِيُّ مَقْهُورٌ تَحْتَ أَيْدِينَا عَلَى مَا فَرَّرْنَاهُ فِي تَوَفَّفِ التَّصَرفَاتِ بِنَاءً عَلَيْهِ وَصَارَ كَالْحَرِي يَدْخُلُ دَارَنَا بِغَيْرِ أَمَانٍ فَيُؤْخَذُ وَيَظْهَرُ وَيَتَوَفَّفُ تَصَرَفَاتُهُ لَتَوقَفِ حَالِهِ وَكَذَا الْمُرْتَدُّ وَاسْتِحْفَاقَهُ الْقَتلَ لِبُطَلَانِ سَبَبِ الْعِصْمَةِ فِى الْفَصْلَيْنِ فَأَوْجَبَ خَلَا فِى الْأَهْلِيَّةِ بِخِلَافِ الزَّانِى وَقَاتِلِ الْعَمَدِ لِأَنَّ الْإِسْتِحْفَاقَ فِي ذَالِكَ جَزَاء عَلَى الْجِنَايَةِ وَبِخِلَافِ الْمَرْأَةِ لأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ حَرْبِيَّةً وَلِهَذَا لَا تُقْتَل
ترجمہ اور قدوری رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ مرتد نے اپنی ردت کی حالت میں جو مال فروخت کیا یا خرید ایا آزاد کیا یا ہبہ کیا یار بہن کیا یا اپنے مال میں کچھ اور تصرف کیا تو اس کا یہ تمام تصرف موقوف رہے گا۔ یعنی اگر وہ دوبارہ اسلام قبول کرلے تو اس کا ہر تصرف صحیح مان لیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر وہ اسی حالت میں مرجائے یا قتل کر دیا جائے یا دار الحرب میں داخل ہو جائے تو اس کا یہ پچھلا تمام تصرف باطل ہو جائے گا۔ یہ قول امام ابو حنیفہ رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف ومحمد رحمہما اللہ نے کہا ہے کہ دونوں صورتوں میں اس نے جو کچھ تصرف کیا وہ سب جائز ہوگا۔
إِعْلَمُ أَنَّ تَصَرُّفَاتَ الْمُرْتَةِ الخ ۔ واضح ہو کہ مرتد کے تصرفات کئی قسم کے ہوتے ہیں۔
اول .. وہ جو بالا تفاق نافذ ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے ام ولد بنانا اور طلاق دینا ( یعنی عدت کی حالت میں اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دی یا دونوں ایک ساتھ مرتد ہو گئے پھر طلاق دی تو صحیح مانتے ہوئے نافذ ہوگا ) کیونکہ ایسے تصرف میں حقیقی ملک اور پوری ولایت کی ضرورت نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اسی بناء پر اپنے لڑکے کی باندی سے استیلا د (ام ولد بنانا ) صحیح ہے۔ اور غلام کی طلاق بھی صحیح ہوتی ہے۔ اور حق شفعہ دے دینا اور ہبہ قبول کرنا بھی اس قسم سے ہے۔ رو وہ تصرف جو بالا تفاق باطل ہے جیسے نکاح اور ذبیہ (اور وارث ہونا ) کیونکہ اپنے تصرف کے لئے ملت ( اسلام ) پر اعتماد ضروری ہے۔ جبکہ مرتد کے واسطے کوئی ملت نہیں ہے۔ سوم وہ تصرف جو بالاتفاق موقوف ہے جیسے ( کاروبار کرتے ہوئے ) شرکت مفاوضہ کیونکہ اس میں جانبین کے درمیان مساوات کی شرط ہوتی ہے جبکہ ایک مسلمان اور ایک کافر کے درمیان جب تک کہ مرتد مسلمان نہ ہو جائے دونوں میں مساوات نہیں مانی جاتی ہے۔
چهارم وہ تصرف جس کے موقوف ہونے میں اختلاف ہے۔ اور یہ وہی تصرفات ہیں جن کو ہم اوپر بیان کر چکے ہیں (یعنی خرید و فروخت معتق در من، اسی طرح مکاتب بنانا اور قرض وصول کرنا ، اجارہ اور ولایت)۔ اس میں صاحبین رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایسا تصرف اس صورت میں صحیح ہوتا ہے جبکہ تصرف کرنے والے میں اس کی اہلیت پائی جائے اور اس کا مالک ہونے سے وہ نافذ ہو جاتا ہے اور اس بات میں کوئی شبہ نہیں ہے کہ اس شخص میں دبے تصرف کی اہلیت موجود ہے کیونکہ وہ احکام الہی کا مخاطب ہے۔اسی طرح اس میں ملکیت بھی موجود ہے۔ جیسا کہ ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ وہ مرتد کے مرجانے تک باقی ہے ۔ اسی وجہ سے اگر اس کے مرتد ہو جانے کے بعد اس کی مسلمان بیوی سے چھ مہینے کے اندر کوئی بچہ پیدا ہوا تو وہ بھی اس کا وارث ہوگا۔ (اس لئے اگر اس کی ملکیت ختم ہوگئی تو وہ وارث نہ ہوتا ) اور اگر اس کے مرتد ہونے کے بعد اور مرنے سے پہلے یہ بچہ مر گیا تو وارث نہ ہوگا۔ (اور اگر ملکیت خستم ہوگئی ہوتی تو وارث ہوتا ۔ ) تو اس سے یہ بات ثابت ہوئی کہ اس کے مرنے سے پہلے اس کے تصرفات صحیح ہیں۔ لیکن صاحبین کے درمیان آپس میں صرف یہ اختلاف ہے کہ ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے نزدیک یہ تصرفات اسی طرح صحیح ہوں گے جیسے تندرست آدمی کے تصرفات صحیح ہوتے ہیں ۔ یعنی اس کے کل مال سے صحیح ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ وہ اسلام کی طرف لوٹ آئے گا۔ اس لئے کہ
Ruling on buying, selling, and transactions of the apostate in the state of apostasy. He (al-Quduri) said: Whatever he sold, bought, freed, gifted, pawned, or made any disposition of his wealth during his apostasy is suspended. If he becomes Muslim, his contracts become valid; if he dies, is killed, or joins the abode of war, they become void. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Whatever he did in both cases is permitted. Know that the dispositions of the apostate are of categories: Those that are effective by consensus, such as making a slave a mother of a child (istilad) and divorce, because they do not require actual ownership and full authority; Those that are void by consensus, such as marriage and slaughtering, because they depend on a religion and he has no religion; Those that are suspended by consensus, such as partnership (mufawada), because it depends on equality, and there is no equality between a Muslim and an apostate unless he becomes Muslim; And those whose suspension is disputed, which we have enumerated. Their (the Sahibayn) argument is that validity depends on legal capacity, and enforcement depends on ownership. There is no doubt that he has legal capacity because he is addressed by divine commands, and likewise ownership exists as it remains until his death, as we established earlier. For this reason, if a child is born to him from a Muslim woman within six months after his apostasy, the child inherits from him; and if his child dies after apostasy but before his death, he does not inherit from the child. Thus his dispositions before death are valid. However, there is a difference between the Sahibayn: According to Abu Yusuf, they are valid like the dispositions of a healthy person, because the apparent expectation is that he will return to Islam, as he is not killed (like a female apostate). According to Muhammad, they are valid like the dispositions of a sick person, because one who adopts a false creed, especially turning away from his upbringing, rarely abandons it, leading to killing – unlike the female apostate who is not killed. According to Abu Hanifa, he is like a harbi (enemy combatant) subdued under our authority, as we established, so his dispositions are suspended based on the uncertainty of his state. He is like a harbi who enters our land without aman, is captured, and his dispositions are suspended due to the uncertainty of his situation. Similarly, the apostate’s expectation of death due to loss of inviolability necessitates a defect in legal capacity, unlike the adulterer and intentional killer, where the expectation of death is a punishment for crime, and unlike a woman, as she is not a harbi and thus not killed. Translation: Al-Quduri said that whatever the apostate sold, bought, freed, gifted, pawned, or otherwise disposed of during his apostasy, all such dispositions are suspended. That is, if he embraces Islam again, all his dispositions are considered valid; if he dies in that state, is killed, or enters dar al-harb, all his previous dispositions become void. This is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said that in both cases, whatever he did is permissible. Know that the dispositions of the apostate are of several types. First: Those that are effective by consensus, such as making a female slave umm walad and giving divorce (i.e., during the waiting period, or if both apostatized together and then divorce, it is effective), because such dispositions do not require actual ownership and full authority. Similarly, making his son's female slave umm walad (istilad) is valid, and a slave's divorce is valid. Giving up the right of pre-emption and accepting a gift are also of this type. Second: Those that are void by consensus, such as marriage and slaughtering (and inheritance), because they depend on religion, and the apostate has no religion. Third: Those that are suspended by consensus, such as partnership (mufawada) in business, because it requires equality between the two parties, and there is no equality between a Muslim and an apostate until the apostate becomes Muslim. Fourth: Those whose suspension is disputed, and these are the ones we mentioned earlier (i.e., buying, selling, manumission, kitaba, collecting debts, leasing, and guardianship). The proof of the Sahibayn is that such a disposition is valid when the person has legal capacity and ownership, and there is no doubt that he has legal capacity for disposition because he is addressed by divine commands. Similarly, he has ownership, as we previously established that it remains until his death. For this reason, if after his apostasy a child is born to him from his Muslim wife within six months, that child inherits from him (because if his ownership had ceased, he would not inherit); and if that child dies after apostasy but before his death, he does not inherit (and if ownership had ceased, he would inherit). Thus it is established that his dispositions before death are valid. However, there is a difference between the Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf holds that these dispositions are valid like the dispositions of a healthy person, i.e., from all his wealth, because the apparent is that he will return to Islam, since he is not immediately killed, like a female apostate. Muhammad holds that they are valid like the dispositions of a sick person, because one who adopts a false creed, especially turning away from what he was raised upon, rarely abandons it, so it leads to killing – unlike the female apostate. And Abu Hanifa: He is a subdued harbi under our authority, as we established, so his dispositions are suspended accordingly. He is like a harbi who enters our land without aman, is captured and appears, and his dispositions are suspended due to the uncertainty of his situation. Similarly, the apostate's expectation of death due to the invalidation of inviolability in both cases creates a defect in legal capacity, unlike the adulterer and premeditated murderer, because the expectation of death there is a punishment for the crime, and unlike a woman, because she is not a harbi and therefore not killed.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of an apostate's transactions during his apostasy. Abu Hanifa holds that all such dispositions (selling, buying, manumission, gifting, pawning) are suspended: they become valid if he returns to Islam, but void if he dies, is killed, or flees to dar al-harb. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) consider them immediately valid in both scenarios. The text then categorizes an apostate's dispositions into four types: (1) effective by consensus (e.g., making a female slave umm walad, divorce) – these do not require full ownership; (2) void by consensus (e.g., marriage, slaughtering) – they require a religion; (3) suspended by consensus (e.g., mufawada partnership) – due to lack of equality; (4) disputed suspension (the ones in the matn). The Sahibayn argue that the apostate has legal capacity (khitab) and ownership (until death), so his transactions are valid. They cite that a child born within six months inherits from him, proving ownership. Abu Yusuf sees him as likely to return to Islam, like a female apostate (not killed). Muhammad sees him as unlikely to return, so his transactions are like those of a sick person (valid but restricted to one-third of wealth). Abu Hanifa analogizes him to a harbi captured without aman, whose state is uncertain, so transactions are suspended. The text distinguishes this from an adulterer or murderer, who face execution as punishment, not due to loss of inviolability.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): A legal disposition that is suspended, conditional upon a future event (return to Islam or death/fleeing).
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Refers to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main students of Abu Hanifa.
اہلیت (ahliyyah): Legal capacity to perform valid transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the status of an apostate's sale if he returns to Islam?
A) It becomes valid.
B) It remains suspended.
C) It becomes void.
D) It is valid only if approved by the judge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school is divided on an apostate's transactions: Abu Hanifa suspends them pending return, while the Sahibayn validate them immediately, each based on different analogies and views of legal capacity.

intermediate
8 min
Diyah of a Murtadd: Which Property Pays for Accidental Killing?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on property source for murtadd's diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions regarding the property used to pay diyah for a murtadd's accidental killing and apply the principle of nufudh al-tasarruf.

Core Idea
A murtadd's property is divided: Abu Hanifa excludes apostasy earnings; the Sahibayn include all.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the diyah (blood money) for a murtadd (apostate) who accidentally kills someone. The issue is not whether diyah is owed, but from which portion of the murtadd's property it must be paid. The disagreement hinges on the legal effectiveness (nufudh al-tasarruf) of a murtadd's transactions during apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and disputed element
The act is the payment of diyah for accidental killing committed by a murtadd. The disputed element is the source of property from which the diyah is taken.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that diyah must be taken only from property earned during Islam. Property earned during apostasy is not considered effectively owned because his transactions are suspended (mawquf).
Key term: mawquf – suspended, not immediately effective.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that diyah can be taken from all earnings, both during Islam and apostasy. They argue transactions are effective (nafidh) in both states, so all property is his.
Key term: nufudh – effectiveness of transactions.
4
Identify the underlying principle
The dispute centers on whether a murtadd's transactions during apostasy are effective. Abu Hanifa says they are suspended, so the property is not truly his. The Sahibayn say they are effective, so all earnings are his property.
This principle also affects inheritance and disposal of property.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, if the murtadd's Islamic earnings are insufficient, diyah may remain unpaid. Under the Sahibayn, all his earnings are available, ensuring full payment. Also affects inheritance distribution.
Mufta bihi likely the Sahibayn's view for practicality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ختم النُّصْرَةِ فَيَكُونُ فِى مَا لِه وَعِندَهُمَا الْكَسْبَان جَمِيعًا مَالُهُ لِنُفُوذِ تَصَرُّفَاتِهِ فِي الْحَالَيْنِ وَلِهَذَا يَجُرِى الْإِرْتُ فِيْهِمَا عِندَهُمَا وَعِندَهُ مَالُهُ الْمُكْتَسَبُ فِي الْإِسْلَامِ لِيفًا ذِتَصَرُّفِهِ فِيهِ دُونَ الْمَكْسُوبِ فِي الرَدَّةِ لِتَوَقُفِ تَصَرُّفِهِ وَلِهَذَا كَانَ الاَوَّلُ مِيرَ انَّا عَنْهُ وَالثَّانِي فَيْنًا عِندَهُ
...so it is in his property, and according to them (Sahibayn) the two earnings together are his property because his transactions are effective in both states, and therefore inheritance runs in both according to them. And according to him (Abu Hanifa), his property is what he earned in Islam because his transaction is effective in it, not what he earned in apostasy because his transaction is suspended. And therefore the first is his inheritance and the second is something else according to him.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whose property a murtadd's diyah is taken from when he commits accidental killing. Abu Hanifa holds that only property earned during Islam is considered his, as his transactions during apostasy are suspended and thus not his effective property. Therefore, diyah is taken only from Islamic earnings. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that all earnings, both during Islam and apostasy, are his property because his transactions are effective in both states. Consequently, inheritance runs through both according to them, while Abu Hanifa sees apostasy earnings as not being inherited (possibly becoming fay' or ghanimah).

Key Terms
كسبان (kasbaan): Earnings (plural) – property acquired during both Islam and apostasy.
نفوذ التصرف (nufudh al-tasarruf): Effectiveness of a transaction; a valid act that produces legal consequences.
إرث (irth): Inheritance – the transfer of property from deceased to heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, from which property is the diyah of a murtadd who committed accidental killing taken?
A) From all his earnings, both during Islam and apostasy.
B) Only from property he earned during Islam.
C) Only from property he earned during apostasy.
D) From the property of his 'aqilah (tribal guarantors).

Key Takeaway
The division of a murtadd's property hinges on the effectiveness of his transactions during apostasy, leading to two valid Hanafi positions on diyah and inheritance.
